Accepting Testimonies from Muslims in Dar al-Harb
Fatwa on accepting rulings/testimonies from dar al-harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle regarding the acceptance of testimony from Muslims residing in dar al-harb and identify the conditions under which their legal probity (ʿadāla) is impugned.

Core Idea
Residence in non-Muslim lands does not automatically disqualify a Muslim's testimony; the default is acceptance unless clear proof of deliberate sin exists.

This lesson examines a fatwa by Imam al-Mazari that clarifies the Hanafi position on the validity of judicial rulings and testimonies of Muslims living under non-Muslim rule. The fatwa addresses two key objections: that such residence might impair legal probity, and that a judge appointed by non-Muslims lacks proper authority. Through this analysis, you will learn how the Hanafi school balances the presumption of justice in Muslims with the need to prevent abuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Determine the issue: can the judgments and testimonies of Muslims residing in dar al-harb be accepted? Recognize the two objections from the passage: (1) living in dar al-harb may impair ʿadāla, and (2) a judge appointed by non-Muslims lacks authority.
The fatwa is a response to a specific query from Sicily.
2
Examine the first objection (impairment of ʿadāla)
Analyze the condition that residence in dar al-harb could disqualify a Muslim's testimony. Note that the fatwa rejects this as a general rule—the default is good opinion of Muslims (ḥusn al-ẓann) unless there is clear evidence of deliberate sin.
The text says: 'The first is not to be relied upon... because it is based on good opinion of Muslims.'
3
Examine the second objection (lack of authority)
Consider the objection that a judge appointed by non-Muslims lacks valid authority. The fatwa implies this does not automatically nullify the ruling, as the Hanafi school separates the enforcement power from the act of judging itself.
This aspect is grounded in the earlier discussion of the judge's authority not depending on enforcement.
4
Determine the ruling based on the nature of residence
Distinguish between residence by compulsion (ḍarūra) or valid intention (e.g., hope of Islam, freeing captives) and residence by choice without valid excuse. The former preserves ʿadāla; the latter may impugn it.
The fatwa states: 'If it is by compulsion, then there is no doubt that it does not impugn his justice... but if he stayed due to the rule of ignorance... then this impugns his justice.'
5
Apply the default principle of excuse (al-ʿudhr)
In cases of doubt about the nature of residence, the default is to accept the testimony. The burden of proof lies on those who wish to reject it, requiring clear qarāʾin indicating voluntary wrongful stay.
This reflects the maxim 'al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bish-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى الشيخ محمد عليش: سئل الإمام أبو عبد الله المازري رحمه الله تعالى عن أحكام [قاضي] في زمانه من صقلية من عند قاضيها أو شهود عدول هل يقبل ذلك منهم أم لا مع أنها ضرورة ولا تدرى أقامتهم هناك تحت أهل الكفر هل هي اضطرار أم اختيار؟ فأجاب: لا قادح في هذا وجهان: الأول يشمل القاضي وبينانة ناحية اختلال العدالة إذ لا يباح المقام في دار الحرب في قياد أهل الكفر. والثاني من ناحية الولاية إذا القاضي مولى من قبل أهل الكفر. والاول وقع لا يعتمد عليها في هذه المسألة وشبهها وهي تحسين الظن بالمسلمين ومباعدة العاصي عنهم فلا يعدل عنها لاحتمالات كانية وتوهمات واهية كتجويز من ظاهرة العدالة وقد يجوز في الأحقاد ونفس الأمر أن يكون ارتكب كبيرة الأمن قام الدليل على عصمته وهذا التجويز مطروح والحكم بالظاهر الأهو الأرحام إلا أن يظهر من الحال ما يوجب الخروج عن العدالة فيجب التوقف حينئذ حتى يظهر باقي وجه زوال موجب راجحة العدالة ويبقى الحكم لغلبة الظن بعد ذلك إلى أن قال: وهذا المقيم بدار الحرب إن كان اضطرارا فلا إشكال أنه لا يقدح في عدالته وإن كان تأويله صحيحا مثل إقامته ببلد الحرب لرجاء إسلام أهل الحرب ونقلهم عن مثلا توهم كما أشار إليه الباقلاني وكما أشار إليه أصحاب مالك في تجويز الدخول لفكاك الأسير وأما لو أقام بحكم الجاهلية والإعراض عن التأويل اختيارا فهذا قدح في عدالته واختلف أهل المذهب في رد شهادة الداخل اختيار التجارة ضمن ظهرت عبادة منهم وشك في إقامته على أي وجه فالأصل العذر لأن محل الاحتمالات السابقة شهد لعذر فلا يرد لاحتمال واحد إلا أن توجد قرائن تشهد أن إقامته كانت اختيارا على وجه...
And in the fatawa of Sheikh Muhammad 'Ulaysh: Imam Abu Abdullah al-Mazari was asked about the rulings of [a judge] in his time from Sicily, from his judge or upright witnesses, is that accepted from them or not, given that it is a necessity, and we do not know whether their stay there under the people of disbelief is out of compulsion or choice? He answered: No objection in this, two aspects: The first includes the judge and [his] situation regarding the impairment of justice, since staying in the land of war is not permissible under the leadership of the disbelievers. The second is from the aspect of authority, since the judge is appointed by the disbelievers. The first is not to be relied upon in this matter and the like, because it is based on good opinion of Muslims and distancing the disobedient from them. So it should not be turned away from due to possible scenarios and flimsy assumptions, like deeming apparent justice permissible, and it may be that in hatred and in reality he committed a major sin, but there is no proof of his sinlessness. This assumption is discarded, and judgment is based on the apparent, unless there appears from the situation what necessitates departure from justice; then one must pause until the remaining aspect for removal of the outweighing cause of justice appears, and judgment remains based on preponderance of opinion after that, until he said: And this resident in the land of war, if it is by compulsion, then there is no doubt that it does not impugn his justice, even if his interpretation is correct, like his staying in the land of war with hope of the conversion of the people of war and their transfer from, for example, supposition, as al-Baqillani indicated and as indicated by the followers of Malik regarding permitting entry for the release of captives. But if he stayed due to the rule of ignorance and turning away from proper interpretation by choice, then this impugns his justice. And the people of the madhhab differed regarding rejecting the testimony of one who enters by choice for trade, if it appears that he worshiped among them and there is doubt about which basis his stay is on. The default is excuse, because the place of previous possibilities testifies for excuse, so it is not rejected due to one possibility, unless there exist evidences that testify that his stay was by choice in a certain manner...
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) for accepting the judicial rulings and testimonies of Muslims living in non-Muslim lands. The fatwa of Imam al-Mazari addresses two objections: first, that living in non-Muslim lands might impugn one's justice; second, that a judge appointed by non-Muslims lacks proper authority. The response refutes the first objection by emphasizing that Muslims should be presumed just unless evidence of wrongdoing appears, and staying in a non-Muslim land may be excused by necessity or valid intention (e.g., to free captives or hope for conversion). The second objection is handled by the earlier discussion that a judge's authority does not depend on enforcement power. The text then discusses the conditions under which one's testimony is accepted: if the stay is by compulsion or with a valid excuse, it does not affect justice; if it is by choice without excuse, it may. The default is to accept testimony unless clear evidence shows the stay was voluntary and without religious justification. This reflects the Hanafi principle of guarding the honor of Muslims and the maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bish-shakk'.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Muslims may live under certain conditions
العدالة (al-ʿadāla): Legal probity; the quality of being upright and credible
تحسين الظن (taḥsīn al-ẓann): Holding a good opinion; the principle of presuming good
الأصل العذر (al-aṣl al-ʿudhr): The default is excuse; the legal principle that in case of doubt, the Muslim is given the benefit of the doubt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa, what is the default ruling regarding the testimony of a Muslim living in dar al-harb?
A) It is rejected unless he can prove his stay was by compulsion
B) It is accepted unless there is evidence that his stay was by choice without valid excuse
C) It is always rejected because residence in dar al-harb is haram
D) It is accepted only if he was appointed by a Muslim ruler

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school presumes the justice of Muslims; residence in dar al-harb does not automatically disqualify testimony.

Tafwid al-Talaq: Delegating Divorce to the Wife as a Legal Stratagem
Question and answer on the validity and conditions of delegating divorce to the wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi legal stratagem of tafwid al-talaq, identify its conditions, and apply it to a case where the husband fails in his duties.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a husband can delegate the authority to divorce to his wife at marriage, providing a lawful remedy for oppressive situations.

This passage from Al-Hamiyya al-Najiza addresses a pressing problem: what recourse does a wife have when her husband oppresses her, fails to provide maintenance, or abandons her, and there is no Shari'a judge to intervene? The answer is a carefully crafted legal stratagem (hila) called tafwid al-talaq, whereby the husband delegates the power of divorce to the wife in the marriage contract. The author emphasizes that this is permissible in Hanafi fiqh, but the wife must not use this authority hastily; she must follow proper procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and the proposed hila
Recognize the social problem: oppressive husbands, lack of maintenance, absence of Shari'a judge. The hila is writing conditions in the marriage deed giving the wife authority to divorce herself.
This is a legal stratagem (hila) to provide relief.
2
Understand the ruling and terminology
The act is jā'iz (permissible) and is called tafwid al-talaq in Hanafi terminology. The delegation can be before, during, or after marriage.
The ruling is based on the need to prevent hardship.
3
Recognize the conditions for validity
The specific wording provided in the text must be used exactly; altering it may render the delegation useless. Additionally, the wife must not act hastily even after receiving authority.
The wording is carefully crafted to balance interests.
4
Apply the adab (etiquette) of use
The wife must only use the authority after thoughtful consideration, consultation with well-wishers, and performing istikhara. Haste is disliked in Shari'a.
This prevents misuse of the delegation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلاصه : المجلة الناجزه :: للحملة الاجزه (جس کے دو جز دریں) جز وائل -: بابت تفویض طلاق بوقت نکاح : (از فقه حنفی) سوال : آج کل ہندوستان میں قاضی شرعی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے جو شکلات عورتوں کو پیش آرہی ہیں مختارج بیان نہیں، بھنی مرو ظلم کرتا ہے اور بیوی کے حقوق ادا نہیں کرتا۔ نہ نان نفقہ دیتا ہے نہ طلاق کبھی بیوی بچوں کو چھوڑ کر لاپتہ ہوجاتا ہے کہیں مجنوں ہو جاتا ہے، اگر شرعی قاضی موجود ہوتے تو ان مشکلات کا حل سہل تھا۔ لیکن اب جو دشواریاں ہیں کسی سے مخفی نہیں، لہذا دریافت طلب یہ ہے ۔ (۱) کہ بعض جگہ ان مشکلات کا جو یہ علاج تجویز کیا گیا ہے کہ بوقت نکاح کا بین نامہ میں مرد سے کچھ شرطیں ایسی لکھوائی جائیں جن کی وجہ سے عورتوں کو بوقت ضرورت اپنے اوپر طلاق واقع کرنے کا خود اختیار حاصل ہو جائے یہ شرعاً صحیح اور معتبر ہے یا نہیں۔ (۲) اور کیا اس کا بین نامہ کے قبل از نکاح اور بعد از نکاح لکھوانے یا عین نقد نکاح کے وقت شرطوں کو زبانی کہلانے میں کوئی فرق ہے۔ الجواب (1) اسی قسم کا کا بین نامہ لکھوانا جس میں طلاق کا اختیار عورت کے ہاتھ میں دے دیا گیا ہو اور بوقت ضرورت اس سے کام لینا جائز ہے ۔ اور اصطلاح فقر میں اس اختیار دے دینے کو تفویض طلاق کہتے ہیں۔ (۲) اس تفویض کی کئی صورتیں جائز ہیں جن کی تفصیل مع شرائط کے اصل رسالہ الحمیانہ الناجزہ میں مذکورہ ہے، اس جگہ صرف وہ صورت ذکر کی جاتی ہے عوام کے لیے سب سے زیادہ آسان اور عورتوں کے لیے زیادہ مفید اور طرفین کے سب مصالح کی جامع ہے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح سے پہلے ایک اقرار نامہ مندرجہ ذیل الفاظ کے ساتھ مرد سے لکھوا لیا جائے۔ یہ یاد رہے کہ اس اقرار نامہ کا ایک ایک لفظ غور کر کے شرعی قواعد کے موافق طرفین کے مصالح کی پوری رعایت رکھ کر لکھا گیا ہے ، اس میں سے کوئی لفظ بدلا نہ جائے ور یہ بعض صورتوں میں یہ اقرار نامہ بالکل بے کار و بے فائدہ ہو جائے گا، اور وہ اقرار نامہ به شکل کا بین نامہ یہ ہے۔ عہ چونکہ طلاق میں جلدی کرنا شرعاً نا پسندیدہ ہے اس لیے عورت کو لازم ہے کہ اختیار مل جانے کے بعد بھی طلاق واقع کرتے ہیں جلدی نہ کرے بلکہ سوچ سمجھ کر غصہ فرد ہونے کے بعد اپنے خیر خواہوں سے مشورہ اور سنت کے موافق استخارہ کر کے رائے قائم کرے
Summary: The Successful Journal: For the Carrying Group (which has two parts herein). First part: Regarding delegation of divorce at the time of marriage (from Hanafi fiqh). Question: Nowadays in India, due to the absence of a Shari'a judge, the difficulties faced by women are beyond description. The husband oppresses and does not fulfill the wife's rights. He does not provide maintenance nor gives divorce. Sometimes he leaves the wife and children and disappears, or becomes insane. If a Shari'a judge were present, the solution to these difficulties would be easy. But now the problems are not hidden from anyone, so it is inquired: (1) Some places have proposed this remedy: at the time of marriage, certain conditions are written in the marriage deed, giving the woman the authority to effect divorce upon herself when needed; is this legally correct and valid? (2) And is there any difference between writing this in the marriage deed before or after the marriage, or having the conditions spoken verbally at the exact time of marriage? Answer: (1) Writing such a deed in which the authority of divorce is given into the woman's hand and using it at the time of need is permissible. In legal terminology, giving this authority is called 'tafwid al-talaq'. (2) There are several permissible forms of this delegation, the details of which along with conditions are mentioned in the original treatise 'Al-Hamiyya al-Najiza'. Here only that form is mentioned which is easiest for the common people, most beneficial for women, and comprehensive for the interests of both parties. It is that before the marriage, a declaration (iqrarnama) be written from the man with the following wording. It should be remembered that every word of this declaration has been written with consideration, in accordance with Shari'a rules, fully observing the interests of both parties. No word should be changed, otherwise in some cases this declaration will become completely useless and fruitless. And that declaration in the form of a marriage deed is as follows. However, since haste in divorce is disliked in Shari'a, the woman is required, even after receiving the authority, not to hasten in effecting divorce, but to think carefully, after anger subsides, consult her well-wishers, and perform istikhara in accordance with the Sunnah, then make a decision.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) to address the problem of oppressive husbands in the absence of a Shari'a judge. The author first states the problem: women suffer because husbands do not fulfill rights or give divorce. Then the question is posed: can a condition be written in the marriage contract giving the wife authority to divorce herself? The answer is yes, this is permissible in Hanafi fiqh and is called tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce). The author then notes that there are many valid forms, but he provides one specific form that is easiest for the public. He emphasizes that the wording must not be changed, as it has been carefully crafted to preserve the interests of both parties. Finally, he advises women not to use this authority hastily, but to consider carefully after anger, consult others, and perform istikhara. This reflects the Hanafi preference for avoiding unnecessary divorce.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (tafwid al-talaq): Giving the authority to the wife to divorce herself, typically through a condition in the marriage contract.
اقرار نامہ (iqrarnama): A written declaration or deed of acknowledgment, here specifically a deed wherein the husband delegates divorce authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on writing a condition in the marriage contract giving the wife the authority to divorce herself?
A) It is not permissible because divorce is only in the husband's hand.
B) It is permissible and called tafwid al-talaq.
C) It is permissible only if witnessed by a Shari'a judge.
D) It is permissible only after the marriage has been consummated.

Key Takeaway
Tafwid al-talaq is a valid Hanafi legal stratagem that gives a wife the right to divorce herself when her husband fails in his duties, provided precise wording is used and she does not act hastily.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Hila for Tafwid al-Talaq: Conditions and Procedure
Explains the ruling and procedure for a marriage contract condition granting divorce right to wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid Tafwid al-Talaq condition in a marriage contract and identify when the wife's authority to divorce is triggered.

Core Idea
A carefully worded condition in the marriage deed can lawfully give the wife the power to divorce herself — this is a valid hila in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson presents a practical hila (legal stratagem) from the Hanafi tradition to address the difficulty of a wife being trapped in a marriage without access to divorce. The author, Mufti Asraf Ali Thanwi, provides a detailed template for a condition in the marriage deed that grants the wife the right to pronounce divorce upon herself if the husband violates stipulated conditions. We will analyze the legal validity, the necessary conditions, and the precise wording required, as well as the ethical guidance for the wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying problem
Recognize the situation: a wife may need to exit a marriage but lacks khula or judicial recourse. The hila provides a contractual solution.
2
Understand the concept of Tafwid al-Talaq
Tafwid al-Talaq is the husband delegating his right of divorce to the wife, usually conditional on specific events. In Hanafi fiqh, this is permissible if the conditions are clear and not contrary to the marriage contract.
3
Analyze the conditions triggering the wife's authority
The wife only gets authority when the husband violates one of the stipulated conditions and at least two witnesses confirm the violation. This ensures the wife does not act arbitrarily.
4
Note the time limit and scope of authority
The wife must exercise her authority within one month from the confirmation of violation. The authority is limited to the current marriage; if divorced and remarried, the conditions do not carry over.
5
Apply the ethical guidance
Despite having authority, the wife should not hasten to divorce; she must consult, perform istikharah, and ensure it is a considered decision, as divorce is discouraged in haste.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱) کہ بعض جگہ ان مشکلات کا جو یہ علاج تجویز کیا گیا ہے کہ بوقت نکاح کا بین نامہ میں مرد سے کچھ شرطیں ایسی لکھوائی جائیں جن کی وجہ سے عورتوں کو بوقت ضرورت اپنے اوپر طلاق واقع کرنے کا خود اختیار حاصل ہو جائے یہ شرعاً صحیح اور معتبر ہے یا نہیں۔
(۲) اور کیا اس کا بین نامہ کے قبل از نکاح اور بعد از نکاح لکھوانے یا عین نقد نکاح کے وقت شرطوں کو زبانی کہلانے میں کوئی فرق ہے۔
الجواب
(1) اسی قسم کا کا بین نامہ لکھوانا جس میں طلاق کا اختیار عورت کے ہاتھ میں دے دیا گیا ہو اور بوقت ضرورت اس سے کام لینا جائز ہے۔ اور اصطلاح فقر میں اس اختیار دے دینے کو تفویض طلاق کہتے ہیں۔
(۲) اس تفویض کی کئی صورتیں جائز ہیں جن کی تفصیل مع شرائط کے اصل رسالہ الحلیۃ الناجزہ میں مذکورہ ہے، اس جگہ صرف وہ صورت ذکر کی جاتی ہے عوام کے لیے سب سے زیادہ آسان اور عورتوں کے لیے زیادہ مفید اور طرفین کے سب مصالح کی جامع ہے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ نکاح سے پہلے ایک اقرار نامہ مندرجہ ذیل الفاظ کے ساتھ مرد سے لکھوا لیا جائے۔ یاد رہے کہ اس اقرار نامہ کا ایک ایک لفظ غور کر کے شرعی قواعد کے موافق طرفین کے مصالح کی پوری رعایت رکھ کر لکھا گیا ہے، اس میں سے کوئی لفظ بدلا نہ جائے ورنہ بعض صورتوں میں یہ اقرار نامہ بالکل بے کار و بے فائدہ ہو جائے گا، اور وہ اقرار نامہ بہ شکل کا بین نامہ یہ ہے۔ چونکہ طلاق میں جلدی کرنا شرعاً ناپسندیدہ ہے اس لیے عورت کو لازم ہے کہ اختیار مل جانے کے بعد بھی طلاق واقع کرتے وقت جلدی نہ کرے بلکہ سوچ سمجھ کر غصہ فرد ہونے کے بعد اپنے خیر خواہوں سے مشورہ اور سنت کے موافق استخارہ کر کے رائے قائم کرے۔
کابین نامہ
بسم الله الرحمن الرحیم اما بعد: علیکم

ساکن
کے ساتھ شرائط ذیل پر عوض مہر
روپیہ سکہ رائج الوقت کے قرار پایا ہے، لہذا میں بدرستی پویش و حواس با کسی جبر کراہ کے مندرجہ ذیل اقرارنامہ لکھتا ہوں تاکہ میں اس کا پابند ہوں اور در صورت عدم پابندی مسماة مذکور کے لیے رہائی کی صورت ہو سکے۔

پس میں اقرار کرتا ہوں کہ جب تک وہ میرے نکاح میں رہیں شرائط ذیل کا پابند رہوں گا، اور بغرض اطمینان مسماۃ لکھتا ہوں کہ اگر میں مسماة مذکورہ سے نکاح کروں تو نکاح کرنے کے بعد جب کبھی اس کو اس نکاح میں رکھتے ہوئے شرائط ذیل میں سے کسی شرط کے خلاف کروں اور اس خلافت کا ہیرا ہونے کو مندرجہ ذیل اشخاص میں سے م از کم دو آدمی تسلیم کریں تو اس کے بعد مسماة مذکور کو اختیار ہوگا کہ اسی وقت یا خلاقیت شرط تسلیم ہونے سے ایک ماہ تک پھر کسی وقت چاہے اپنے اوپر ایک طلاق بائن واقع کر کے اس نکاح سے الگ ہو جائے۔ اور جب کبھی کسی مشروط کا خلاف وقوع پذیر ہونے ہر بارہ ایک ایک ماہ کے لیے اختیار حاصل ہوتا رہے گا اگر یہ اختیارہ ایک ہی نکاح ایک محدود ہے، اگر کسی طرح فرقت و علیحد گی کے بعد نکاح کا اعادہ ہو تو اس کے بعد یہ اختیار اور شرائط نہیں بلکہ اس وقت جو کچھ دوبارہ طے ہو جاوے اس کے موافقی تملا یا ماہوگا۔
زیادہ احتیاط در کار ہو تو تسلیم کر لیں، کے ہو یہ جملہ بھی لکھ دیا جادو سے " اور وہ دونوں صاحب عورت کے لئے علی گی کو مناسب بھی قرار دے دیں ۔
(1) That in some places, among these difficulties, the remedy that is prescribed is that at the time of marriage, in the marriage deed, some conditions be written from the man which give women the authority to effect divorce upon themselves at the time of need. Is this legally valid and reliable or not? (2) And is there any difference in having the marriage deed written before the marriage, after the marriage, or at the exact moment of marriage having the conditions verbally stated? The answer: (1) Having a marriage deed written in which the authority of divorce is given to the woman and using it at the time of need is permissible. In legal terminology, giving this authority is called Tafwid al-Talaq (delegation of divorce). (2) There are several permissible forms of this delegation, details of which with conditions are mentioned in the original treatise Al-Hilat al-Najizah. Here only that form is mentioned which is easiest for the common people, most beneficial for women, and comprehensive of all interests of both parties. And that is that before marriage, an acknowledgement deed (Iqrar Namah) be written from the man with the following words. Note that every word of this acknowledgement deed has been written after careful consideration, in accordance with legal principles, maintaining full regard for the interests of both parties. Not a word should be changed, otherwise in some cases this acknowledgement deed will become completely useless and fruitless. And that acknowledgement deed in the form of a marriage deed is as follows. Since haste in divorce is disliked legally, therefore it is necessary for the woman that even after receiving the authority, she should not hasten in effecting divorce, but rather think carefully, after anger subsides, consult well-wishers and after performing Istikharah according to Sunnah, form an opinion. Marriage Deed: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. After that: Peace be upon you. Son of, resident of, district of, I am. My marriage with [named] of [community], resident of, is fixed on the following conditions in lieu of dower [amount] rupees of current coinage. Therefore, with full sanity and senses, without any coercion or aversion, I write the following acknowledgement deed so that I am bound to it, and in case of non-compliance, there may be a means of release for the aforementioned woman. So I acknowledge that as long as she remains in my marriage, I will remain bound to the following conditions. And for the satisfaction of the aforementioned woman, I write that if I marry the aforementioned woman, then after marriage, whenever I act contrary to any of the following conditions while keeping her in this marriage, and at least two people from the following individuals confirm the occurrence of this violation, then thereafter the aforementioned woman will have the authority that at that time or within one month from the confirmation of the violation, whenever she wishes, she may effect one irrevocable divorce (talaq-e-bain) upon herself and separate from this marriage. And whenever any violation of a condition occurs, this authority will be obtained each time for a period of one month. If this authority is limited to one marriage only, if by some means separation occurs and marriage is renewed, then afterwards this authority and conditions do not apply; rather whatever is settled again at that time will be acted upon accordingly. If more caution is required, then let them confirm and also write this sentence: 'And those two persons shall also deem it (the separation) appropriate for the woman.'
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) from the Hanafi tradition for giving a wife the right to divorce herself (Tafwid al-Talaq) through conditions written in the marriage deed. The author, Mufti Asraf Ali Thanwi, addresses a common difficulty: women being trapped in abusive marriages with no access to khula or judicial divorce. The answer states that such an arrangement is permissible (ja'iz). The delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq) is a recognized concept in Hanafi fiqh where the husband delegates his right of divorce to the wife, usually conditional on certain events. The author then provides a specific template for an acknowledgement deed (Iqrar Namah) to be signed by the husband before marriage. He emphasizes that the exact wording must be preserved because it is carefully crafted to satisfy all legal requirements and protect the interests of both parties. The deed includes a mechanism: if the husband violates one of the stipulated conditions and at least two witnesses confirm the violation, the wife gets the authority to pronounce one irrevocable divorce (talaq-e-bain) upon herself within one month. Importantly, the authority is limited to the current marriage; if they remarry, the conditions do not carry over. The author also advises the wife not to act hastily but to consult and perform istikharah, since divorce is discouraged in haste. This passage is a practical application of the hila method for legitimate problem-solving in marriage.

Key Terms
تفویض طلاق (Tafwid al-Talaq): The husband delegating the power of divorce to his wife, so that she may pronounce divorce upon herself under specified conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must happen before the wife can exercise her authority to divorce?
A) She must wait one month after marriage
B) The husband must violate a condition and two witnesses confirm it
C) She must obtain permission from a judge
D) The husband must verbally agree at the time of divorce

Key Takeaway
A valid hila for tafwid al-talaq requires a carefully worded written condition, witness confirmation of violation, and a time-limited authority, all while maintaining the ethical discouragement of haste in divorce.

Conditions and Structure of Conditional Delegation of Divorce
Marriage contract deed granting wife conditional delegation of divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the key clauses of a Hanafi marriage deed that grants the wife conditional delegation of divorce, including the trigger, duration, renewal, and termination of the option.

Core Idea
The wife's delegated right to divorce is conditional, time-limited, and confined to one marriage.

This passage presents a practical legal stratagem (hila) from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's work. It illustrates how a husband can grant his wife the right to divorce herself under specific conditions. The deed is a kabin namah (marriage contract) that includes a conditional delegation of divorce (tafwid al-talaq), allowing the wife to pronounce one talaq ba'in if the husband violates stipulated conditions and at least two witnesses confirm the violation. Understanding this structure is essential for anyone advising on contemporary Muslim marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and essential terms
The deed begins by identifying the husband, wife, dower amount, and the recitation of conditions. The core legal mechanism is the husband's declaration that he will abide by the conditions and that breach triggers the wife's option.
Look for phrases like 'شرائط ذیل پر' and 'اقرار کرتا ہوں'.
2
Locate the condition triggering the delegation
The text states that violation of any condition, confirmed by at least two named persons, gives the wife the option to effect a talaq ba'in upon herself.
The condition is 'اگر میں... شرائط ذیل میں سے کسی شرط کے خلاف کروں' and confirmation by witnesses.
3
Determine the duration and renewal of the option
The option lasts for one month from the confirmation of violation. If not exercised, it lapses. However, each new violation grants a fresh one-month option.
The text says 'اخلاق شرط تسلیم ہونے سے ایک ماہ تک' and 'ہر بارہ ایک ایک ماہ کے لیے اختیار حاصل ہوتا رہے گا'.
4
Identify when the option terminates permanently
The option is limited to the current marriage. If the couple divorces and later remarries, the delegation does not carry over; new terms must be agreed.
The text says 'اگر کسی طرح فرقت و علیحد گی کے بعد نکاح کا اعادہ ہو تو اس کے بعد یہ اختیار اور شرائط نہیں'.
5
Note the additional procedural recommendations
The author advises including three impartial persons as witnesses, consulting lawyers, registering the deed, and for the husband's benefit, adding a condition to waive the dower if the wife divorces.
These are practical steps to ensure the hila is enforceable.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. To proceed: Greetings. I, [name], son of [father's name], resident of [district], am [tribe/community], resident of [place], have contracted my marriage with [wife's name], [tribe], resident of [place], upon the following conditions in exchange for a dower of [amount] rupees of current coinage. Therefore, in sound state of mind and senses, without any compulsion or coercion, I make the following declaration so that I am bound by it, and in case of non-compliance, there may be a way for the aforementioned [wife] to obtain release. So I declare that as long as she remains in my marriage, I will abide by the following conditions, and for her satisfaction I write that if I marry the aforementioned [wife], then after the marriage, whenever I act contrary to any of the following conditions while keeping her in this marriage, and at least two of the following persons confirm that this violation has occurred, then thereafter the aforementioned [wife] will have the option to effect one irrevocable divorce upon herself and separate from this marriage, either immediately or within one month from the confirmation of the violation, at any time she wishes. And whenever a violation of any condition occurs, for each time she will have this option for one month. This option is limited to one marriage. If after separation and estrangement the marriage is renewed, then thereafter this option and conditions are null; rather, what is mutually agreed at that time will be followed. If more caution is required, then have them confirm, and also write this sentence: "And those two persons shall also deem the separation appropriate for the woman." These are the persons: [list]. These are the conditions: [list]. I have approved this deed and written after seeing and hearing, today on date [day], month [month], year [year], I sign and fingerprint. The servant, witness, witness. The effect of this deed: After writing this deed, upon one violation of a condition, the woman gets the option for only one month, and at the end of the month the option lapses. But thereafter, if another violation of any condition occurs, then again the option is obtained for one month, and each time a violation occurs the option continues in this manner. However, once the woman effects a divorce or separation occurs in any other way, then upon remarriage, the option is not obtained due to violation of conditions. It is appropriate that at least the names of three persons be determined and written with mutual consent. Regarding the conditions agreed upon, it is appropriate to consult knowledgeable and experienced people, and also lawyers, whether these conditions are valid in law. And registration of the deed is better if possible. And one beneficial thing for the man is that he stipulate the condition of waiving the dower. And in the deed, before the sentence "effect one divorce upon herself", let these words be written: "and after waiving the dower, upon herself..." etc.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage presents a practical hila (legal stratagem) for a wife to obtain divorce in a Hanafi context where the husband has exclusive right of talaq. The document is a marriage deed (kabīn nāmah) that includes a conditional delegation of divorce: the husband agrees that if he violates any of the agreed conditions (to be specified), and at least two of the designated persons confirm the violation, then the wife has the option to pronounce one irrevocable divorce (talaq bā'in) upon herself within one month. This option renews with each violation but expires after one month if not exercised. Importantly, if the marriage ends and later the couple remarries, the option does not carry over; new terms must be agreed. The author also notes precautionary measures: choose three impartial persons, consult experts and lawyers, register the deed, and for the husband's benefit, include a condition waiving the dower. This hila allows the wife to secure a divorce without the husband's direct consent, using a conditional delegation (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq), which is valid in Hanafi law when the husband stipulates it in the marriage contract.

Key Terms
کابین نامہ (kabīn nāmah): A marriage deed or contract document that records the terms of the marriage, including dower and any conditions.
طلاق بائن (ṭalāq bā'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, with no possibility of revocation during the waiting period unless a new marriage contract is made.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): The option or right granted to the wife to pronounce divorce upon herself, conditional on the husband's breach of stipulated conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Indefinitely until she exercises it
B) One month from the confirmation
C) Only for the first violation
D) Until the end of the marriage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a wife can be granted a conditional delegated right to divorce, which is time-bound per violation and does not survive remarriage.

Hanafi Legal Basis for Conditional Delegation of Divorce (Tafwid al-Talaq)
Marriage contract deed granting wife conditional delegation of divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce) and construct a simple conditional delegation clause in a marriage contract.

Core Idea
Tafwid al-talaq is valid in Hanafi fiqh when the husband explicitly delegates and the wife accepts, making the divorce effective upon her choice.

While the previous lesson focused on parsing the deed, this lesson examines the underlying legal principle: tafwid al-talaq (delegation of divorce). The Hanafi school permits a husband to delegate the right to divorce to his wife, either unconditionally or conditionally. The passage illustrates a conditional delegation tied to specific breaches. Understanding the principle allows a mufti to properly advise couples who wish to include such clauses in their marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Define tafwid al-talaq in Hanafi fiqh
Tafwid al-talaq is the husband's delegation of the right to pronounce divorce to his wife. It can be absolute (e.g., 'I leave the matter to you') or conditional (e.g., 'If I hit you, you may divorce yourself'). Hanafis accept both forms.
The term 'tafwid' appears in classical fiqh. The passage uses 'اختیار' to indicate the delegated right.
2
Distinguish between types of delegation
Absolute delegation gives the wife immediate power to divorce at any time. Conditional delegation limits it to a specified event. The passage is a conditional delegation.
This distinction affects when the option becomes available and whether it can lapse.
3
State the conditions for validity
The delegation must be explicit, the wife must accept (explicitly or by conduct), and the conditions must be clear and possible. The husband must be of sound mind and not coerced.
Hanafi texts emphasize clarity to avoid future disputes.
4
Apply to the source passage
The deed fulfills these conditions: explicit declaration, witnesses, defined conditions, and the wife's acceptance through signing. The option is limited to one talaq ba'in per violation.
Note that the delegation is not absolute; it is tied to violations and has time limits.
5
Consider the practical fatwa implications
A mufti must ensure the delegation is documented properly, witnesses are impartial, and the wife understands the limits. The deed should also comply with local civil law if registration is required.
The passage itself includes recommendations for consultation and registration.

اور شرائط نہیں بلکہ اس وقت جو کچھ دوبارہ طے ہو جاوے اس کے موافقی تملا یا ماہوگا۔
زیادہ احتیاط در کار ہو تو تسلیم کر لیں، کے ہو یہ جملہ بھی لکھ دیا جادو سے " اور وہ دونوں صاحب عورت کے لئے علی گی کو مناسب بھی قرار دے دیں ۔
وہ اشخاص یہ ہیں۔
شرائط یہ ہیں
اس کا بین نامہ کو میں نے منظور کیا اور لکھا کر دیکھنے، سننے کے بعد، آج بتاریخ ماہ
سنہ میں دستخط انسان انگشت کرتا ہوں۔
العبد گواه شد گواه شد
اس کا بین نامہ کا اثر
ی کا بین نامہ لکنے کے بعد ایک مرتبہ خلاف شرط کرنے سے عورت کو صرف ایک ماہ کے لیے اختیار ملے گا اور مہینے کے ختم پر اختیار ساقط ہو جائے گا لیکن اس کے بعد اگر پھر کبھی کسی شرط کی خلاف ورزی ہوئی تو پھر کر اختیار ایک ماہ کے لیے مل جائے گا اور ہر مرتبہ خلاف کرنے سے اسی طرح اختیار تمار رہے گا ،مگر ایک مرتبہ عورت طلاق واقع کرے یا اور کسی طرح علیحدگی ہو جاوے تو اس کے بعد دوبارہ نکاح ہونے پر خلان شرط کے وقوع سے اختیار حاصل نہ ہو گا۔
عدہ مناسب ہے کہ کم از کم در آدمیوں کے نام تراضی طرفین سے متعین کر کے لکھ دیے جائیں ۔ سے جو شرائط طے ہوں ان میں اہل فہم اور تجربہ کار لوگوں سے مشورہ کرنا مناسب ہے، تیز و کلاء سے بھی کہ یہ شرائط قانون میں معتبر یں یا نہیں، اور کابین نامہ کی رجسٹری ہو مجھے تو بہتر ہے اور مرد کے حق میں ایک مفید بات یہ ہے کہ مہر معاف کرنے کی شرط لگا لے اور کابین نام میں جو یہ جملہ ہے " اپنے اوپر ایک طلاق واقع کہ ہے، اس سے پیشتر یہ لفظ لکھ دیئے جاویں و مہر معاف کر کے اپنے اوپر الخمر والخر
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. To proceed: Greetings. I, [name], son of [father's name], resident of [district], am [tribe/community], resident of [place], have contracted my marriage with [wife's name], [tribe], resident of [place], upon the following conditions in exchange for a dower of [amount] rupees of current coinage. Therefore, in sound state of mind and senses, without any compulsion or coercion, I make the following declaration so that I am bound by it, and in case of non-compliance, there may be a way for the aforementioned [wife] to obtain release. So I declare that as long as she remains in my marriage, I will abide by the following conditions, and for her satisfaction I write that if I marry the aforementioned [wife], then after the marriage, whenever I act contrary to any of the following conditions while keeping her in this marriage, and at least two of the following persons confirm that this violation has occurred, then thereafter the aforementioned [wife] will have the option to effect one irrevocable divorce upon herself and separate from this marriage, either immediately or within one month from the confirmation of the violation, at any time she wishes. And whenever a violation of any condition occurs, for each time she will have this option for one month. This option is limited to one marriage. If after separation and estrangement the marriage is renewed, then thereafter this option and conditions are null; rather, what is mutually agreed at that time will be followed. If more caution is required, then have them confirm, and also write this sentence: "And those two persons shall also deem the separation appropriate for the woman." These are the persons: [list]. These are the conditions: [list]. I have approved this deed and written after seeing and hearing, today on date [day], month [month], year [year], I sign and fingerprint. The servant, witness, witness. The effect of this deed: After writing this deed, upon one violation of a condition, the woman gets the option for only one month, and at the end of the month the option lapses. But thereafter, if another violation of any condition occurs, then again the option is obtained for one month, and each time a violation occurs the option continues in this manner. However, once the woman effects a divorce or separation occurs in any other way, then upon remarriage, the option is not obtained due to violation of conditions. It is appropriate that at least the names of three persons be determined and written with mutual consent. Regarding the conditions agreed upon, it is appropriate to consult knowledgeable and experienced people, and also lawyers, whether these conditions are valid in law. And registration of the deed is better if possible. And one beneficial thing for the man is that he stipulate the condition of waiving the dower. And in the deed, before the sentence "effect one divorce upon herself", let these words be written: "and after waiving the dower, upon herself..." etc.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage presents a practical hila (legal stratagem) for a wife to obtain divorce in a Hanafi context where the husband has exclusive right of talaq. The document is a marriage deed (kabīn nāmah) that includes a conditional delegation of divorce: the husband agrees that if he violates any of the agreed conditions (to be specified), and at least two of the designated persons confirm the violation, then the wife has the option to pronounce one irrevocable divorce (talaq bā'in) upon herself within one month. This option renews with each violation but expires after one month if not exercised. Importantly, if the marriage ends and later the couple remarries, the option does not carry over; new terms must be agreed. The author also notes precautionary measures: choose three impartial persons, consult experts and lawyers, register the deed, and for the husband's benefit, include a condition waiving the dower. This hila allows the wife to secure a divorce without the husband's direct consent, using a conditional delegation (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq), which is valid in Hanafi law when the husband stipulates it in the marriage contract.

Key Terms
تفویض الطلاق (tafwīḍ al-ṭalāq): Delegation of the right to divorce from husband to wife, either absolutely or conditionally, valid in Hanafi fiqh.
طلاق بائن (ṭalāq bā'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, with no possibility of revocation during the waiting period unless a new marriage contract is made.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): The option or right granted to the wife to pronounce divorce upon herself, conditional on the husband's breach of stipulated conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, is it permissible for a husband to delegate the right of divorce to his wife conditionally?
A) Yes, it is permissible and valid.
B) No, divorce cannot be delegated.
C) Only absolute delegation is valid.
D) It is makruh and discouraged.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi law recognizes tafwid al-talaq as valid, allowing the wife to pronounce divorce if properly delegated, offering a Shariah-compliant mechanism for conditional divorce.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
6 min
Effect of Condition Violation on the Wife's Option in the Marriage Contract
Ruling on the effect of condition violation on wife's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the wife's option to divorce upon condition violation, including the duration of the option, its revival, and its permanent lapse after remarriage.

Core Idea
Each violation gives a one-month option; it lapses after that month but revives on each new violation; after divorce and remarriage, the option is lost forever.

This passage from Asraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatun Najijah explains a legal stratagem (hila) that allows a wife to secure the right to divorce herself if the husband violates agreed conditions. The ruling clarifies the temporal limits of this option and its fate after a remarriage. Understanding this is crucial for muftis drafting marriage contracts with conditional delegations of divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hila mechanism
The hila is a condition in the marriage contract giving the wife the right to divorce herself (tafwid) upon violation of specific terms. This circumvents the normal rule that only the husband can initiate divorce.
This is a valid delegation (tafwid) in Hanafi law as long as it is clearly stipulated.
2
Apply the durational rule
Each violation triggers a one-month window for the wife to exercise her option. If she does not use it, the option lapses at the end of the month. However, a new violation revives it for another month.
The option is not permanent; it is tied to the violation event.
3
Analyze the permanent lapse scenario
If the wife actually divorces (or otherwise separates) using this option, and then the couple remarries, the option does not revive upon future violations. This prevents the wife from using the same condition repeatedly after remarriage.
The remarriage nullifies the original conditional delegation; a new contract would be required to reestablish it.
4
Consider practical drafting advice
The passage advises including a condition for remission of mahr (dower) in favor of the husband, and to consult experts and lawyers to ensure the conditions are legally valid. It also recommends registering the contract.
The remission condition is a common counterbalance to protect the husband's interests.

Source Text

These are the persons. These are the conditions. I have approved this marriage contract and written it after seeing and hearing. Today, date month year, I sign or fingerprint. The servant, witnessed, witnessed. The effect of this marriage contract: After writing the marriage contract, if he violates a condition once, the woman will get an option for only one month, and at the end of the month the option will lapse. But after that, if any condition is violated again, then again the option will be granted for one month, and each time he violates, the option will remain in effect similarly. But if the woman effects a divorce or separation in any other way, then after that, if they remarry, she will not obtain the option from the occurrence of a violation of conditions. It is appropriate that at least four [؟] witnesses' names be written down with mutual consent. Among the conditions that are agreed upon, it is appropriate to consult with understanding and experienced people, and also with lawyers whether these conditions are valid in law, and registration of the marriage contract is better for me. And for the husband, a beneficial thing is that he include a condition for remission of the mahr. And in the marriage contract, this sentence "I will effect one divorce upon myself" — before this, these words should be written: 'And after remitting the mahr, upon myself...' [؟]
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage explains the legal effect of a condition in a marriage contract (kabin nama) that gives the wife the option of divorce if the husband violates certain terms. It is a legal stratagem (hila) to protect the wife's rights. The ruling: each violation gives the wife a one-month window to exercise her option; after that month, the option lapses. However, if the husband violates again, the option revives for another month. Importantly, if the wife actually exercises her option and divorces (or separates in any way), and then they remarry, subsequent violations do not grant her the option again. The passage also advises that at least four witnesses be named, and that the terms be drafted with expert consultation. A recommended condition for the husband is to include remission of the mahr in exchange for the option.

Key Terms
کابین نامہ (kabin nama): The marriage contract document containing the terms and conditions agreed upon by the spouses.
اختیار (ikhtiyar): The option given to the wife to divorce herself upon violation of conditions, valid for one month per violation.
خلاف شرط (khilaf shart): Violation of a condition stipulated in the marriage contract.
تفویض (tafwid): Delegation of the right to divorce by the husband to the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the husband violates a condition again after the wife has already exercised her option and divorced, and then they remarry?
A) The wife gets the option again each time he violates.
B) The wife does not get the option again after remarriage.
C) The option becomes permanent after the first violation.
D) The option lasts for six months after remarriage.

Key Takeaway
A wife's conditional right to divorce in a marriage contract is valid but limited: one month per violation, reviving on new violations, but permanently lost after a divorce and remarriage.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate

The Hila of Adopting the Maliki School for Marriage Annulment
Discusses types of marital harm and the hila for annulment when no qadi is available.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a fatwa that permits a Hanafi woman to annul her marriage by adopting the Maliki school when no Muslim qadi is available and the husband refuses divorce.

Core Idea
In severe necessity, a Hanafi may follow the Maliki school to annul a harmful marriage.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najiyah addresses a pressing modern dilemma: what happens when a Muslim woman is trapped in a harmful marriage but has no access to a Muslim qadi? The author lists five common harms and then presents a hila—a legal stratagem—that allows the woman to obtain annulment by adopting the Maliki school. This lesson unpacks the conditions and reasoning behind this fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Marital Harms
List the five specific types of harm that the author enumerates as grounds for annulment. This establishes the scope of the problem.
The harms are: impotence, insanity, being missing, withholding maintenance, and abandonment.
2
Understand the Necessity of a Qadi
Recognize that in all cases, a woman cannot act independently; she must obtain a qadi's verdict. This is the baseline Hanafi rule.
3
Assess the Contemporary Scenario
Consider the context of colonial India (and by extension modern secular states) where a proper Muslim qadi is absent. Understand the deadlock.
The author notes that non-Muslim judges' verdicts are invalid even if the judge is Muslim but does not apply Shariah.
4
Recognize the Hanafi Deadlock
If the husband refuses divorce or khula, and no qadi exists, the Hanafi school offers no direct remedy. This is the problem the hila solves.
The passage says 'according to Hanafi school, there is no way for the woman to obtain separation.'
5
Construct the Hila
The solution is to adopt the Maliki school, which permits a congregation of Muslims to act as qadi and issue annulment in necessity. Identify the conditions (all members Muslim, following Maliki procedure).
The adoption is permissible only in severe necessity (darura).

ہندوستان میں قاضی کے فیصلہ کی حیثیت
ہندوستان کی جین ریاست میں شرعی قاضی موجود ہیں وہاں پر تو معاملہ آسان ہے لیکن حکومت کے علاقوں میں جہاں پر یہ صورت نہیں ہے ان میں وہ حکام وغیرہ جو لوگ وہ گورنمنٹ کی طرف سے اس قسم کے معاملات میں فیصلہ کا اختیار رکھتے ہیں وہ اگر مسلمان ہوں۔ اور شرعی قاعدہ کے مطابق فیصلہ کریں توان کاحکم بھی قاضی کے فیصلہ کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے اور اگر فیصلہ کرنے والے مسلمان ہوا جیسا کہ آج کل کے عموماً اور ہندوستان کی عدالت کے جج وغیرہ تو قانون شریعت کی رو سے ان کا فیصلہ تسلیم نہیں ہوتا ۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر جوں ، یا ممبران وغیرہ کی کمیٹی فیصلہ کر سے تو ان تمام کا مسلمان ہونا شرط ہے۔ اگر ایک حج یا مبروغیرہ بی غیرمسلم ہو تو شرکا فیصلہ منبر نہیں۔ مسلمان حاکم نہ ہونے کی صورت کا حکم اگر کسی جنگ سان حاکم موجودنہ ہوا سامان اگر کسی جگہ مسلمان حاکم حکم حاکم کی عدالت میں مقدمہ لے جانے کا
قانون کی رو سے اختیار ہویا مسلمان حاکم قانون شریعیت کے مطابق فیصلہ نہ کرتا ہو تو اس صورت میں مذہب حنفی کے مطابق عورت کی علیحدگی کے لیے شوہر سے طلاق لینے یا ضلع دینی مہر یا مال کے بدلہ شوہر سے طلاق لینے کے کوئی صورت نہیں لیکن اگر شوہر طلاق اور خلع پر بھی کسی طریقہ سے رضا مند نہ ہو یا مفقود یا مجنون یا نا بالغ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے طلاق و خلع نہ ہو سکے تو اس وقت مذہب امام مالک کے مطابق جس کا اختیار کرنا ضرورت شدیدہ میں حنفیہ کے نزدیک بھی جائز ہے مسلمانوں کی جماعت کا حکم بھی قامتی کے فیصلہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا۔ اور اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ محلہ بالیستی کے
Part Two: Annulment of Marriage. Introduction: After marriage, the problems that women face from their husbands, and in which there is widespread affliction and severe harm, are several. First: the husband is not capable of fulfilling the wife due to impotence etc., which in fiqh terminology is called 'ain. Second: the man has insanity. Third: the husband is missing and his whereabouts are unknown. Fourth: the husband is present and has the power to provide maintenance but oppresses: he neither gives maintenance nor divorces. Fifth: the husband, though present, leaves the wife and children and goes to another place; he does not manage any maintenance etc., nor does he come back, nor does he send for them, nor does he divorce. For all these cases, there are separate Shariah methods for the liberation of the woman, which will be presented in detail. But in all these cases, this matter is common: the woman or her guardians are not independent in this liberation; rather, the verdict of the qadi is a condition, i.e., it is necessary for the woman to file her case in the court of the qadi. And the qadi, after proper Shariah investigation, issues a ruling of separation etc. But in the present state of India, since a Shariah qadi is not available, therefore this Shariah stratagem is foremost. The status of the qadi's verdict in India: In the princely states of India where Shariah qadis exist, the matter is easy. But in the government territories where this situation does not exist, those officials etc. who are authorized by the government to decide such matters: if they are Muslim and decide according to Shariah rules, then their ruling also stands in place of the qadi's verdict. And if those deciding are not Muslim, as is common nowadays and the judges of India's courts etc., then according to the law of Shariah, their verdict is not accepted. Even if a jury or committee of members gives a verdict, all of them being Muslim is a condition. If one member or chairman etc. is non-Muslim, the verdict of the partners is not valid. The ruling in the absence of a Muslim ruler: if in any place a Muslim ruler is not present, or if a Muslim ruler is present but there is no access to his court due to law, or if the Muslim ruler does not decide according to the law of Shariah, then in this case, according to the Hanafi school, there is no way for the woman to obtain separation by taking a divorce from the husband or by taking a divorce in exchange for the dowry or money. But if the husband does not consent to divorce or khula by any means, or divorce or khula cannot be obtained from him due to him being missing, insane, or a minor, then at that time, according to the Maliki school, the adoption of which is permissible in severe necessity according to the Hanafis, the ruling of a congregation of Muslims will also stand in place of the qadi's verdict. And its form is that the...
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage introduces the second part of the book, dealing with annulment of marriage (faskh al-nikah). The author (Maulana Ashraf Ali Thanwi) lists five common marital problems that cause severe harm to women: (1) the husband's impotence ('ain), (2) his insanity, (3) being missing (mafqud), (4) oppressively withholding maintenance without divorce, and (5) abandoning the family without support or divorce. In all such cases, a woman cannot simply separate herself; she must obtain a qadi's verdict. However, in colonial India, a proper Islamic qadi is often not available. The author discusses the status of government judges: if they are Muslim and rule by Shariah, their verdicts are valid; if they are non-Muslim, their verdicts are invalid. Even a jury must be entirely Muslim. When no Muslim judge exists or the Muslim judge does not apply Shariah, the Hanafi school leaves no remedy if the husband refuses divorce or khula. In severe necessity, it is permissible to adopt the Maliki school, which allows a congregation of Muslims to issue a separation ruling. This is the hila (legal stratagem): seeking annulment through the Maliki school when the Hanafi system fails.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of marriage through qadi's verdict, distinct from talaq and khula.
قاضي (qadi): A Muslim judge qualified to give Shariah rulings; his verdict is necessary for faskh.
مذهب مالك (madhhab Malik): The school of Imam Malik, adopted as a hila when Hanafi offers no remedy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which situation is it permissible for a Hanafi to adopt the Maliki school regarding marriage annulment?
A) Whenever a woman finds her husband impotent
B) When no Muslim qadi is available and the husband refuses divorce
C) Only if the judge is a Muslim
D) When the husband is missing

Key Takeaway
When the Hanafi system cannot provide relief due to absence of a Muslim qadi, a mufti may direct a woman to obtain annulment through the Maliki school using a Muslim committee.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate

Shari'ah Committee as Substitute for Muslim Qadi
Explaining the legal stratagem and conditions for a shari'ah committee to act as qadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid shari'ah committee as a substitute for a qadi in the absence of a Muslim judge, applying the Hanafi conditions of 'adalah and scholarly consultation.

Core Idea
In severe necessity, a committee of three just Muslims can replace the qadi — but only if they are 'adil and include or consult scholars.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi addresses a pressing dilemma for Muslims living under non-Muslim rule: how to obtain a Shari'ah-recognized divorce or khula when no Muslim qadi exists. The author presents a legal stratagem (hila) — forming a shari'ah committee that acts as a substitute qadi, adopting the Maliki school's allowance of judicial annulment (faskh) under necessity. But this committee is not any group; it must meet strict conditions of moral integrity (adalah) and scholarly competence. Let us examine these conditions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Recognize the absence of a Muslim qadi and the difficulty for a woman to obtain divorce/khula under default Hanafi rules. The Hanafi school does not allow a qadi to dissolve a marriage except in rare cases like impotence.
Without this stratagem, the woman would remain trapped in a harmful marriage.
2
Recognize the Hila
Understand that in severe necessity (darurat shadidah), the Hanafi school permits adopting the Maliki ruling, which allows a group of Muslims to act as a qadi and grant faskh.
This is a legitimate cross-madhhab adoption based on necessity.
3
Analyze the Conditions
List the conditions for a valid shari'ah committee: all members must be Muslim and 'adil, the committee must consist of at least three persons, and it must include or consult scholars.
Each condition is explicitly stated in the passage.
4
Apply the Definition of 'Adil
Use the definition of 'adil (one who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and repents immediately) to identify who is disqualified: usurer, bribe-taker, beard-shaver, liar, neglecter of prayer.
This definition ensures the integrity of the committee.

مسلمان حاکم نہ ہونے کی صورت کا حکم
اگر کسی جگہ مسلمان حاکم موجود نہ ہو یا اگر مسلمان حاکم حکم حاکم کی عدالت میں مقدمہ لے جانے کا قانون کی رو سے اختیار ہو یا مسلمان حاکم قانون شریعت کے مطابق فیصلہ نہ کرتا ہو تو اس صورت میں مذہب حنفی کے مطابق عورت کی علیحدگی کے لیے شوہر سے طلاق لینے یا ضلع دینی مہر یا مال کے بدلہ شوہر سے طلاق لینے کے کوئی صورت نہیں لیکن اگر شوہر طلاق اور خلع پر بھی کسی طریقہ سے رضا مند نہ ہو یا مفقود یا مجنون یا نا بالغ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے طلاق و خلع نہ ہو سکے تو اس وقت مذہب امام مالک کے مطابق جس کا اختیار کرنا ضرورت شدیدہ میں حنفیہ کے نزدیک بھی جائز ہے مسلمانوں کی جماعت کا حکم بھی قاضی کے فیصلہ کے قائم مقام ہوگا۔ اور اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ محلہ بالیستی کے دیندار اور اثر و رسوخ رکھنے والے مسلمانوں کی ایک جماعت بناکر جو کہ کم از کم تین حضرات پیش ہو اپنا معاملہ پیش کیا جائے اور وہ جماعت واقعہ کی تحقیق کر کے شریعت کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دے۔
شرعی کمیٹی کی شرائط
شرعی کمیٹی کو قاضی شرعی کے قائم مقام کرنے کے لیے چند شرائط ہیں جس کمیٹی میں یہ چند شرائط موجود نہ ہوں وہ شرعاً معتبر نہ ہوگی۔
عادل کی تعریف
کم از کم تین آدمیوں کی جماعت ہو ایک یا دو آدمی فیصلہ کریں تو وہ معتبر نہیں۔ اس کمیٹی کے تمام ارکان کا عادل ہونا شرط ہے، اور عادل وہ شخص ہے جو تمام کبیرہ گناہوں سے بچتا ہو اور صغائر پر مصر نہ ہو اور اگر کوئی گناہ سرزد ہوجاتا ہے تو فوراً توبہ کر لیتا ہو۔ لہذا سود خور اور رشوت لینے والا، داڑھی منڈانے والا، جھوٹ بولنے والا اور بے نماز اس جماعت کا رکن نہیں بن سکتا اگر بدقسمتی سے کسی جگہ کے با اثر لوگ دیندار نہ ہوں تو یہ تدبیر کرلی جائے کہ وہ با اثر اشخاص چند دینداروں کو اختیار دے دیں تا کہ شرکا فیصلہ کی نسبت دیندار جماعت کی رائے ہو اور ان با اثر اشخاص کو کوشش کا ثواب حاصل ہو جائے۔
فیصلہ میں علماء کی شرکت لازم اور شرط ہے، کی فیصلہ میں عام کی شرکت لازم ہے صرف عوام کی جماعت کا [؟] دیکر قاضی کے قائم مقام نہیں ہو سکتا، اس لیے یہ چاہیے کہ جماعت کے سب ارکان اہل علم ہوں ور اگر یہ ممکن نہ ہوتو کم از کم ایک عالم کو ضرور جماعت کا رکن بنائیں اور دور سے اس کا معاملہ کے تمام پہلوؤں کو اس عالم صاحب سے خوب سمجھ کر رائے قائم کریں اور اگر کسی جگہ یہ بھی ممکن نہ ہوتو پھر یہ لازم ہے کہ جماعت کے ارکان معاملہ کی روداد مرتب کر کے علماء محققین سے ہر ہر جزئی کا حکم دریافت کریں اور جو ان کا فتوی ہو اس کے مطابق فیصلہ کریں۔
In the present situation, since a Shari'ah qadi is not present, therefore the Shari'ah stratagem for this is rather foremost. The status of a qadi's decision in India: In the princely states of India where Shari'ah qadis exist, the matter is easy there, but in government areas where this situation is not present, those officials etc. who have authority from the government to decide in such matters, if they are Muslims and decide according to Shari'ah rules, then their ruling also stands in place of the qadi's decision. And if the decision-makers are not Muslims, as is common nowadays and the judges of Indian courts etc., then according to Shari'ah law their decision is not accepted. Even if a committee of [??] or members decides, being Muslim is a condition for all of them. If one judge or member is non-Muslim, the decision is not valid. Ruling for the situation where there is no Muslim ruler: If in some place there is no Muslim ruler, or if a Muslim ruler exists but there is no authority to take a case to his court according to the law, or the Muslim ruler does not decide according to Shari'ah law, then according to the Hanafi school there is no way for a woman to obtain separation from her husband by taking divorce or by taking divorce in exchange for dower or property. But if the husband does not consent to divorce or khula in any way, or because he is missing, insane, or a minor, divorce or khula cannot be obtained from him, then according to the Maliki school, which it is permissible for Hanafis to adopt in severe necessity, the ruling of a group of Muslims will also stand in place of the qadi's decision. Its form is that a group of the pious and influential Muslims of the locality, consisting of at least three persons, be formed, and the case be presented to them, and that group investigate the reality and decide according to Shari'ah. Conditions of the Shari'ah committee: There are several conditions for the Shari'ah committee to stand in place of a Shari'ah qadi; a committee that does not have these conditions will not be valid Shari'ah-wise. Definition of 'adil: The group should consist of at least three people; if one or two persons decide, it is not valid. All members of this committee being 'adil is a condition. And an 'adil person is one who avoids all major sins and does not persist in minor sins, and if a sin occurs, he immediately repents. Therefore, a usurer, a bribe-taker, a beard-shaver, a liar, and a neglecter of prayer cannot be members of this group. If unfortunately in some place the influential people are not pious, then this device may be used: that those influential persons delegate authority to a few pious persons so that the decision is based on the opinion of the pious group, and the influential persons receive the reward of effort. The participation of scholars in the decision is necessary and a condition. [It is] necessary [that] the general public's participation [??] cannot stand in place of the qadi. Therefore, it is necessary that all members of the group be scholars; if this is not possible, then at least one scholar must be made a member of the group, and from afar the group should understand all aspects of the case well from that scholar and form an opinion. And if in some place this is also not possible, then it is incumbent that the members of the group prepare a record of the case and inquire from investigating scholars the ruling on every detail, and according to whatever fatwa they give, they should decide accordingly.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a legal stratagem (hila) from the Hanafi tradition, addressing the problem of obtaining a Shari'ah divorce or khula when there is no properly appointed Muslim qadi. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, explains that in British India, government courts and non-Muslim judges cannot issue a valid Shari'ah divorce. However, in severe necessity (darurat shadidah), it is permissible for Hanafis to adopt the Maliki school, which allows a group of Muslims (at least three) to act as a qadi and grant a faskh (judicial annulment) or khula. The passage then outlines the conditions for such a committee: all members must be Muslim and 'adil (just). The definition of 'adil is given: one who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and repents immediately. Thus, those who commit usury, take bribes, shave their beards, lie, or neglect prayer cannot serve. Additionally, the committee must include at least one scholar, or if not possible, must consult scholars. This ensures the decision is based on proper fiqh. This teaching is a practical solution for Muslims living under non-Muslim rule or in areas without a Shari'ah judiciary.

Key Terms
قاضی شرعی (qadi shara'i): A Shari'ah judge appointed by a Muslim ruler to adjudicate disputes according to Islamic law.
عادل ('adil): A person who avoids major sins, does not persist in minor sins, and repents quickly if he sins.
ضرورت شدیدہ (darurat shadidah): Severe necessity that permits adopting a different madhhab (e.g., Maliki) for a specific ruling to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum number of members required for a shari'ah committee to act as a qadi?
A) One person
B) Two persons
C) Three persons
D) Five persons

Key Takeaway
A shari'ah committee can substitute for a qadi when all members are Muslim, 'adil, at least three, and include or consult scholars — a hila valid under severe necessity.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on the Wife of an Impotent Husband: Definition and Procedure for Faskh
Defines 'aneen and details faskh procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term 'aneen in Hanafi law, explain the conditions under which a wife can seek annulment (faskh), and identify the steps in the judicial procedure, including the dispute about the length of the waiting period.

Core Idea
A wife may seek annulment only after a one-year waiting period, during which the husband may seek treatment.

This lesson addresses a critical hila (legal stratagem) in family law: the case of the 'aneen (impotent husband). Hanafi jurists have detailed procedures to balance the wife's right to a consummated marriage with the husband's opportunity to remedy his condition. Understanding this ruling is essential for muftis dealing with modern marriage disputes.

Guided Path
1
Define the 'aneen
Identify the linguistic and legal definition: a man who has the male organ but cannot perform intercourse due to any cause (illness, weakness, old age, witchcraft).
Note the key condition: inability must be specific to this woman.
2
Distinguish functional impotence
If the husband can have intercourse with some women, he is not considered 'aneen with respect to those women. This is a crucial condition (shart) that determines the applicability of the ruling.
The definition is relative to the particular wife.
3
Outline the judicial procedure
The wife goes to a qadi. The qadi investigates: first asks the husband. If he admits, a one-year waiting period is given. If he denies, and the wife does not claim virginity, he is asked to swear an oath; if he swears, she cannot annul; if he refuses, the waiting period is given. If she claims virginity, an examination by women is ordered, and depending on the result, either an oath or direct waiting period is given.
The procedure balances the husband's word with objective evidence.
4
Identify the internal ikhtilaf
The waiting period: According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the core texts), it is a lunar year. However, a transmission from Hasan ibn Ziyad (Riwayat al-Hasan) says it is a solar year. Later scholars preferred the solar year out of caution (ihtiyat).
This is a valid intra-madhhab difference.
5
Apply the tarjih for fatwa
The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) today is the solar year, as adopted by the mutakhkhirin (later scholars) and common practice of muftis. The year starts from the date of the judge's order.
Any time before the order is not counted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عنین (نامرد) کی بیوی کے احکام

سوالات :- شریعت کی اصطلاح میں عنین کس کو کہتے ہیں۔ وہ عینین کی بیوی کو نکاح کے فسخ کرانے کا اختیار دیا جائے گا یا نہیں ؟ اگر اختیار دیا جائے تو اس کی کیا صورت ہوگی اور اس کے لیے کیا شرائط ہیں۔ کے تفریق (یعنی فیم نکاح کے بعد جنین پر مہر اوپر واجب ہو گا یا آدھا، نیز عورت پر عدت لازم ہوگی یا نہیں۔

الجواب : شریعت کی اصطلاح میں عین اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ تو باد جود عضو مخصوص ہونے کے عورت سے ہمبستری کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو خواہ یہ حالت کسی بیماری کی وجہ سے پیدا ہوئی ہو یا کمزوری کی وجہ سے یا ضعیفی کی وجہ سے ، یا اس وجہ سے کہ اس پر کسی نے جادو کرایا ہو۔ اور اگر کوئی شخص ایسا ہو کہ بعض عورتوں سے ہمبستری کرنے پر قدرت رکھتا ہے اور بعض پر نہیں، تو میں عورت سے ہمبستری پر قدرت ہو اس کے حق میں یہ شخص عیین نہیں بلکہ عام مرد سمجھا جائے گا۔

نامرد کی بیوی کو اپنے شوہر سے عنین کی بیوی کے فسخ نکاح کی صورت تفریق رفسخ نکاح کی یہ صورت ہے کہ عورت اپنا معالمہ قاضی شرعی کی عدالت میں پیش کرنے قاضی، واقعہ کی تحقیق کرے یعنی پہلے شوہر سے دریافت کرے اگر وہ خود اقرار کرے کہ بے شک میں اس عورت بستری پر قادر نہیں ہوا تو اس کو ایک سال کی مہلت علاج کرنے کے لیے دسے دے اور اگر وہ اقرار نہ کرے بلکہ ہمبستری کا دعوی کرے تو اس وقت یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر عورت باکرہ کنواری ہونے کا دعوی نہ کرتی ہو جب تو شوہر سے حلف لیا جائے گا، اور اگر اس نے حلف کر لیا تو عورت کو تفریق کا منی حاصل نہ ہو سکے گا۔ اور اگر شوہر نے حلف سے انکار کر دیا تو اس کو ایک سال کی مہلت علاج کے لیے دے دی جائے گی اور اگر عورت باکرہ ہونے کی مدعی ہو تو قاضی عورتوں سے اس کی بیوی کا معائنہ کرائے ایک عادل تجربہ کار عورت کا معائنہ بھی کافی ہے لیکن احتیاط اس میں ہے کہ دو عادل عورتیں معائنہ کریں آگے بعد معائنہ کے دو صورتیں ہیں، ایک صورت یہ که عورتین به بیان کریں کہ یہ عورت باکره یعنی کنواری نہیں رہی تب تو خاوند سے اس بات پر حلف لیا جائے کہ اس نے جماع کیا ہے اگر وہ علف کرلے تو اس کا قول معتبر ہو جائے گا اور عورت کو تفریق کا حق باقی نہ رہے گا اور اگر شوہر حلف سے انکار کرے تو تا جیل لینی ایک سال کی ملت کا حکم کردیا جائے گا ،اور دوسری صورت یہ کہ عورتیں یہ بیان کریں کہ ابھی تک یہ لڑکی باکرہ کنواری ہے تو پھر قاضی بدون کسی سے حلف لیے ہوئے شوہر یعنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت علاج کے لیے دے دے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ جب کسی دلیل سے محقق ہو جاوے کہ عورت باکرہ نہیں بلکہ یہ ہے خواہ ٹیبہ ہونا اس طرح عام ہو کہ وہ ہوں ہو اور شوہر اول سے اولاد ہو چکی ہو یا خود عورت کے اقرار سے یا عورتوں کے معائنہ سے ان تینوں حالتوں میں مرد کا قول خلف کے ساتھ قبول کر لیا جاوے گا کہ وہ ہم بستری کر چکا اور عورت کو علیحدگی کا حق نہ دیا جائے گا، اور اگران تینوں حالتوں میں مرد حلف سے انکار کر دے تو عورت کا دعویٰ درست مان کر مرد کو ایک سال کی مہلت دے دیں۔ اور اگر عورتوں کے معائنہ سے زوجہ کا باکرہ ہونا ثابت ہو تو بغیر حلف ہیں ایک سال کی مہلت دے دی جاوے اور اس مہلت کے لیے ظاہر الروابیہ ہیں تو مری سال کا اعتبار کا گیا ہے لیکن روایت حسن میں شمسی سال کو لیا ہے اور بعض اصحاب ترجیح نے احتیاطاً اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے اور عموما متاخرین نے اسی پر فتوی دیا ہے اور اب بھی عام اہل فتوی کا بھی معمول ہے اور یہ سال حاکم کی مہلت دینے کے وقت سے شروع سمجھا جائے گا اس سے پہلے خواہ کتنی ہی مدت گزر گئی ہو معتبر
Rulings on the wife of an impotent husband. Questions: In Shar'i terminology, who is called an 'aneen? Will the wife of an 'aneen be given the right to annul the marriage? If given, what is the procedure and what are its conditions? After annulment, will the full mahr be due or half? Will the woman have to observe 'iddah? Answer: In Shar'i terminology, an 'aneen is one who, despite having a male organ, is unable to have intercourse with a woman, whether due to illness, weakness, old age, or witchcraft. If a person is able to have intercourse with some women but not others, then for the woman he can have intercourse with, he is not an 'aneen but a normal man. The procedure for a woman to seek annulment from her impotent husband is: she presents her case to a Shar'i judge; he investigates, first asking the husband. If the husband admits he cannot have intercourse, the judge gives him one year to seek treatment. If he denies it and claims he did have intercourse, then if the woman does not claim to be a virgin, he is asked to take an oath. If he swears, the woman cannot get annulment. If he refuses the oath, he is given one year. If the woman claims virginity, the judge has her examined by women; one reliable experienced woman suffices, but caution is with two. After examination: if they say she is not a virgin, the husband is asked to swear he had intercourse. If he swears, his word is accepted and she loses the right. If he refuses, one year is granted. If they say she is still a virgin, the judge gives one year without any oath. Summary: When it is established by some evidence that she is not a virgin — either through general knowledge (e.g., she has children from a previous husband), her own admission, or examination — then the husband's word backed by oath is accepted that he had intercourse and she cannot separate. But if he refuses the oath, her claim is accepted and one year is given. If examination shows she is a virgin, one year is given without oath. For the year, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, a lunar year is counted, but in Riwayat al-Hasan, a solar year is taken, and some later scholars preferred it for caution, and generally the later scholars gave fatwa on it, and now common practice of most muftis is also that. This year is considered from the time the judge gives the respite; any period passed before that is not considered.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling (hila) dealing with the case of an impotent husband ('aneen). It begins by defining 'aneen: a man who cannot perform intercourse despite having the organ, irrespective of cause (illness, weakness, old age, or witchcraft). If a man can have intercourse with some women but not with this specific woman, he is not considered 'aneen for her. The core ruling: the wife has the right to seek annulment (faskh) of the marriage. The procedure is detailed: the wife goes to a qadi; the qadi investigates. If the husband admits impotence, he gets one year for treatment. If he denies and claims intercourse, then if the wife does not claim virginity, he is asked to swear an oath; if he swears, she cannot annul; if he refuses, he gets one year. If the wife claims virginity, the qadi orders an examination by women. If the women report she is not a virgin, the husband swears; if he swears, he is believed; if he refuses, one year. If they report she is still a virgin, no oath is needed; one year is given. The summary clarifies three ways to establish non-virginity: common knowledge, her own admission, or examination; in those cases the husband's oath is accepted. If he refuses, her claim is accepted. The passage also discusses the length of the year: according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmissions), it is a lunar year; but in a rare transmission (Riwayat Hasan), it is a solar year. Many later scholars (mutakhkhirin) preferred the solar year for caution, and this is the common practice of muftis. The year starts from the judge's order; any previous period is not counted. Note: The text does not explicitly answer the questions about mahr and 'iddah here, so we leave that aside.

Key Terms
عنین ('aneen): A man who cannot perform intercourse despite having the male organ, due to any cause.
فسخ نکاح (faskh al-nikah): Annulment of marriage by judicial decree at the wife's request due to husband's impotence.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation between spouses due to a defect; synonymous with faskh in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the length of the waiting period as per Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) One solar year
B) One lunar year
C) Six months
D) One month

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a detailed procedure for annulment due to impotence, with a one-year waiting period starting from the judge's order, and the operative fatwa uses the solar year.
