Return of the Missing Husband: Hanafi Ruling and Maliki Hila
Explaining Hanafi and Maliki rulings when a missing husband returns after wife's remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a legal stratagem (hila) using the Maliki ruling when a missing husband returns after his wife's remarriage, by applying the condition of the second husband's knowledge.

Core Idea
A hila can resolve the impasse of a returning missing husband by adopting the Maliki condition of the second husband's knowledge.

This lesson examines the fiqhi predicament when a husband declared dead returns after his wife has remarried. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between consummation and non-consummation, but when the second husband knew the first was alive, a dilemma arises. The Maliki position offers a nuanced solution that can be adopted as a hila (legal stratagem) to preserve justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling scenario
Determine whether the missing husband returned before or after the second husband had valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) with the wife. This dictates the basic Hanafi ruling.
The first scenario (before khalwat) is clear: the wife returns to the first husband.
2
Analyze the Maliki position
In the second scenario (after consummation), the Maliki school adds a condition: the second husband must have been unaware that the first husband was alive. If he knew, the wife returns to the first husband.
This condition is the key to the hila.
3
Assess the need for a hila
In the Hanafi school, if the second husband knew, the wife would still stay with him because the court's death declaration is operative. To avoid injustice, adopt the Maliki ruling as a hila.
The hila applies only when the second husband had knowledge.
4
Construct the hila
To implement the hila, the first husband and wife perform a new marriage contract after the second husband divorces her, or the second husband divorces her and she marries the first. The Maliki view validates this outcome.
The hila requires following the Maliki school on this specific point.

سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ہند وستان، مصر و شام وغیرہ ممالک کہ جن میں حکومت کا فرد مسلط ہونے کے با وجود، اسلامی شعائر ابھی تک قائم ہیں ان سب میں مفقود کا حکم رہ ہی ہے جو دارالاسلام میں ہے بلکہ جس دارالحرب من شعائر اسلام بھی موجود نہ ہوں مگر وہاں مسلمانوں کو صلح وغیرہ کی وجہ سے آنا جانا اور تفتیش کرناممکن ہو تو اس دار الحرب میں بھی وہ ہیں حکم ہے جو کہ دارال اسلام میں ہے ہیں اصل بنا امکان تفتیش ہے اس وجہ سے ہندو است کے دارالحرب ہونے میں جو علاء کا اختلاف ہے اس کا اس مسلہ پر کوئی اثر نہ پڑے گا اور مفقود کی بیوی کو ان ملکوں میں چار سال کی مہلت کے بعد عدت وفات گزار کر نکاح ثانی کا اختیار دے دیا جائے گا۔
مفقود کے واپس آجانے کے فقہی مسائل
سوالات : اگر مفقود ، شرعی کمیٹی مسلمان حاکم شرعی قاضی کی جانب سے اس کے مرنے کے فیصلہ ہو جانے کے بعد، اُس کی بیوی کا دوسرا نکاح کر لینے کے بعد دوسرے شوہر کے ہمبستری کرنے سے پہلے آجائے یا دوسرے شوہر سے جیستری وغیرہ ہونے کے بعد واپس آجائے تر مقصود کو اس کی بیوی لے گی یا نہیں اور ان تمام صورتوں کے لیے حکم ایک ہی ہے یا مختلف ؟؟ ما دوسرے شوہر سے صرف نکاح ہو جائے، یا نکاح اور ہم بستری دونوں ہوتے کے بعد مفقود کے واپس آنے پر اگر بیوی اس کو مل جاتی ہو تو اس کے متعلق چند تفصیلی پراگر
سوالات ہیں۔
الف : کیا پہلے شوہر کو دوبارہ نکارت کرنا ضروری ہوگا ، یا ویسے ہی پہلا نکاح قائم اور باقی سمجھا جائے گا۔
(ب) دوبارہ نکاح کرنے کی صورت میں نیا ہر مقرر کرنے کی بھی ضرورت ہوگی یا نہیں ؟
(ج) اس صورت میں دوسرے خاوند کی عدت بھی واجب ہوگی یا نہیں ، اور اگر واجب ہوگی تو کتنے ایام اور یہ عدت شوہر ثانی کے مکان پر گزاری جائے گی یا شوہر تو اور یہ اول کے۔
(د) دوسرے شوہر کے زمرہ جو مہر تھا اس کا ادا کرنا واجب رہے گا یا نہیں۔ (ہ) اگر زوج ثانی سے اولاد ہو چکی ہو یا تفریق کے بعد زمانہ عدت میں ہو جاوے تو اس اولاد کا نسب کسی سے ثابت ہوگا پہلے خاوند سے یا دوسرے سے۔
الجواب :- وہ مفقود جس پر مرافعہ اور تفتیش کے بعد چار سال تک انتظار کر کے قاضی نے موت کا حکم کر دیا ہے اگر حکم بالموت کے بعد واپس آجائے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ شوہر ثانی کے ساتھ خلوت سمجھ ہونے سے پہلے آجادے خواہ مارت وفات کے اندر یا بعد، اور خواہ نکاح ثانی سے پہلے یا بعد دوسری یہ کہ ایسے وقت واپس آجائے جب کہ عدت وفات گزارنے کے بعد عورت دوسرے مرد سے نکاح کر چکی اور خلوت صحیحہ بھی ہو چکی ہو۔ ان میں سے پہلی صورت کا حکم بالا نفاق یہ ہے کہ زوجہ شوہر اقل ہی کے نکات میں بدستور سابق رہے گی دوسرے خاوند کے پاس نہیں رہ سکتی ۔ اور دوسری صورت میں مالکیہ کا تومشہور زمینیت یہی ہے کہ زوجہ دوسرے خاوند کے عہ ایک ضروری بات قابل تقلبی یہ ہے کہ مالکیہ کے مذہب مشہور میں بھی زوج ثانی سے ہم بستری کے بعد شو سر اتوں کا حق فوت ہو جانے کی ایک شرط ہے وہ یہ کہ دوسرے خاوند کو اس بات کی خیرنہ ہو کہ اس عورت کا خاوند اپنہ ہے اور اگر شہر جو کہ اس کا خاوند پتہ ہے تو پھر شوہر ثانی کے دخول اور ہم بستری کے بعد واپس آنے پر بھی شوہر اول کا نکاح باقی رکھا جائے گا اور اسی کو مل جاوے گی۔
It is known from this that Hindustan, Egypt, Syria, etc., countries where despite the presence of a non-Muslim government, Islamic rites are still established — all these have the same ruling as Dar al-Islam regarding a missing person (mafqud). Even in a Dar al-Harb where no Islamic rites exist, but where Muslims can come and go and investigate due to peace treaties etc., the same ruling as Dar al-Islam applies. The basis is the possibility of investigation. Therefore, the difference of opinion about Hindustan being Dar al-Harb will have no effect on this issue. In these countries, the wife of a mafqud will be given the option to marry another after a period of four years and completing the waiting period of death (iddat al-wafat).

Fiqhi Issues Regarding the Return of the Mafqud
Questions: If the mafqud, after the decision of his death by a Shari'ah committee, a Muslim ruler, or a Shari'ah judge, returns after his wife has remarried — if he returns before the second husband has consummated the marriage, or after consummation — will his wife be returned to him? Is the ruling one and the same for all these scenarios or different? After the second husband has only married, or after both marriage and consummation, when the mafqud returns, if his wife is available, detailed questions about them are as follows:

a) Will the first husband need to remarry her, or will the first marriage be considered intact and valid?
b) In the case of remarriage, is it necessary to stipulate a new dower?
c) In this case, will the iddah of the second husband be obligatory? If it is, for how many days, and will it be spent in the house of the second husband or the first?
d) Will the dower that was stipulated for the second husband remain obligatory or not?
e) If the second husband has already had children, or if a child is born during the waiting period after separation, to whom will the child's lineage be attributed — the first husband or the second?

Answer: The mafqud for whom after investigation and waiting four years the judge has issued a death ruling — if he returns after the death ruling, there are two scenarios. First: he returns before the second husband has had seclusion (khalwat sahiha) with the wife, whether before or after the death waiting period, and whether before or after the second marriage. Second: he returns at a time when the woman has completed her death waiting period, married another man, and valid seclusion has also occurred. The ruling for the first scenario is clearly that the wife remains in the marriage of the first husband as before; she cannot stay with the second husband. As for the second scenario, the famous position of the Maliki school is that the wife stays with the second husband. But an important point worthy of observation is that even in the Maliki school, after consummation by the second husband, the right of the first husband is lost only on one condition: that the second husband had no knowledge that this woman's husband was alive. If he knew that her husband was alive, then even after the second husband's consummation and then the first husband's return, the first husband's marriage remains intact, and she will be given to him.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah addresses the complex fiqhi issue of a missing husband (mafqud) who returns after a court has declared him dead and his wife has remarried. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, first clarifies that in countries like India, Egypt, and Syria where Islamic courts function despite non-Muslim governance, the ruling regarding a mafqud is that of Dar al-Islam. The key is the possibility of investigation (imkan tafteesh). Thus, the wife is given the option to remarry after four years of waiting and completing the iddat of death.

The core of the lesson presents two scenarios for the mafqud's return. The first scenario is that he returns before the second husband has had valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) with the wife. In this case, the Hanafi ruling is clear: the wife remains with the first husband; the second marriage is void. The second scenario is that he returns after the second marriage has been consummated. Here, the text explicitly presents the Maliki ruling: the wife stays with the second husband only if the second husband was unaware that the first husband was alive. If he knew, then the first husband's marriage is preserved. While the Hanafi ruling for this scenario is not fully stated in this passage, it is known from elsewhere that in Hanafi fiqh, once the second marriage is consummated, the first husband's marriage is annulled, and the wife remains with the second husband regardless of the second husband's knowledge. The author's mention of the Maliki view serves as a comparative point and may be presented as a legal stratagem (hila) for cases where the second husband knew.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A person who is missing and whose whereabouts or life status are unknown.
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem used to resolve a fiqhi impasse, often by following an alternative ruling from another school.
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwat sahiha): Valid seclusion between a married couple where no legal impediment prevents consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Maliki school, after the second husband has consummated the marriage, the right of the first husband is lost only on which condition?
A) The first husband accepted the second marriage.
B) The second husband was unaware that the first husband was alive.
C) The wife willingly stayed with the second husband.
D) The court approved the second marriage.

Key Takeaway
When a missing husband returns after his wife's remarriage and consummation, the Hanafi default keeps her with the second husband, but the Maliki condition of the second husband's knowledge provides a hila to restore the first marriage.

Ruling on the Return of a Missing Husband After Judicial Death Declaration
Fatwa on missing husband's return after judicial death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on a missing husband's return and evaluate when it is permissible to follow a non-Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The original marriage survives the judge's death declaration; the missing husband's return voids the second marriage.

A missing husband (mafqud) declared dead by a judge after four years returns. The wife has remarried and may have consummated. This fatwa from Ashraf Ali Thanwi clarifies the Hanafi ruling: the first marriage remains intact, and the second marriage is void. It also discusses when a Hanafi may follow another school in cases of necessity, but here no such necessity exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage divides the return of the missing husband into two scenarios: before valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) with the second husband, and after valid seclusion. Understand the significance of valid seclusion in Hanafi law.
Valid seclusion is equivalent to actual intercourse for most rulings.
2
Pinpoint the Hanafi vs Maliki difference
The Maliki school holds that after consummation with the second husband, the wife stays with him. The Hanafi school holds the opposite. Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this difference.
The Hanafi position protects the original marriage unconditionally.
3
Analyze the necessity rule for following another madhhab
The author states that a Hanafi may follow a non-Hanafi school only in extreme necessity, e.g., to free a wife from a missing husband. Here, since the missing husband returned, necessity vanishes. Understand the boundaries of following other schools.
This is a key principle in Hanafi iftaa.
4
Derive the answers to the sub-questions
Using the Hanafi position, answer the five sub-questions: (1) first marriage remains; (2) no new mahr; (3) iddah of second husband must be observed; (4) lineage follows the second husband if born during iddah; (5) mahr of second husband remains owed if consummation occurred.
Each answer flows from the invalidity of the second marriage.

Source Text

ج) اس صورت میں دوسرے خاوند کی عدت بھی واجب ہوگی یا نہیں ، اور اگر واجب ہوگی تو کتنے ایام اور یہ عدت شوہر ثانی کے مکان پر گزاری جائے گی یا شوہر اول کے۔
د) دوسرے شوہر کے ذمہ جو مہر تھا اس کا ادا کرنا واجب رہے گا یا نہیں۔
ہ) اگر زوج ثانی سے اولاد ہو چکی ہو یا تفریق کے بعد زمانہ عدت میں ہو جاوے تو اس اولاد کا نسب کسی سے ثابت ہوگا پہلے خاوند سے یا دوسرے سے۔
الجواب :- وہ مفقود جس پر مرافعہ اور تفتیش کے بعد چار سال تک انتظار کر کے قاضی نے موت کا حکم کر دیا ہے اگر حکم بالموت کے بعد واپس آجائے تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ شوہر ثانی کے ساتھ خلوت صحیحہ ہونے سے پہلے آجائے خواہ ماہ وفات کے اندر یا بعد، اور خواہ نکاح ثانی سے پہلے یا بعد۔ دوسری یہ کہ ایسے وقت واپس آجائے جب کہ عدت وفات گزارنے کے بعد عورت دوسرے مرد سے نکاح کر چکی اور خلوت صحیحہ بھی ہو چکی ہو۔ ان میں سے پہلی صورت کا حکم بالانفا یہ ہے کہ زوجہ شوہر اول ہی کے نکاح میں بدستور سابق رہے گی دوسرے خاوند کے پاس نہیں رہ سکتی ۔ اور دوسری صورت میں مالکیہ کا تو مشہور مذہب یہی ہے کہ زوجہ دوسرے خاوند کے پاس رہے گی شوہر اول کا اب اس سے کوئی تعلق نہیں رہا لیکن امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ علیہ الرحمة کا مذہب اس بارے میں یہ ہے کہ اگر مفقود حکم بالموت کے بعد بھی واپس آجائے تو اس کی عورت ہر حال میں اسی کو ملے گی۔ خواہ عدت وفات کے اندر آجائے یا بعد انقضائے عدت اور خواہ نکاح ثانی اور خلوت و صحبت کے بعد آئے یا پہلے، اور حنفی کے لیے غیر حنفیہ کے مذہب پر فتوی دینا سخت ضرورت کے وقت جائز ہے جیسے تخلیص زوجہ مفقود وغیرہ کی صورتیں لیکن واپسی مفقود کی صورت میں دوسرے مذہب پر عمل کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں، لہذا صورت ثانیہ میں بھی یعنی جب کہ واپسی مفقود سے قبل شوہر ثانی خلوت صحیحہ بھی کر چکا ہو تب بھی عورت اپنے پہلے ہی شوہر کے نکاح میں رہے گی دوسرے شوہر کے پاس رہنا جائز نہیں ۔ کیوں کہ دوسرے شوہر کی واپسی سے دوسرا نکاح باطل قرار دیا گیا۔
واللہ اعلم
مذکورہ بالا سوال کے پانچ اجزاء کا جواب بالترتیب مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔
ا پہلا نکاح قائم رہے گا۔ دوبارہ نکاح کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں اگر چہ دوسرے شوہر سے ہمبستری بھی ہو چکی ہو۔
جب دوبارہ نکاح پڑھائے جانے کی ضرورت نہیں تو اب دوبارہ مہر مقرر کی ضرورت کہاں ؟
ھ دوسرے شوہر کی عدت گزارنا واجب ہے جب تک عدت ختم نہ ہو اس وقت تک پہلے شوہر کو اس عورت کے پاس جانا یا ہمبستری کرنا جائز نہیں بلکہ مکمل احتیاط لازم ہے اور عدت کے بارے میں جو تفصیل دوسرے مواقع میں ہے وہ یہاں بھی ہوگی یعنی اگر عورت حاملہ ہے تو بچہ پیدا ہونا ورنہ تین حیض
(c) In this situation, is the iddah of the second husband also obligatory or not? And if obligatory, how many days? And should this iddah be spent at the house of the second husband or the first? (d) Is the payment of the mahr that was due from the second husband still obligatory or not? (e) If offspring had been born from the second husband, or occurs during the iddah after separation, from whom is the lineage of that child established—from the first husband or the second? Answer: That missing person (mafqud) regarding whom after litigation and investigation, and after waiting for four years, the judge has passed a ruling of death—if he returns after the ruling of death, then there are two scenarios. First: that he returns before valid seclusion with the second husband, whether within the month of death or after, and whether before the second marriage or after. Second: that he returns at a time when after finishing the death-iddah the woman has married another man and valid seclusion has also occurred. Among these, the ruling of the first scenario in summary is that the wife remains in the marriage of the first husband as before; she cannot stay with the second husband. And in the second scenario, the famous maliki school is that the wife stays with the second husband; the first husband has no connection with her anymore. But the school of Imam Abu Hanifa, may mercy be upon him, regarding this matter is that if the missing person returns even after the ruling of death, his wife will go to him in all circumstances—whether he returns within the death-iddah or after its expiration, and whether after the second marriage and seclusion or before. And for a Hanafi, issuing a fatwa according to a non-Hanafi school is permissible at times of extreme necessity, like cases of extricating the wife of a missing person. But in the case of the missing person's return, there is no need to act upon another school. Therefore, even in the second scenario—that is, when before the missing person's return the second husband has already performed valid seclusion—the wife still remains in the marriage of her first husband; it is not permissible for her to stay with the second husband, because his return renders the second marriage void. And Allah knows best. The answer to the five parts of the above question in order is as follows: (1) The first marriage remains intact; there is no need to renew the marriage, even if intercourse with the second husband has occurred. (2) When there is no need to perform a new marriage, then where is the need to fix a new mahr? (3) It is obligatory to observe the iddah of the second husband; as long as the iddah is not completed, it is not permissible for the first husband to go to this woman or have intercourse with her; rather, complete caution is necessary. And the details regarding iddah that apply in other cases will also apply here—that is, if the woman is pregnant, until childbirth; otherwise, three menstruations.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah presents a detailed fatwa on the case of a missing husband (mafqud) who is declared dead by a judge after a four-year wait and then returns. It addresses five sub-questions covering the status of the marriage, mahr, iddah, and lineage. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, outlines two scenarios: (1) the missing husband returns before the second husband has had valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah), and (2) after valid seclusion has occurred. The Maliki position is mentioned—that in the second scenario the wife stays with the second husband—but the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that regardless of when the missing husband returns, his marriage remains valid and the wife belongs to him. The second marriage is rendered void. The passage also discusses that following another madhhab is only permissible in extreme necessity, but here no such necessity exists. The final section gives the summarized answers: (a) the first marriage remains, (b) no new mahr, (c) the iddah of the second husband must be observed before the first husband can resume relations, with details depending on pregnancy or menstruation.

Key Terms
مفقود الخبر (mafqud al-khabar): A person whose whereabouts are unknown and from whom no news has been received; in this context, a missing husband declared dead by a judge after four years.
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwah sahihah): Valid seclusion between a husband and wife in a place where intercourse is possible, which entails the same legal effects as actual intercourse (e.g., confirming the marriage and obligating mahr).
حکم بالموت (hukm bil-mawt): The judge's ruling declaring a missing person dead, based on evidence and the passage of time (four years in the absence of news).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a missing husband returns after the judge's death declaration and after his wife has remarried and consummated, what is the status of the first marriage?
A) The first marriage is dissolved; the wife stays with the second husband.
B) The first marriage remains valid; the wife returns to the first husband; the second marriage is void.
C) The first marriage is dissolved only if the second husband had valid seclusion.
D) The wife may choose which husband to stay with.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling protects the original marriage of a missing husband despite a judicial death declaration, voiding any subsequent marriage upon his return.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Ruling on the Return of a Missing Husband (Mafqud al-Khabar)
Explains the Hanafi ruling on the return of a missing husband and the five consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the return of a missing husband and apply the five sub-rulings regarding marriage, dower, 'iddah, and lineage.

Core Idea
A missing husband's return revives the original marriage; the second marriage becomes void automatically.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a missing husband (mafqud al-khabar) who returns after being declared dead. The passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah clarifies that the first marriage persists, and outlines the practical consequences for the wife, the second husband, and any children. Understanding these sub-rulings is crucial for muftis handling such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core Hanafi principle
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the original marriage is not truly dissolved by the judge's declaration of death. It is suspended. If the husband returns alive, the marriage is revived ab initio.
This differs from other madhhabs that treat the declaration as final.
2
Apply the first sub-ruling: no re-nikah
Since the first marriage is revived, a new nikah is not required, even if the wife had consummated the second marriage.
The second marriage is automatically void.
3
Apply the second sub-ruling: no new dower
No additional mahr is due from the first husband because the original mahr already covers the revived marriage. Any mahr from the second husband if khalwat sahiha occurred is still due.
The passage states 'when there is no need to perform marriage again, then where is the need to fix a new dower?'
4
Apply the third sub-ruling: 'iddah from second husband
The wife must observe an 'iddah from the second husband (if consummated) before returning to the first. During this period, the first husband cannot have intercourse.
The 'iddah is three menstruations or until childbirth if pregnant. The 'iddah is spent at the first husband's house.
5
Apply the fourth and fifth sub-rulings: mahr and lineage
If valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) occurred with the second husband, the full mahr is due to the wife. Any child born from the second husband is attributed to him (nasab).
The passage implies that if no khalwat, no mahr is due from the second husband, but it is not explicit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پاس رہے گی۔ شوہر کا اب اس سے کوئی تعلق نہیں رہا۔ لیکن امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ رحمہ اللہ کا مذہب اس بارے میں یہ ہے کہ اگر مفقود حکم بالموت کے بعد بھی واپس آجائے تو اس کی عورت ہر حال میں اسی کو ملے گی، خواہ عدت وفات کے اندر آجائے یا بعد انقضائے عدت، اور خواہ نکاح ثانی اور خلوت و صحبت کے بعد آئے یا پہلے۔ اور حنفی کے لیے غیر حنفیہ کے مذہب پر فتویٰ دینا سخت ضرورت کے وقت جائز ہے جیسے تزویج زوجہ مفقود وغیرہ کی صورتیں۔ لیکن واپسی مفقود کی صورت میں دوسرے مذہب پر عمل کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں، لہٰذا صورت ثانیہ میں بھی یعنی جب کہ واپسی مفقود سے قبل شوہر ثانی خلوت صحیحہ بھی کر چکا ہو، تب بھی عورت اپنے پہلے ہی شوہر کے نکاح میں رہے گی، دوسرے شوہر کے پاس رہنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ دوسرے شوہر کی [؟] سے دوسرا نکاح باطل قرار دیا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم۔

مذکورہ بالا سوال کے مفقود الخبر کا سابقہ نکاح باقی رہے گا، اس کی تفصیل جواب بالترتیب مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔
کے پانچ اجزاء کا:
۱: پہلا نکاح قائم رہے گا۔ دوبارہ نکاح کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں اگرچہ دوسرے شوہر سے ہمبستری بھی ہو چکی ہو۔
۲: جب دوبارہ نکاح پڑھائے جانے کی ضرورت نہیں تو اب دوبارہ مہر مقرر کرنے کی ضرورت کہاں؟
۳: دوسرے شوہر کی عدت گزارنا واجب ہے۔ جب تک عدت ختم نہ ہو، اس وقت تک پہلے شوہر کو اس عورت کے پاس جانا اور ہمبستری کرنا جائز نہیں، بلکہ مکمل احتیاط لازم ہے۔ اور عدت کے بارے میں جو تفصیل دوسرے مواقع میں ہے وہ یہاں بھی ہوگی، یعنی اگر عورت حاملہ ہے تو بچہ پیدا ہونے تک، ورنہ تین حیض۔ باقی یہ بات کہ عورت عدت کس جگہ گزارے، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عورت عدت پہلے شوہر کے یہاں گزارے۔
۴: اگر خلوت صحیحہ ہو چکی ہے تو پورا مہر جو بوقت نکاح مقرر کیا گیا تھا ادا کرنا واجب ہوگا، اور اگر خلوت صحیحہ نہ ہوئی تو اس مدت میں مہر کا حکم صراحتہ نظر سے نہیں ہے کہ اس صورت میں مہر بالکل نہیں ملے گا، لیکن قواعد سے معلوم [؟]۔
۵: اس اولاد کا نسب دوسرے شوہر سے ثابت ہوگا۔

مفقود کی سخت ترین ضرورت میں زوجہ مفقود کو ایک سال کی مدت انتظار [؟] کے لیے چار سال مزید انتظار کا حکم تو اسی صورت میں متفقہ طور سے ضروری ہے جب کہ عورت اس قدر زمانہ تک مہر سے اور باعصمت زندگی گزار سکے۔ لیکن اگر یہ صورت ممکن نہ ہو یعنی عورت گناہ میں مبتلا ہونے کا اندیشہ ظاہر کرے اور اس نے ایک عرصہ دراز تک مفقود کا انتظار کرنے کے بعد مجبور ہو کر اس حالت میں درخواست دی ہو، جب کہ مہر سے عاجز ہوگئی ہو، تو اسی صورت میں اس کی بھی گنجائش ہے کہ مذہب مالکیہ کے موافق چار سال کی میعاد میں تفریق کردی جائے، کیونکہ جب عورت کے گناہ میں مبتلا ہونے کا شدید اندیشہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک کم از کم ایک سال صبر و انتظار کے بعد تفریق جائز ہے۔ ایک سال غائب ہونے کے وقت سے لگے گا یا دعویٰ کرنے کے وقت سے؟ قدیم نسخہ کے حاشیہ کے مضمون: عرصہ دراز کی تبیین حاکم کے رائے پر ہے، یعنی قاضی یا شرعی کونسل مدعیہ کے خاص حالات میں غور کر کے فیصلہ کریں کہ عورت نے معاملہ پیش کرنے سے پہلے کافی انتظار کیا۔ یہ حاشیہ میں تھا۔
It will remain with her. The husband has no connection with her. But the madhhab of Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding this is that if the missing person returns even after being declared dead, his wife will belong to him in every case, whether he returns within the waiting period of death or after its expiry, and whether after a second marriage and seclusion and intercourse or before. And for a Hanafi, giving a fatwa according to the madhhab of non-Hanafis is permissible in severe necessity, like the marriage of the wife of a missing person and similar situations. But in the case of the return of the missing person, there is no need to act on another madhhab. Therefore, in the second scenario - that is, when the second husband had already performed valid seclusion before the return of the missing person - the woman will still remain in the marriage of her first husband; staying with the second husband is not permissible, because the second marriage was declared void due to the [return?] of the second husband. And Allah knows best.

The previous marriage of the missing person mentioned in the above question will remain; its details are as follows in the answer, consisting of five parts:
1: The first marriage will remain. There is no need to perform marriage again, even if intercourse with the second husband has occurred.
2: When there is no need to perform marriage again, then where is the need to fix a new dower?
3: It is obligatory to observe the waiting period ('iddah) from the second husband. As long as the 'iddah is not completed, it is not permissible for the first husband to go to this woman and have intercourse; rather, complete caution is necessary. And the details that exist in other places regarding the 'iddah will also apply here: if the woman is pregnant, until childbirth; otherwise, three menstruations. As for where the woman should observe the 'iddah, the answer is that the woman should observe the 'iddah at the first husband's house.
4: If valid seclusion has occurred, then it is obligatory to pay the full dower that was fixed at the time of marriage; and if valid seclusion did not occur, then the ruling of the dower in that period is not explicitly seen: that in this case the dower will not be received at all, but it is known from the rules [missing].
5: The lineage of this child will be established from the second husband.

In severe necessity of the missing person, the ruling that the wife of the missing person must wait one year and then four more years is necessary by consensus only when the woman can live a chaste life without a husband during that long period. But if this scenario is not possible - that is, the woman fears falling into sin and after waiting for a long period for the missing person, being compelled, she applies in that state when she has become unable to bear the [wait?] - then in that case there is also scope that separation be effected according to the Maliki madhhab within a four-year term, because when there is severe fear of the woman falling into sin, according to them, separation is permissible after at least one year of patience and waiting. Does the one year count from the time of disappearance or from the time of claim? The content of the marginal note in the old edition: The explanation of 'long period' is left to the judge's opinion, meaning the judge or Islamic council will consider the specific circumstances of the plaintiff and decide whether the woman waited sufficiently before presenting the case. This was in the margin.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah deals with the complex case of a missing husband (mafqud al-khabar) and provides the Hanafi ruling along with practical guidance for the mufti. The passage opens by stating the Hanafi position: if a missing husband who was declared dead by a judge later returns, the wife remains his wife regardless of any intervening events, including a second marriage and consummation. This is based on the principle that the first marriage was never truly dissolved under Hanafi law; the declaration of death only allowed the woman to remarry by necessity, but if the husband is alive, the original bond persists. The text then notes that while a Hanafi mufti may follow a non-Hanafi madhhab in dire necessity (e.g., to allow remarriage of the missing wife), in the scenario of the husband's return there is no need for such departure because the Hanafi ruling itself resolves the matter. The passage then enumerates five sub-rulings: (1) the first marriage remains, no re-nikah needed; (2) no new mahr is required; (3) the wife must observe ‘iddah from the second husband, during which the first husband cannot have intercourse; (4) if valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) occurred with the second husband, full mahr is due; otherwise, the mahr falls (the text says 'from the rules it is known' but leaves the result implied); (5) any child born from the second husband is attributed to him (nasab). Finally, the passage addresses the extreme case where the woman cannot wait the full Hanafi period (which is indefinite after the four-year search period) and permits following the Maliki view that after one year of waiting (from disappearance or from claim? The judge decides) the marriage can be dissolved after four years total. This is a practical application of the legal maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease), allowing the mufti to choose a different madhhab in genuine necessity to prevent the woman from falling into sin.

Key Terms
مفقود الخبر (mafqud al-khabar): A husband whose location and condition (alive or dead) are unknown.
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwat sahiha): Valid seclusion between a husband and wife with no legal impediment to intercourse.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after dissolution of marriage or death of husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a missing husband (mafqud al-khabar) who was declared dead returns after his wife has remarried and consummated the second marriage, what is the status of the first marriage?
A) The first marriage is automatically dissolved upon the declaration of death.
B) The first marriage is revived, and the wife must return to the first husband after observing 'iddah from the second.
C) The wife may choose between the two husbands.
D) The first marriage is void, and the second marriage remains valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling gives absolute primacy to the original marriage; the wife must return to the first husband regardless of intervening events.

Using Another Madhhab in Necessity: The Missing Husband's Wife
Explains the permissibility of following the Maliki madhhab in severe necessity for the missing husband's wife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir to justify following another madhhab in severe necessity, and identify the conditions for doing so in the case of a missing husband's wife.

Core Idea
When hardship threatens chastity, the mufti may leave the Hanafi position and follow the Maliki view for separation after one year.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah, which addresses the situation where the wife of a missing husband cannot remain chaste during the long wait required by the Hanafi madhhab. The author permits following the Maliki madhhab to effect a separation after a minimum of one year of waiting, applying the maxim 'hardship brings ease.' Understanding when and how to apply this exception is vital for the mufti dealing with genuine cases of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of hardship
The woman cannot live a chaste life (ba'ismat) for the extended period; she fears falling into sin.
This is the trigger for the exception.
2
Recall the maxim: hardship brings ease
The qa'ida al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir allows departing from the standard ruling when hardship is extreme.
This is a major maxim of fiqh.
3
Apply the Maliki alternative
According to the Maliki madhhab, if a husband is missing, the judge may dissolve the marriage after a minimum of one year of waiting (from the time of disappearance or claim? The judge decides). Here, the text mentions a four-year term, but the Maliki position allows dissolution after one year with some differences.
The text says 'after one year of patience and waiting, separation is permissible.' The 'four-year' seems a typo or means the Hanafi period; the author says to effect separation according to Maliki within a four-year term. This likely means the judge can dissolve after one year, but the total period from disappearance should not exceed four years.
4
Check the istithna: when no hardship exists
If the woman can be patient and remain chaste, the exception does not apply; the Hanafi ruling stands.
The maxim 'certainty not removed by doubt' applies.
5
Role of the judge
The judge determines whether the woman's waiting period was sufficient based on her circumstances. The one-year period may be counted from the time of disappearance or from the time she submits the claim; the marginal note leaves it to the judge's discretion.
This gives flexibility to the courts.

مذکورہ بالا سوال کے مفقود الخبر کا سابقہ نکاح باقی رہے گا، اس کی تفصیل جواب بالترتیب مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔
کے پانچ اجزاء کا:
۱: پہلا نکاح قائم رہے گا۔ دوبارہ نکاح کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں اگرچہ دوسرے شوہر سے ہمبستری بھی ہو چکی ہو۔
۲: جب دوبارہ نکاح پڑھائے جانے کی ضرورت نہیں تو اب دوبارہ مہر مقرر کرنے کی ضرورت کہاں؟
۳: دوسرے شوہر کی عدت گزارنا واجب ہے۔ جب تک عدت ختم نہ ہو، اس وقت تک پہلے شوہر کو اس عورت کے پاس جانا اور ہمبستری کرنا جائز نہیں، بلکہ مکمل احتیاط لازم ہے۔ اور عدت کے بارے میں جو تفصیل دوسرے مواقع میں ہے وہ یہاں بھی ہوگی، یعنی اگر عورت حاملہ ہے تو بچہ پیدا ہونے تک، ورنہ تین حیض۔ باقی یہ بات کہ عورت عدت کس جگہ گزارے، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عورت عدت پہلے شوہر کے یہاں گزارے۔
۴: اگر خلوت صحیحہ ہو چکی ہے تو پورا مہر جو بوقت نکاح مقرر کیا گیا تھا ادا کرنا واجب ہوگا، اور اگر خلوت صحیحہ نہ ہوئی تو اس مدت میں مہر کا حکم صراحتہ نظر سے نہیں ہے کہ اس صورت میں مہر بالکل نہیں ملے گا، لیکن قواعد سے معلوم [؟]۔
۵: اس اولاد کا نسب دوسرے شوہر سے ثابت ہوگا۔

مفقود کی سخت ترین ضرورت میں زوجہ مفقود کو ایک سال کی مدت انتظار [؟] کے لیے چار سال مزید انتظار کا حکم تو اسی صورت میں متفقہ طور سے ضروری ہے جب کہ عورت اس قدر زمانہ تک مہر سے اور باعصمت زندگی گزار سکے۔ لیکن اگر یہ صورت ممکن نہ ہو یعنی عورت گناہ میں مبتلا ہونے کا اندیشہ ظاہر کرے اور اس نے ایک عرصہ دراز تک مفقود کا انتظار کرنے کے بعد مجبور ہو کر اس حالت میں درخواست دی ہو، جب کہ مہر سے عاجز ہوگئی ہو، تو اسی صورت میں اس کی بھی گنجائش ہے کہ مذہب مالکیہ کے موافق چار سال کی میعاد میں تفریق کردی جائے، کیونکہ جب عورت کے گناہ میں مبتلا ہونے کا شدید اندیشہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک کم از کم ایک سال صبر و انتظار کے بعد تفریق جائز ہے۔ ایک سال غائب ہونے کے وقت سے لگے گا یا دعویٰ کرنے کے وقت سے؟ قدیم نسخہ کے حاشیہ کے مضمون: عرصہ دراز کی تبیین حاکم کے رائے پر ہے، یعنی قاضی یا شرعی کونسل مدعیہ کے خاص حالات میں غور کر کے فیصلہ کریں کہ عورت نے معاملہ پیش کرنے سے پہلے کافی انتظار کیا۔ یہ حاشیہ میں تھا۔
It will remain with her. The husband has no connection with her. But the madhhab of Imam A'zam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding this is that if the missing person returns even after being declared dead, his wife will belong to him in every case, whether he returns within the waiting period of death or after its expiry, and whether after a second marriage and seclusion and intercourse or before. And for a Hanafi, giving a fatwa according to the madhhab of non-Hanafis is permissible in severe necessity, like the marriage of the wife of a missing person and similar situations. But in the case of the return of the missing person, there is no need to act on another madhhab. Therefore, in the second scenario - that is, when the second husband had already performed valid seclusion before the return of the missing person - the woman will still remain in the marriage of her first husband; staying with the second husband is not permissible, because the second marriage was declared void due to the [return?] of the second husband. And Allah knows best.

The previous marriage of the missing person mentioned in the above question will remain; its details are as follows in the answer, consisting of five parts:
1: The first marriage will remain. There is no need to perform marriage again, even if intercourse with the second husband has occurred.
2: When there is no need to perform marriage again, then where is the need to fix a new dower?
3: It is obligatory to observe the waiting period ('iddah) from the second husband. As long as the 'iddah is not completed, it is not permissible for the first husband to go to this woman and have intercourse; rather, complete caution is necessary. As for where the woman should observe the 'iddah, the answer is that the woman should observe the 'iddah at the first husband's house.

Procedure for Judicial Separation Due to Non-Maintenance
Legal procedure for tafriq when husband refuses nafaqah despite ability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the procedural steps for a woman to obtain tafriq when her husband refuses nafaqah, and apply the Maliki-based ruling that treats the separation as revocable during iddah.

Core Idea
A qadi can grant tafriq when a husband refuses maintenance; if he reforms during iddah, the separation is revocable.

This passage from al-Hilat al-Najiyah addresses a dire situation: a husband who refuses to provide maintenance despite having the means. The author outlines a legal procedure for the wife to petition the qadi, who may effect a separation (tafriq) after warning the husband. A key nuance is that the separation may be treated as revocable (talaq raj'i) if the husband reforms during the iddah, based on Maliki practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grounds for tafriq
Read the passage to list the two hardship conditions that justify seeking tafriq: (1) wife has no means of support, (2) wife can manage but fears sin by staying.
These are the entrance requirements for the hila.
2
Outline the judicial process
Trace the procedural steps: wife presents case to qadi/sultan/committee, shari'ah testimony verification, warning to husband, and if he refuses, qadi pronounces tafriq.
No waiting period is required, by agreement of schools.
3
Understand the post-tafriq scenarios
Note the outcome if husband reforms after iddah: he loses all authority and they may remarry by consent. If he reforms during iddah, two views exist.
The adopted view treats it as revocable.
4
Analyze the Maliki influence
Recognize that standard Hanafi fiqh does not allow tafriq for non-maintenance; this is a Maliki-based hila adopted by the author for necessity.
Author follows 'Allamah Salih of the Maliki school.
5
Note the cautious recommendation
Although the fatwa allows return without wife's consent, the author suggests it is better to renew the marriage contract.
This shows prudence in applying the hila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نان و نفقہ کا انتظام نہ ہو سکے اور باعصمت زندگی نہ گذارنے کا حکم
سخت مجبوری کی وہ صورت ہیں ایک یہ کہ عورت کے نان و نفقہ کا کوئی انتظام نہ ہو سکے بھی نہ تو کوئی شخص بیوی کے نان و نفقہ کا انتظام کرتا ہو اور نہ عورت ، عزت و آبرود کے ساتھ گزارہ کر سکتی ہو اور دوسری صورت مجبوری کی یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ سہولت یا دشواری کے ساتھ خرچ کا انتظام ہو سکتا ہے لیکن شوہر سے علیحدہ رہنے نہیں گناہ میں مبتلا ہونے کا قوی اندیشہ ہو،
تفریق کی صورت یہ ہے
سرکش شخص کی بیوی کے مقدمہ کی کاروائی کا طریقہ کہ عورت اپنا مقدمہ قاضی شرعی یا سلطان حاکم [؟] اور ان کے نہ ہونے کی صورت میں تشریعی کمیٹی کے سامنے پیش کرے اور جس کے پاس پیش ہو وہ معاملہ کی شرعی شہادت کے ذریعہ سے پوری تحقیق کرے اور اگر عورت کا دعوی صحیح ثابت ہو کہ با وجود وسعت کے خرچ نہیں دیتا تو اس کے شوہر سے کہا جائے کہ تم اپنی بیوی کے حقوق ادا کرو یا طلاق دے دو، ورنہ ہم تفریق تم پر واقع کر دیں گے اس کے بعد بھی اگر وہ کسی صورت پر عمل نہ کرے تو قاضی یا جو شرعا اس کے قائم مقام ہو اس کی بیوی پر طلاق واقع کرے اس میں کسی نوع انتظار و جہالت کی باتفاق مذہبیہ [؟] ضرورت نہیں۔
اگر عورت کے حقوق فسخ نکاح کے بعد اگر سرکش شخص اصلاح کرلے یعنی لاپرواہ شخص اپنی حرکت سے اس وقت باز آئے جب کہ حاکم شرعی اُس کی بیوی پر طلاق واقع کر چکے اور عدت بھی گزر چکے ، تو اب اس کا کوئی اختیار بیوی پر نہیں رہتا، کیوں کہ عدت گزرنے کے بعد رجوع کا حق نہیں رہتا ، اگر چہ طلاق ابھی ابھی ہوں جب بھی دونوں فریق کی برضامندی سے دوبارہ نکاح ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر وہ مدت پوری ہونے سے پہلے پہلے اپنی حرکت سے باز آجائے اور نفقہ دینے پر آمادہ ہو جائے تو اس سلسلہ میں مذہب مالکیہ میں واضح روایت نہیں پر اس وجہ سے حضرات مفتیان کرام کے نزدیک احتمال میں ایک یہ کہ اس تفریق کو طلاق رجعی قرار دیا جائے اور عدت کے اندر اندر رجعت کو صحیح کہا جائے۔
دوسرا یہ کہ طلاق بائنہ قرار دی جائے اور رجعت کا ستی شوہر کو نہ دیا جائے لیکن علامہ صالح مذہب مالکی کے مفتی نے پہلے احتمال کو زیادہ قریب لکھا ہے اور ہمیں بھی علامہ صالح کی رائے اُن کے فتویٰ میں غور کرنے کے بعد درست معلوم ہوتی ہے اس وجہ سے ہمارے نزدیک فتوی یہی ہے کہ عدت کے اندر اندر شوہر اپنے تفریط یعنی لاپرواہ ہونے سے باز آنے کی صورت میں عورت کو اسی کے پاس رہنا پڑے گا خواہ عورت راضی ہو یا نہ ہو کیونکہ رجعت میں عورت کی رضامندی ضروری نہیں ، مگر احتیاطاً تجدید نکاح ہو جائے تو بہتر ہے۔
Ruling regarding [when] maintenance cannot be arranged and a chaste life cannot be lived. The situations of severe compulsion are two: one is that no arrangement of maintenance for the woman can be made, neither any person arranges maintenance for the wife nor can the woman live with honor and dignity. And the second situation of compulsion is that even if the expense can be arranged with ease or difficulty, but there is a strong fear of falling into sin by not remaining separate from the husband. The form of separation is: the procedure of the wife's case of a recalcitrant person: that the woman should present her case to a shari'ah judge or a ruler, and in their absence, to a legislative committee. And whoever it is presented to, they should fully investigate the matter through shari'ah testimony. And if the woman's claim is proven true, that despite his capacity he does not give expenses, then it should be said to her husband: 'Fulfill the rights of your wife or divorce her, otherwise we will effect a separation upon you.' After this, if he still does not act on any form, then the judge or whoever is his shari'ah representative should effect a divorce upon his wife. In this, there is no need for any kind of waiting or ignorance, by agreement of the schools. After the annulment of marriage, if the recalcitrant person reforms, i.e., the heedless person refrains from his action at the time when the shari'ah judge has already effected divorce upon his wife and the waiting period has also passed, then now he has no authority over the wife, because after the waiting period passes, the right of return does not remain, even if the divorce just occurred. In both cases, both parties can remarry with mutual consent. And if he refrains from his action before the completion of the period and becomes ready to pay maintenance, then regarding this there is no clear narration in the Maliki school. On this basis, among the honorable muftis there are two probabilities: one is that this separation be considered a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) and that return (ruju') within the waiting period be considered valid. The second is that it be considered an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) and the right of return not be given to the husband. But 'Allamah Salih, the mufti of the Maliki school, has written the first probability as closer, and we also find the view of 'Allamah Salih correct after reflecting on his fatwa. Therefore, according to us, the fatwa is that if the husband refrains from his heedlessness within the waiting period, the woman must remain with him, whether she is willing or not, because the woman's consent is not necessary in return. But cautiously, it is better to renew the marriage.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage presents a hila (legal stratagem) for a woman whose husband obstinately refuses to provide maintenance despite having the means. It outlines two levels of hardship justifying separation: (1) when she has no means of support at all, and (2) even if she could manage but fears sin due to forced separation. The legal procedure requires the woman to approach a qadi, sultan, or in their absence a legislative committee. After verification via shari'ah testimony, the husband is warned to either fulfill rights or divorce; if he refuses, the qadi may effect a divorce without delay. A key issue arises if the husband reforms after the tafriq but before the iddah ends. Citing Maliki fiqh, the author, 'Allamah Ashraf 'Ali Thanwi, follows the view of 'Allamah Salih of the Maliki school, treating the separation as a revocable divorce (raj'i), so the husband can return during the iddah without the wife's consent. The cautious recommendation is to renew the marriage contract. This ruling is a Maliki-based hila adopted by Hanafi muftis for extreme necessity, showing inter-madhhab borrowing.

Key Terms
تفریق (tafriq): The separation effected by the qadi between a couple due to the husband's failure to provide maintenance, constituting a judicial divorce.
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce during the iddah period where the husband may return without a new marriage contract.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or annulment before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can a qadi effect a separation (tafriq) without waiting?
A) After three months of the husband's absence
B) When the husband refuses to provide maintenance despite ability and also refuses divorce
C) Only if the wife agrees to a divorce
D) After a year of marriage

Key Takeaway
Under this Maliki-based hila, a qadi may effect a revocable tafriq for non-maintenance, allowing the husband to return during iddah if he reforms.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

8 min
The Wife of an Absent but Known Husband: Renewal of Nikah as a Hila
Legal hila for wife of absent but known husband

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling for a gha'ib ghayr mafqud situation and construct a fatwa using the Maliki-based hila of tajdid al-nikah.

Core Idea
An absent husband known but neglectful: wife cannot remarry; only hila is renewing the same contract.

When a husband is absent but his whereabouts are known, and he neither returns nor provides maintenance, the wife faces a predicament. The marriage remains valid, so remarriage is forbidden. This lesson examines a Maliki-based legal stratagem (hila) adopted for extreme necessity: renewing the marriage contract (tajdid al-nikah). You will learn the conditions, the ruling, and how to apply this hila in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Recognize the wife's situation: husband absent, location known, no shelter or maintenance. Understand why standard Hanafi rules (waiting for mafqud procedures) do not apply.
The key distinction is 'ghayr mafqud' — the husband is not missing, so a qadi cannot dissolve the marriage.
2
State the General Ruling
The woman cannot marry another because the marriage is still valid. She must stay with the absent husband. Remarriage is haram.
This ruling protects the inviolability of the existing marriage contract.
3
Introduce the Hila (Legal Stratagem)
To relieve the wife's hardship while keeping the marriage lawful, the Maliki-based hila of tajdid al-nikah is permitted. Understand what tajdid al-nikah entails: renewing the marriage contract with the original husband (through representation or consent).
This is an exceptional remedy for severe necessity, not a general rule.
4
Analyze the Conditions and Consequences
Identify the conditions that must exist for the hila to be valid: husband ghayr mafqud, location known, neglect of duties, severe necessity. Also note that if the wife refuses to renew, the husband may keep her without renewal (the original contract remains valid).
The hila is optional for the wife; if she refuses, the marriage status quo persists.
5
Apply in Fatwa Practice
Construct a fatwa for a real scenario: state the case, cite the hila, mention the Maliki borrowing, and give the operative ruling (mufta bihi). Emphasize that this is an exceptional measure under extreme necessity.
Always clarify that this is not the default Hanafi ruling but a solution from Maliki fiqh adopted for necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غائب غیر مفقود کی زوجہ کا حکم
کی بھی فقہ مالک سے لیاگیا ہے تاکہ بوقت ضرورت شدیدہ مظلومہ کو نجات حاصل ہے۔
سوال
(1) جو شخص غائب ہو جاوے اور پتہ اس کا معلوم ہے لیکن نہ وہ خود آتا ہے نہ خرچ بھیجتا ہے تو اس کی بیوی کا کیا حکم ہے؟
جواب
اگر شوہر غائب ہے اور اس کا پتہ معلوم ہے لیکن نہ وہ آتا ہے نہ خرچ بھیجتا ہے تو عورت کو دوسری جگہ نکاح کرنا حرام ہے اور اسی مرد کے پاس رہنا ضروری ہے اس لیے عورت کو بھی لازم ہے کہ تجدید نکاح کرلے۔ لیکن اگر عورت اپنی طرف سے تجدید نکاح نہ کرے تو مرد کو جائز ہے کہ بلا تجدید بھی رکھ لے
Ruling for the wife of an absent husband not missing. This too is taken from Maliki fiqh so that at the time of severe necessity the oppressed woman may obtain relief. Question: (1) What is the ruling for a woman whose husband becomes absent? His whereabouts are known but he neither comes himself nor sends expenses. Answer: If the husband is absent and his location is known, but he neither comes nor sends expenses, then it is forbidden for the woman to marry elsewhere, and she must remain with that husband. Therefore, it is necessary for the woman to renew the marriage contract. But if the woman does not renew the marriage from her side, then it is permissible for the man to keep her even without renewal.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from 'Al-Hilatul Najijah' addresses the situation of a wife whose husband is absent but not missing (gha'ib ghayr mafqud): his location is known, yet he neither returns nor provides maintenance. The author adopts a Maliki-based ruling as a hila (legal stratagem) to relieve the woman's hardship. The ruling states that the wife cannot remarry because the marriage is still valid; remarriage would be forbidden (haram). However, to maintain the marriage lawfully without the husband's presence, the woman should renew the marriage contract (tajdid al-nikah) — presumably with the husband's consent or through a wakil. If she refuses to do so, it is still permissible for the husband to keep her without renewal, meaning the existing marriage continues. This highlights the tension between necessity and legal formality: the wife is stuck, but the hila allows renewal as a remedy. The authority weight is from Maliki fiqh adopted for Hanafi practice under extreme necessity.

Key Terms
غائب غیر مفقود (gha'ib ghayr mafqud): An absent husband whose whereabouts are known and he is not missing (i.e., presumed alive with known location but not fulfilling marital duties).
تجدید نکاح (tajdid al-nikah): Renewal of the marriage contract to ensure its validity when the husband is absent but known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She may marry another man after one year
B) She should renew the marriage contract (tajdid al-nikah)
C) She must immediately seek a divorce from the qadi
D) She can ignore the situation and do nothing

Key Takeaway
For a wife whose absent husband is known but neglectful, remarriage is forbidden; the only hila is to renew the nikah, a Maliki-based remedy for extreme necessity.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

Legal Stratagem (Hila) for the Wife of an Absent Husband
Providing a legal stratagem (hila) for a wife whose husband is absent and neglects maintenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the steps of the hila for a wife of an absent husband and identify whether the qadi's separation is revocable or irrevocable per the adopted position.

Core Idea
When a husband is absent and neglects maintenance, the wife may seek a Maliki-based hila: first khula', then qadi separation treated as revocable divorce.

This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) from the Maliki school, adopted by the Hanafi mufti Ashraf Ali Thanwi for cases of extreme necessity. It addresses the plight of a wife whose husband is absent (location known) and fails to provide maintenance or divorce. The core issue is the nature of the judicial separation: revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in). The author, after evaluating Maliki opinions, adopts the view that it is raj'i, meaning the husband may return during the 'iddah. The hila proceeds stepwise: first attempt khula', then if impossible and hardship unbearable, seek qadi intervention with proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Recognize the scenario: a wife whose husband is absent (gha'ib ghayr mafqud) and who fails to provide maintenance or divorce. The wife is distressed and seeks release from the marriage.
This is not a missing husband (mafqud) case; location is known.
2
Distinguish the two Maliki probabilities
The passage mentions two possible natures for the qadi's separation: revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in). Understand the difference in consequences for the wife's status during 'iddah.
The author follows Allamah Salih's preference for raj'i.
3
Apply the preferred view
Given the raj'i view, the husband can take back the wife during 'iddah without her consent, though cautionary renewal of nikah is advised. This affects the wife's obligation if the husband returns.
If ba'in, a new nikah would be required.
4
Outline the hila steps
List the sequential steps: (1) try to obtain khula' from the husband; (2) if he refuses, bear hardship if possible; (3) if unbearable, go to the qadi, prove the marriage, prove that the husband left without providing maintenance and made no arrangement, then request separation.
Where no qadi exists, the earlier ruling in the text applies.

حضرات مفتیان کرام کے نزدیک احتمال میں ایک یہ کہ اس تفریق کو طلاق رجعی قرار دیا جائے اور عدت کے اندر اندر رجعت کو صحیح کہا جائے۔ دوسرا یہ کہ طلاق بائنہ قرار دی جائے اور رجعت کا ستی تشوہر کو نہ دیا جائے لیکن علامہ صالح مذہب مالکی کے مفتی نے پہلے احتمال کو زیادہ قریب لکھا ہے اور ہمیں بھی علامہ صالح کی رائے اُن کے فتویٰ میں غور کرنے کے بعد درست معلوم ہوتی ہے اس وجہ سے ہمارے نزدیک فتوی یہی ہے کہ عدت کے جان سے تو بہتر ہے۔ غائب غیر مفقود کی زوجہ کا حکم کی بھی فقہ مالک سے لیاگیا ہے تاکہ بوقت ضرورت شدیدہ مظلومہ کو نجات حاصل ہے۔ سوال (1) جو شخص غائب ہو جاوے اور پتہ اس کا معلوم ہے لیکن نہ وہ خود آتا ہے نہ اسی غائب کی زوجیت سے اپنے آپ کو الگ کرلے اور جائز طور پر دوسری جگہ نکاح کر سکے۔ (۲) در صورت جهاز تفریق اگر تفریق کے بعد نکاح ثانی سے پیشتر با نکاح ثانی کے بعد وہ شخص واپس آجائے اور نان نفقہ کا انتظام کرنے پر آمادہ ہوتو کیا زوجہ اس کو مل جائے گی اور اگر واپس مل جاتی ہے تو کن شرائط اور کس تفصیل کے ساتھ ملتی ہے۔ الجواب : (1) اس عورت کی رہائی کے واسطے غائب غیر مفقود کی بیوی کے لیے قومی جو صورت با تفاق المره با صحیح ہے وہ تو یہ ہے کہ اس خادند و خلع پر راضی کیا جائے اور اگر وہ سنگدلی خلع پر بھی راضی نہ ہوتو کو پھر اگر یہ عورت مہر کر کے اپنا زمانہ مفت میں گزار سکے تو بہتر ہے ورنہ جب گذارہ اور نان نفقہ کی کوئی صورت مکن نہ ہو تو سخت مجبوری میں یہ بھی گنجائش ہے کہ مذہب ،مالکیہ کے عراقی صورت ذیل اختیار کر کے رہائی حاصل کر لیے۔ دہ صورت یہ ہے کہ اولا قاضی کے پاس غائب کی بیوری کے مقدمہ کا طریقہ مقدم پیش کرلئے گواہوں سے اس غائب کے ساتھ اپنا نکاح ہونا ثابت کرے پھر یہ ثابت کرے کہ وہ مجھ کو نفقہ دے کر نہیں گیا اور نہ وہاں سے اس نے میرے نان و نفقہ کا کوئی انتظام کیا۔ اور نہ میں نے 20 عنہ اور جہاں قاضی نہ ہو وہاں کا حکم متقدمہ میں مفصل گزر چکا ہے اس کو ضرور دیکھ لیا جاوے
The wife can remarry with the consent of the [first] party. And if before the completion of the period he comes back from his action and becomes ready to give maintenance, then regarding this, in the Maliki school there is no clear narration; therefore, according to the honorable muftis, there are two probabilities: one is that this separation be considered a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) and return (ruju') during the 'iddah be considered valid. The second is that it be considered an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) and the husband not be allowed to return. But Allamah Salih, the mufti of the Maliki school, has written the first probability as closer [to the truth], and we also find Allamah Salih's opinion correct after considering his fatwa; therefore, according to us, the fatwa is that within the 'iddah, if the husband becomes remorseful from his negligence and comes back, the wife must stay with him whether she is willing or not, because in [this matter of] return, the wife's consent is not necessary. However, cautionarily, it is better to renew the marriage. The ruling for the wife of an absent but not lost (gha'ib ghayr mafqud) husband is also taken from Maliki fiqh so that at times of severe necessity the oppressed woman may attain relief. Question (1): A person is absent, his whereabouts are known, but neither does he come himself nor does he [provide?] when the maintenance is established, then it is forbidden for the wife to marry elsewhere and it is necessary for her to stay with that man; therefore, it is necessary for the wife to renew the marriage. But if the wife does not renew the marriage on her own, then it is permissible for the husband to keep her without renewal. 60 He does not call his wife to him, nor does he arrange for her sustenance or anything, nor does he divorce her, therefore the wife is distressed and worried. So is there any way for this woman to separate herself from the marriage of this absent husband and validly marry elsewhere? (2) In the case of separation by the qadi, if before the second marriage or after the second marriage that person returns and becomes ready to arrange maintenance, will the wife return to him, and if she returns, under what conditions and details does she return? Answer: (1) For the relief of this woman, the correct way according to [?] for the wife of an absent but not lost husband is that [the husband] be made agree to khula'; and if he, with stone-heartedness, does not agree to khula', then if this woman can pass her time by [taking] the dower [?], that is better. Otherwise, when there is no possible means of livelihood and maintenance, then in extreme compulsion there is room to adopt the following method from the Maliki school to obtain relief. The method is that first, [she] should present the case of the absent husband's wife to the qadi in the prescribed manner, prove with witnesses her marriage to that absent man, then prove that he left without giving her maintenance and that from there he made no arrangement for her maintenance, and that she [did not receive anything?]. And where there is no qadi, its ruling has already passed in detail in the preceding [section]; it should be consulted.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) from the Maliki school, adopted to resolve the plight of a wife whose husband is absent but not lost (gha'ib ghayr mafqud). The author first discusses the Maliki position on the nature of the separation ordered by the qadi—whether it is revocable (raj'i) or irrevocable (ba'in). Following Allamah Salih's preference, the author adopts the view that it is raj'i, meaning the husband can take her back during 'iddah without her consent, though cautionary renewal of nikah is better. The core hila is then presented: when the husband is absent, does not provide maintenance, and refuses divorce, the wife may seek refuge in the Maliki school's solution. The steps are: (1) attempt to obtain khula' from the husband; (2) if he refuses, she must bear the hardship if possible; (3) if unbearable, she should go to the qadi, prove the marriage, prove that the husband left without providing maintenance and did not arrange for it, and then request a judicial separation. This separation effectively terminates the marriage and allows her to remarry. The passage also addresses the scenario of the husband's return after separation, clarifying that if she hasn't remarried, the separation is considered raj'i and she must return to him, but caution dictates renewing the nikah. This is a practical concession for extreme necessity, not a general ruling.

Key Terms
غائب غیر مفقود (ghā'ib ghayr mafqūd): A husband who is absent but his location is known; not missing.
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
قاضی (qādī): The judge authorized to adjudicate marital disputes and order separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the absent husband returns during the 'iddah and is willing to provide maintenance, what is the wife's obligation?
A) She has the right to refuse and seek a new marriage.
B) She must stay with him, whether she consents or not, because the separation is considered revocable.
C) She may only stay if she consents to a renewal of the nikah.
D) She is free to choose to return or not.

Key Takeaway
For a wife of an absent husband who neglects maintenance, the adopted Maliki hila provides a revocable separation that allows return if the husband reforms, with cautionary renewal of nikah.

Maliki Hila for Wife of Absent Husband
A hila (legal stratagem) using Maliki school to dissolve marriage due to non-maintenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the step-by-step procedure for a hila (legal stratagem) to obtain judicial separation (tafriq) for the wife of an absent husband under the Maliki school, applied under extreme necessity.

Core Idea
In extreme necessity, a Hanafi mufti may adopt the Maliki judicial separation for an absent husband's non-maintenance.

A married woman whose husband is absent and fails to provide maintenance faces a severe dilemma. Hanafi law does not permit tafriq (judicial separation) for non-maintenance by an absent husband; the default remedy is khul'. However, when necessity demands, a mufti can guide the woman through a Maliki procedure that allows the judge to dissolve the marriage. This lesson unpacks the steps of that hila as presented by Mawlana Ashraf Ali Thanawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default Hanafi ruling and the necessity exception
Understand that under normal circumstances, Hanafi law does not allow separation for non-maintenance by an absent husband. The wife must seek khul' or wait. But extreme necessity (idtirar) permits adopting the Maliki view.
This is a talfiq (piecing together) of rulings from different schools under duress.
2
Outline the preconditions for adopting the Maliki hila
The woman must first attempt khul'. If refused, and she cannot sustain herself, then the Maliki procedure becomes permissible.
Khul' is the preferred Hanafi remedy; the Maliki hila is a last resort.
3
Describe the procedural steps before the judge
Present the case, prove the marriage, prove the husband's failure to provide maintenance, and establish that he is negligent. Testimony of witnesses is required.
The burden of proof is on the wife to demonstrate the obligation and its breach.
4
Explain the role of witnesses and proper notice
The judge sends reliable deputies to personally deliver notice to the absent husband, giving him options: come, send maintenance, or divorce. A mere postal letter is insufficient.
The method of personal delivery by trustworthy individuals ensures reliable testimony for the judge's decision.
5
Determine the final outcome and conditions
After a month's wait without compliance, the judge decrees separation. The wife's demand is essential; if she withdraws, separation is not effected.
The husband can still avoid separation by responding within the month.

(۲) در صورت جهاز تفریق اگر تفریق کے بعد نکاح ثانی سے پیشتر با نکاح ثانی کے بعد وہ شخص واپس آجائے اور نان نفقہ کا انتظام کرنے پر آمادہ ہوتو کیا زوجہ اس کو مل جائے گی اور اگر واپس مل جاتی ہے تو کن شرائط اور کس تفصیل کے ساتھ ملتی ہے۔

الجواب :
(1) اس عورت کی رہائی کے واسطے غائب غیر مفقود کی بیوی کے لیے قومی جو صورت با تفاق المره با صحیح ہے وہ تو یہ ہے کہ اس خادند و خلع پر راضی کیا جائے اور اگر وہ سنگدلی خلع پر بھی راضی نہ ہوتو کو پھر اگر یہ عورت مہر کر کے اپنا زمانہ مفت میں گزار سکے تو بہتر ہے ورنہ جب گذارہ اور نان نفقہ کی کوئی صورت مکن نہ ہو تو سخت مجبوری میں یہ بھی گنجائش ہے کہ مذہب ،مالکیہ کے عراقی صورت ذیل اختیار کر کے رہائی حاصل کر لیے۔

دہ صورت یہ ہے کہ اولا قاضی کے پاس غائب کی بیوری کے مقدمہ کا طریقہ مقدم پیش کرلئے گواہوں سے اس غائب کے ساتھ اپنا نکاح ہونا ثابت کرے پھر یہ ثابت کرے کہ وہ مجھ کو نفقہ دے کر نہیں گیا اور نہ وہاں سے اس نے میرے نان و نفقہ کا کوئی انتظام کیا۔ اور نہ میں نے نفقہ معات کیا غرض نان و نفقہ کا وجوب بھی اس کے ذمہ ثابت کرے اور یہ بھی کہ وہ اس واجب میں کوتا ہی کر رہا ہے اور ان باتوں پر جماعت بھی کرے اسی کے بعد اگر کوئی عزیز قریب یا اجنبی اس کے نفقہ کی کفالت کرے تو بہتر ہے ورنہ قاضی انس شخص کے پاس حکم بھیجے کہ یا تم خود حاضر ہو کر اپنی بیوی کے حقوق ادا کر دیا اس کو بالو یا وہاں سے کوئی انتظام کرو ورنہ اس کو طلاق دے دو۔ اگر تم نے ان باتوں میں سے کوئی بات نہ کی تو پھر ہم خود تم دونوں میں تفریق کر دیں گے اس پر بھی اگر شوہم کوئی صورت قبول نہ کرے تو قاضی ایک مہینہ کے مزید انتظار کا حکم دے ، اس بات نہیں بھی اگر اس کی شکایت دور نہ ہوئی تو عورت کو اس غائب کے نکاح سے الگ کمر دے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ تفریق کے لیے عورت کی جانب سے مطالبہ شرط ہے میں اگر غائب کا جواب آنے کے بعد عورت مطالبہ چھوڑ دے تو پھر تفریق نہیں کی جائے گی۔

(2) تنبیه ضروری

غائب کے پاس نوٹس بھیجنے کا طریقہ قامتی جو اس نائب شخص کے پاس حکم انوٹس بھیجے تو بذریعہ ڈاک وغیرہ بھیجا کافی نہیں بلکہ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ حکم نامہ (نوٹس) مستند افراد کو سنا کر ان کے حوالہ کر دے کہ اس کو غائب شخص کے پاس لے جاؤ یہ دونوں شخص غائب کو حکم نامہ پہنچ کر اس سے جواب طلب کریں الیتی جو دعوی ہیں ، اور جو کچھ جواب تحریری با زبانی وہ اسے اس کو اچھی طرح محفوظ رکھیں۔ (بلکہ زبانی جواب کو بھی احتیاطی لکھے ہیں، تاکہ واپس ہو کر اس پر گواہی دے سکیں اگر وہ کچھ جواب نہ دے تو اس کی گواہی دے دیں ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ قاضی جو حکم دے ان دونوں کی گو اپنی فیصلہ پر کرے محض خطہ کو کافی نہ سمجھے۔

غیر اگر نائب شخص کی دور دراز غیر ملک میں جا کر آباد ہو جائے ملک بہ ایسی جگہ ہو کہ ملک
He neither brings his wife to himself nor makes any arrangement for her fridge etc., nor gives her divorce; due to this the woman is distressed and worried. So is there any way for this woman to separate herself from the marriage of this absent husband and marry elsewhere lawfully? (2) In the case of separation, if after separation but before or after a second marriage that person returns and is ready to arrange for food and maintenance, will the wife be reunited with him? And if she is reunited, under what conditions and details? The answer: (1) For the release of this woman, the wife of an absent but not missing husband, the correct method according to consensus of the scholars is to persuade him to khul'. But if he stubbornly refuses khul', then if this woman can spend her time for free by remitting the dower, that is better. Otherwise, when there is no possibility of livelihood and maintenance, in extreme necessity there is also a concession to adopt the following method from the Maliki school to obtain release. That method is: First, present the case of the absent wife to the judge, prove her marriage to the absent husband through witnesses, then prove that he did not leave her maintenance nor made any arrangement from there for her food and maintenance, and she did not receive any maintenance. In short, prove the obligation of maintenance upon him and that he is negligent in this obligation, and also have witnesses testify to these facts. After that, if any relative or stranger guarantees his maintenance, that is better; otherwise, the judge sends a decree to that person: either come yourself and fulfill your wife's rights or take her along, or make some arrangement, or give her divorce. If you do none of these, then we will ourselves decree separation between you. If even then the husband accepts no course, the judge orders a further wait of one month. If even then her complaint is not resolved, then he separates the woman from the marriage of the absent husband. And it is obvious that for separation, the woman's demand is a condition; if after the absent husband's reply the woman abandons her demand, then separation will not be effected. (2) Necessary warning: The method of sending notice to the absent husband — if the judge sends a notice through a deputy, sending it by post etc. is not sufficient. Rather, the method is that the notice be heard by reliable individuals and entrusted to them to take to the absent person. These two persons should deliver the notice to the absent person and ask for his reply regarding the claim. And whatever reply, written or oral, they should preserve it well. (Rather, they should also write down the oral reply carefully so that upon return they can testify to it. If he gives no reply, they should testify to that.) Summary: The judge should base his decision on the testimony of these two, and should not consider a mere letter sufficient. If the deputy person has gone far away, even to a foreign country, to such a place that...
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) from Thanawi's Al-Hilat al-Najizah. It addresses a real-life problem: a woman whose husband is absent (gha'ib) and failing to provide maintenance (nafaqa), yet he is not legally missing (mafqud). Under Hanafi fiqh, a wife cannot unilaterally dissolve the marriage for non-maintenance by an absent husband; the default remedy is khul' (divorce by compensation) or patience. However, when the woman is in extreme distress and cannot support herself, the Hanafi scholar allows borrowing the Maliki school's procedure, which permits judicial separation (tafriq) due to non-maintenance even when the husband is absent. The passage provides step-by-step instructions: prove the marriage, prove the husband's failure to provide, have witnesses testify, then send a formal notice through reliable deputies to the husband giving him options (come, send maintenance, or divorce). If he fails to respond or comply, the judge can decree separation after a month. A critical practical detail is that the notice must be delivered by trustworthy individuals, not just by mail, to ensure proper evidence for the judge's decision. This hila is an example of 'talfiq' (piecing together rulings from different schools) under the principle of necessity (darurah).

Key Terms
غائب غیر مفقود (gha'ib ghayr mafqud): A husband who is absent but not missing; his whereabouts are known or he is alive.
تفریق (tafriq): Judicial separation between spouses, dissolving the marriage.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife by paying compensation to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first recommended step for the wife of an absent husband who does not provide maintenance?
A) Immediately go to a Maliki judge for separation.
B) Try to obtain khul' from her husband.
C) File a complaint to the police.
D) Wait for ten years.

Key Takeaway
The Maliki hila for tafriq is a valid concession under extreme necessity, but requires strict procedural compliance and should only be used when khul' is impossible.

Procedure for Missing Husband's Nafaqah and Judicial Separation
Procedural rules for missing husband's nafaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the full Hanafi legal procedure (hila) for a missing husband's nafaqah case, including the notice process, conditions for judicial separation, and the rulings when the husband returns.

Core Idea
The Hanafi hila ensures wife's maintenance right while preserving husband's marriage through a structured judicial process.

When a husband is absent (gha'ib) and fails to provide nafaqah, the wife faces hardship. Hanafi fiqh provides a lawful procedure (hila) that balances her right to maintenance with the husband's marital rights. This lesson unpacks the step-by-step process from establishing the claim to the consequences of the husband's return.

Guided Path
1
Establish the wife's claim
Identify the conditions: the wife must prove the husband's obligation of nafaqah and his negligence before witnesses. If someone volunteers to pay, that is preferred; otherwise, the judge proceeds.
The claim must be substantiated by witnesses (shuhud).
2
Send proper notice to the absent husband
The judge sends a decree via two trustworthy individuals who personally deliver it and bring back a response. Postal mail is insufficient. The decree offers options: appear, arrange maintenance, or divorce.
If the husband is inaccessible, an alternative procedure is provided.
3
Handle inaccessible or unresponsive husbands
If the husband cannot be reached despite effort, the judge may decree separation after thorough investigation and a one-month waiting period. The wife's demand is a condition for tafriq.
This is a last resort when no response is possible.
4
Apply post-separation rules upon husband's return
If the husband returns during iddah and resumes nafaqah, he can take back the wife (raj'ah). If after iddah, outcome depends on proof: if he proves he fulfilled nafaqah or the wife refused, marriage revives even if she remarried; otherwise, he loses her.
Iddah and mahr for second husband follow mafqud rules.
