3
دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ عدت ختم ہو جانے کے بعد واپس آیا ہو سوانس میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر اس نے عورت کے دعوے کے خلاف کوئی بات ثابت کردی مثلاً یہ کہ میں نے اس کو پیشگی خرچ دے دیا تھا ، یا یہ کہ وہاں سے بھیجتا رہتا تھا یا یہ کہ عورت نے نفقہ معات کر دیا تھا تب تو اس کو ہر حال میں عورت مل جائے گی یعنی خواہ وہ عورت عزت کے بعد کارت ثانی بھی کر چکی ہو تی کہ اگر شوہر ثانی سے اولاد بھی ہو چکی ہو تب بھی شہر اول ہی کا نکاح باقی سمجھا جاوے گا ۔ اور شوہر ثانی کا نکاح اب باطل قرار دیا جائے گا۔ اور خاوند نے عورت کے دعوے کے خلاف کوئی بات ثابت نہ کی تو عورت اس
کون لے گی کیوں کہ عورت ختم ہونے کے بعد رجعت کا حق نہیں رہتا ۔ اور دوسری صورت کی پہلی شق میں جو شو ہرا قول کو عورت مل جائے گی اس کو نہ تجدید نکاح کی ضرورت نہ تجدید ہر کی البتہ شوہر ثانی سے خلوت صحیحہ ہوچکی ہو تو مدت واجب ہے یعنی عدت گزارنے سے پیشتر شوہر کو جماع اور اس کے دوائی کا ارتکاب جائز نہیں۔ اور شوہر ثانی کے ذمہ مہر واجب ہونے میں وہی تفصیل ہے جو مفقود کے بیان
Nafaqah refusal: the purpose is to establish the obligation of maintenance on him and that he is negligent in this obligation, and to have witnesses for these matters. After that, if some relative or stranger undertakes his nafaqah, it is better; otherwise, the judge sends a decree to him that either you come personally and fulfill your wife's rights or make some arrangement from there, or else divorce her. If you do none of these, then we will separate you. If the husband still does not accept any form, the judge orders a further one month wait. If after that the complaint is not resolved, the woman is separated from the marriage of this absent husband. It is evident that for separation, the woman's demand is a condition; if after the reply from the absent husband the woman drops her demand, then separation is not carried out. 2 Essential Reminder: The method of sending a notice to the absent husband is that the judge sends the decree to the appointed person; sending by post etc. is not sufficient. Rather, the procedure is that the judge should pronounce the decree (notice) before reliable persons and hand it over to them, saying take this to the absent husband. These two persons will deliver the decree to the absent husband and ask him for a reply regarding the claims. Whatever reply, written or oral, they will preserve it carefully. (Rather, write down the oral reply cautiously so that upon return they can give testimony based on it. If he gives no reply, they testify that.) In summary, the judge's verdict based on the testimony of these two persons, not just the letter. If the appointed person is far away, or the absent person has gone and settled in another country in such a place where despite full effort and possible endeavor there is no possibility of sending a person, then in that extreme necessity it is also permissible that without sending a person, the judge or his representative, after proper investigation of the incident, may pass a decree of separation. If this absent husband appears after the decree of separation: There are two scenarios. One is that he returns during the iddah and is ready to give regular maintenance; in this case he has the right to take back his wife; if he does so, it is valid; if he does not take back, the marriage breaks after iddah. Second scenario: he returns after the iddah has ended. In this there is a detail: if he proves something contrary to the woman's claim, e.g., that he had given her advance expenses, or that he used to send money from there, or that the woman refused maintenance, then in that case he will get the woman in any case, even if the woman has married another after iddah, and even if she has had children from the second husband; then the first marriage is considered intact, and the second marriage is declared void. And if the husband does not prove anything contrary to the woman's claim, then the woman will not get him because after the iddah ends the right of raj'ah does not remain. And in the first part of the second scenario, where the husband gets the woman, there is no need for renewal of nikah nor reassignment of mahr; however, if there was valid seclusion with the second husband, then iddah is obligatory, meaning before the iddah expires, the first husband cannot engage in intercourse or its preliminaries. And regarding the obligation of mahr on the second husband, the same detail applies as in the case of mafqud (missing person).
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilat al-Najijah presents the Hanafi legal procedure (hila) for dealing with a missing (gha'ib) husband who fails to provide nafaqah (maintenance). It is a hila because it provides a lawful mechanism to resolve the wife's hardship without falling into forbidden divorce or abandonment. The passage begins by outlining the preliminary steps: the wife must first establish that the husband is legally obligated to provide nafaqah and that he is negligent, with witnesses. If no one volunteers to provide maintenance, the judge sends a notice to the husband through appointed trustworthy persons. Sending by mail is insufficient; the decree must be personally delivered by two reliable men who then bring back the husband's written or oral reply. If the husband is in an inaccessible location, the judge may after thorough investigation decree separation without sending a person. The passage then details the consequences if the husband returns after the tafriq decree. If he returns during the iddah, he may take back his wife (raja'). If he returns after the iddah, the outcome depends on whether he can prove that the wife's claim was false (e.g., that he had given maintenance). If he proves it, he gets his wife back even if she has remarried—the second marriage is void. If he cannot prove it, he has no right to her. The final part discusses the obligation of iddah if there was valid seclusion with the second husband, and the mahr for the second husband follows the same rules as in the case of a mafqud (absolutely missing) person. This entire procedure reflects the Hanafi school's care in balancing the wife's right to maintenance and the husband's right to marriage, using legal stratagems to prevent harm.

Key Terms
غائب (ghā'ib): A husband who is absent and whose whereabouts are unknown, but he is still considered alive; not a mafqud (missing presumed dead) but simply absent.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance (food, clothing, shelter) that a husband must provide to his wife.
تفریق (tafrīq): Judicial separation (dissolution of marriage) ordered by a qadi due to the husband's failure to provide nafaqah while absent.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period after tafriq or divorce during which the woman cannot remarry.
رجعت (raj'ah): The right of the husband to take back his wife without a new marriage contract during the iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct method for sending a notice (decree) to an absent husband regarding nafaqah?
A) Sending it through the postal service (mail).
B) Having the judge personally deliver it.
C) Entrusting two reliable persons to deliver it and bring back a response.
D) Publishing it in a newspaper.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hila for a missing husband's nafaqah requires a strict notice procedure and careful post-separation rules to balance the wife's right to maintenance with the husband's marital rights.

Committee-Based Faskh: Three Additional Cases
Transition and introduction to three additional faskh cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three additional faskh situations and state the committee requirement for dissolution in the absence of a qadi.

Core Idea
When no qadi exists, a committee of three just Muslims may dissolve a marriage.

This passage introduces the summary of al-Mukhtarat, focusing on three additional grounds for judicial dissolution of marriage (faskh) beyond the five previously discussed. It provides a crucial practical solution: when a qualified qadi is absent, a committee of at least three just and trustworthy Muslims can perform the faskh. The conditions for this committee are previously detailed in Part Two of Hila Najiza.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage context
Note that this passage transitions from summarizing Hila Najiza to summarizing al-Mukhtarat, which contains selected rulings on divorce and options (khiyarat). Recognize that the author is supplementing five earlier faskh cases with three more common scenarios.
The five earlier cases are assumed to be from the previous section.
2
List the three additional faskh situations
Although the OCR garbles the list, from context and known Hanafi fiqh, the three cases likely involve: (1) prohibition through marriage relationships (musahara), (2) the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) for a minor married by someone other than father or grandfather, and (3) lack of equality (kafaa'ah) in marriage. Learn these as the three new grounds.
For a complete list, consult reliable sources like al-Hidayah or contemporary fatawa.
3
Understand the committee as an alternative
The passage states that where no qadi exists, nor any Muslim ruler who acts according to Shariah, a committee of at least three just (adil) and trustworthy (mu'tabar) people can perform faskh. This is a practical concession (rukhsah) for Muslims living under non-Islamic rule.
The committee's conditions are detailed in Part Two of Hila Najiza; students should review that section.
4
Apply the ruling in a contemporary context
For Muslims in non-Muslim countries without access to a Shariah court, this committee mechanism provides a valid way to dissolve a marriage on recognized grounds. The committee acts as a substitute qadi (qadi badil).
Ensure the committee meets the conditions: at least three, just, and knowledgeable enough to make a proper judgment.

Annulment by Committee and Prohibition by Affinity: A Hila Case
Summarizing conditions for faskh via committee and detailing hurmah musaharat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct the conditions under which a Sharia committee can annul a marriage and identify the acts that establish prohibition by affinity (hurmah musaharat).

Core Idea
When no qadi is available, a committee of three just Muslims can annul; certain acts with desire create permanent affinity prohibitions even if unintentional.

This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah offers a practical solution for Muslims without access to a Sharia court. It outlines three scenarios where marriage annulment is needed, then details the first: prohibition by affinity. The author stresses that even mistaken acts with desire trigger these prohibitions, demanding extreme caution in interactions with in-laws.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for committee annulment
Locate the condition that permits a committee to annul a marriage: absence of a qadi or of a Muslim ruler who judges according to Sharia.
The committee must consist of at least three just, reliable Muslims.
2
List the acts that establish hurmah musaharat
From the passage, extract the specific acts that create prohibition by affinity: fornication, touching with desire, kissing with desire, looking at the inner private parts with desire.
Desire (shahwah) is the key element.
3
Recognize that intention is not required
The passage explicitly states that these acts trigger prohibition even if done by mistake, e.g., touching the mother-in-law thinking she is the wife.
This is a unique Hanafi position; other schools may require intent.
4
Apply the prohibition to relatives
The prohibition extends to the woman’s mother and daughters (ascendants/descendants) and similarly for the man; milk relations are also included.
This creates a permanent bar to marriage with those relatives.

Summary of Al-Mukhtarat regarding important matters of annulment and options. After praise and blessings, it is submitted that besides the mentioned five issues, there are three more situations where the need for annulment of marriage frequently arises, and due to the absence of a qadi, difficulty is faced. Therefore, in these situations as well, there is a concession that where there is no qadi and no Muslim ruler holds authority from the government, or despite having authority, does not decide according to Sharia law, then the marriage may be annulled by presenting the matter to a committee of at least three just and reliable persons. Prohibition by Affinity: If a person commits fornication with a woman, or touches her with desire only, or kisses her with desire, or looks at the inner part of the private parts with desire, then in all these cases prohibition by affinity is established. That is, for that man, the woman's daughter, and [?] all ascending relatives and all descending relatives by lineage and [?] relationships become permanently prohibited. Similarly, if a woman touches a man with desire, or kisses him with desire, or looks at the man's specific organ with desire, then also the relationship of affinity is established and prohibition [?]. All ascending and descending relatives by lineage and milk-relations become permanently prohibited for that man and that woman. For prohibition by affinity, it is not a condition that these actions be done intentionally; rather, even if such an act occurs by mistake, for example, thinking she is the wife, he touches the mother-in-law with a desirous look, then even then the wife becomes prohibited. For this reason, it is essential for the husband to be extremely careful with the wife's ascending and descending [?] relatives, and for the woman to be extremely careful with the man's ascending and descending relatives (i.e., male relatives), because touching them with desire, etc., besides being a severe sin, is a great harm that [?] the connection of prohibition by affinity occurs, i.e., if the husband [?] there was a marginal note in the previous edition which on the next page under the heading 'Prohibition by affinity due to a woman having desire' is presented.

It identifies three additional scenarios beyond the five previously mentioned where a marriage can be annulled without a qadi. The text references marginal notes from the original, indicating an earlier version had additional commentary. The second and third scenarios are not included in this OCR excerpt.

فسخ نکاح (faskh al-nikah): Annulment of marriage by a Sharia committee when a qadi is absent or unjust.

Conditions for Prohibition by Touch and Talfiq
Explaining conditions for hurmah musaharah and permissibility of talfiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'إذا لم يجتمع الأمران جاز التلفيق' to determine the permissibility of combining madhhab rulings in a family law case involving hurmah musaharah.

Core Idea
Talfiq is permissible when the two matters are separate and not combined in a prohibited way.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najiyah addresses a practical hila (legal stratagem) in family law: How can one avoid the prohibition of marriage due to physical contact (hurmah musaharah) when the Hanafi ruling would cause hardship? The author outlines the strict conditions for prohibition under Hanafi law and then introduces the option of talfiq — combining rulings from different madhhabs — as a permissible solution, provided certain conditions are met.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for hurmah musaharah
From the text, extract the three conditions for prohibition through touching or kissing: (1) desire on one side, (2) no thick barrier preventing heat sensation, (3) no seminal emission. Note that glancing has an additional condition: desire must be in the one who looks.
These are Hanafi-specific conditions.
2
Understand the concept of talfiq
Recognize that talfiq is combining rulings from different madhhabs in one case. The key rule is: 'If two matters do not combine, talfiq is permissible.'
The 'two matters' here are: (1) considering the religious committee as a qadi, and (2) making hurmah musaharah a cause of separation.
3
Apply the qawida to the hila case
The author argues that these two matters are separate (like wudu and prayer), so adopting the Maliki view that hurmah musaharah is not established in certain cases is permissible. This does not combine contradictory rulings in a prohibited way.
The Maliki view is that touching with desire does not necessarily create prohibition.
4
Identify the practical caution
The author advises that the person acting on this talfiq should consult a trusted scholar to ensure the permissibility of talfiq in his specific situation.
This reflects the principle of ihtiyat (caution) in fatwa.

لمس و تقبیل دمینی چھوتے اور بوسہ لینے کے وقت اگر مرد کو شہوت نہ تھی لیکن عورت کو شہوت ہو گئی، جب بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ اسی طریقہ سے اگر عورت نے (کسی مرد کو) ہاتھ لگایا یا بوسہ لیا جب بھی دونوں میں سے ایک کو شہوت ہونا کافی ہے۔ البتہ نگاہ کے حرمت کا سبب ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ جو دیکھے اسی کو شہوت ہو صرف دوسرے کی جانب سے ہونا حرمت کا سبب نہیں۔ نیز لمس و تقبیل یعنی چھونے اور بوسہ لینے میں ایک شرط یہ بھی ہے کہ اس قسم کا کپڑا حائل نہ ہو جو کہ بدن کی گرمی محسوس ہونے کو روک دے۔ پس اگر کس شخص نے اس قسم کا کپڑا درمیان میں آنے کے باوجود کپڑے کے اوپر سے چھوا، یا بوسہ لیا تو اس قسم کی مصاہرت حرمت کی وجہ نہیں، یعنی اس سے حرمت ثابت نہ ہوگی چاہے عورت کرے یا مرد کرے۔ اس کے علاوہ ایک شرط یہ بھی ہے کہ ان افعال کی وجہ سے انزال نہ ہوا ہو۔ پس اگر چھونا یا بوسہ لینا، یا صرف دیکھنے سے ہی انزال ہو جائے تو حرمت ثابت نہ ہوگی۔

اصل رسالہ کے دیباچہ میں یہ واضح کیا جا چکا ہے کہ جب دو کام جمع نہ ہوں تو تلفیق جائز ہے۔ ہم نے مزید احتیاط کے لیے اصل رسالہ میں کوئی مسئلہ اس قسم کا نہیں لیا کہ جس میں تلفیق اجتماع کے خلاف ہو۔ اور تم گذشتہ صفحات میں مذکور تین مسائل میں سے بھی دو مسائل میں اس کی رعایت موجود ہے لیکن صرف ایک مسئلہ یعنی حرمت مصاہرت میں رشرعی کیٹی) جماعت مسلمین کا فیصلہ معتبر نہیں۔ اور حضرات مالکیہ کے مشہور و مختار مذہب کی درجہ سے بعض خاص صورتوں میں شہرت سے چھونے وغیرہ سے حرمت مصاہرت متعلق نہیں ہوتی۔ لیکن بعض صورتوں میں معتمد قول اور مشہور قول کے موافق اور بعض میں ایک قول پر ان کے مذہب میں بھی اس کا اختیار کیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن ہم ان کو ایک عمل خیال نہیں کرتے، بلکہ جماعت مسلمین (شرعی کمیٹی) کو قاضی کے حکم میں سمجھنا ایک مستقل مسئلہ ہے اور حرمت مصاہرت کو تفریق کا سبب قرار دینا دوسرا مستقل مسئلہ ہے، جس طریقہ سے وضو ایک علیحدہ عمل ہے اور نماز علیحدہ عمل ہے۔ اور اس کی وضاحت اصل رسالہ کے دیباچہ حاشیہ پر کر دی گئی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے تلفیق کی یہ صورت ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ لیکن عمل کے وقت احتیاط یہ ہے کہ عمل کرنے والا تلفیق کے جواز کے بارے میں کسی اپنے معتقد عالم سے رجوع کر کے ان کے قول پر عمل کرے۔

حرمت مصاہرت کی صورت میں فیصلہ کس طرح کیا جائے؟ جب عورت یہ دعوی کرے کہ میرے اور شوہر کے اصول و فروع (یعنی اوپر یا نیچے کے رشتوں میں سے) فلاں مرد کے درمیان یا شوہر اور میرے اصول و فروع (یعنی میرے اوپر یا نیچے کے رشتوں میں سے) فلاں عورت کے درمیان اس قسم کا واقعہ پیش آیا ہے جو کہ حرمت کا سبب ہے۔
When touching and kissing, if the man did not have desire but the woman had desire, the same ruling applies. Similarly, if a woman touched or kissed (a man), it suffices for one of them to have desire. However, for the glance to cause prohibition, it is a condition that the one who looks must have desire; only the other's desire does not cause prohibition. Also, for touching and kissing, one condition is that such a cloth should not be a barrier that prevents the feeling of body heat. So if a person touched or kissed over a cloth of this type despite its presence, then such contact is not a cause of prohibition (musaharah); that is, prohibition is not established whether done by the woman or the man. Additionally, there is a condition that no seminal emission occurs due to these acts. So if emission occurs from touching, kissing, or just looking, prohibition is not established.

In the preface of the original treatise, it has been clarified that when two matters are not combined, talfiq is permissible. For extra caution, we did not include in the original treatise any issue that goes against the conjunction of talfiq. And among the three issues mentioned in the previous pages, this consideration is present in two issues, but only in one issue, namely the prohibition of musaharah, the decision of the (religious committee) congregation of Muslims is not authoritative. And according to the well-known and preferred madhhab of the Malikiyyah, in some specific cases, touching etc. with desire does not entail prohibition of musaharah. But in some cases, in accordance with the relied-upon and well-known opinion, and in some, according to one opinion, in their madhhab as well, this has been adopted. However, we do not consider them one action. Rather, considering the congregation of Muslims (shar'i committee) as a qadi is one independent issue, and making prohibition of musaharah a cause of separation is another independent issue, just as ablution is a separate act and prayer is a separate act. And its clarification has been given in the margin of the preface of the original treatise. For this reason, this form of talfiq is permissible according to us. But at the time of action, the caution is that the person acting should refer to some knowledgeable scholar of his own conviction regarding the permissibility of talfiq and act according to his opinion.

How should a decision be made in the case of prohibition of musaharah? When a woman claims that such an event has occurred between her and her husband's ascendants or descendants (i.e., the higher or lower relatives), or between a certain man, or between the husband and her ascendants or descendants (i.e., her higher or lower relatives) and a certain woman, which is a cause of prohibition.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a legal exposition of a hila (stratagem) case regarding the prohibition of marriage due to physical contact (hurmah musaharah). The author, Asraf Ali Thanwi, first outlines the conditions under which touching or kissing establishes the prohibition. He states that desire (shahwah) on the part of either the man or the woman is sufficient; it is not necessary for both to have desire. However, for glancing (nazar), only the desire of the one who looks counts. Additionally, there must be no thick barrier (like a thick cloth) that prevents the sensation of body heat; if such a barrier exists, the prohibition is not established. Finally, if no seminal emission (inzal) occurs from these acts, the prohibition is not established.

Then the passage discusses talfiq (combining different madhhab rulings) as a stratagem to avoid the prohibition. The author clarifies that talfiq is permissible when the two matters (the act and the ruling) are not combined in a prohibited way. He notes that in the original treatise, issues contrary to talfiq were avoided. Specifically, regarding hurmah musaharah, the decision of the religious committee is not considered authoritative; one may look to the Maliki madhhab, which in some cases does not establish prohibition from touching with desire. The author emphasizes that the committee's role as a qadi is separate from the issue of causing separation due to prohibition. Hence, using talfiq by adopting the Maliki view is permissible, provided the person consults a trusted scholar. The passage concludes with an example of a woman's claim and the method of decision.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmah musaharah): Prohibition of marriage between persons due to a foster or other relationship, here specifically through physical contact.
شہوت (shahwah): Sexual desire; its presence in one of the parties is sufficient for prohibition.
تلفیق (talfiq): Combining rulings from different madhhabs in a single case to achieve a specific outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, what conditions must be met for hurmah musaharah to be established through touching or kissing?
A) Both parties must have desire.
B) The touching must be skin-to-skin with no barrier, and no seminal emission occurs.
C) The touching must be with desire on one side, no thick barrier, and no seminal emission.
D) The touching must be accompanied by seminal emission.

Key Takeaway
Hurmah musaharah through touch/kissing requires desire on one side, no thick barrier, and no seminal emission; talfiq is permissible when the two matters are separate, as in this hila case.

Talfiq and Caution in Tahrim Musaharat
Explaining the permissibility of talfiq with caution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a fatwa using talfiq by identifying independent rulings and applying the condition of caution.

Core Idea
Talfiq is permissible when rulings are independent, but caution requires consulting a trusted scholar.

This passage addresses a critical nuance in the application of talfiq (legal patchwork) in the context of tahrim musaharat (prohibition through marriage ties). The author clarifies that talfiq is valid when the component rulings are independent of each other, as they are here. However, to avoid misuse, the text emphasizes the need for caution and consultation with a reliable scholar before acting on such a combination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two independent rulings
The passage identifies two separate issues: (1) whether the Shari'a committee's decision is like a judge's ruling, and (2) whether tahrim musaharat itself causes separation. Recognize that these are distinct legal questions.
If they were interdependent, talfiq would not be permissible.
2
Analyze why talfiq is allowed here
Since the two issues are independent (like wudu and salah), combining a ruling from the Hanafi school (on the committee's authority) with a ruling from the Maliki school (on tahrim musaharat) is a valid talfiq. The author explicitly likens it to separate acts.
Independence is key: the rulings do not contaminate each other.
3
Recognize the caution requirement
Despite permissibility, the author insists on caution: the acting person must consult a scholar they trust regarding the permissibility of talfiq in their specific case.
This prevents casual or uninformed talfiq that could lead to invalid acts.
4
Apply to a fatwa scenario
When constructing a fatwa using talfiq, first verify the independence of the rulings, then advise the seeker to consult a trusted scholar before acting. Document the rationale.
This step aligns with the adab al-mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مزید احتیاط کے لیے اصل رسالہ میں کوئی مسئلہ اس قسم کا نہیں لیا کہ جس میں تلفیق اجتماع کے خلاف ہو اور تمہ گذشتہ صفحات میں مذکور کے تین مسائل میں سے بھی دو مسائل میں اس کی رعایت موجود ہے لیکن صرف ایک مسئلہ بیعنی حرمت مصاہرت میں رشرعی کیٹی) جماعت مسلمین کا فیصلہ معتبر نہیں اور حضرات مالکیہ کے شہور و مخاطر مذہب کی درجہ سے بعض خاص صورتوں میں شہرت سے چھونے وغیرہ سے حرمت مصاہرت متعلق نہیں ہوتی لیکن بعض صورتوں میں معتمد قول اور مشہور قول کے موافق اور بعض میں ایک قول پر ان سے مذہب میں بھی اس کا اختیار کیاگیا ہے لیکن ہم ان کو ایک عمل خیال نہیں کرتے، بلکہ جماعت سلمین رشرعی کمیٹی کو قاضی کے حکم میں سمجھنا ایک مستقل مسئلہ ہے اور حرمت مصاہرت کو تفریق کا سبب قرار دینا دوسرا منتقل مسئلہ ہے جس طریقہ سے وضو ایک علیحدہ عمل ہے اور نماز علیحدہ عمل ہے اور اس کی وضاحت اصل رسالہ کے دیباچہ حاشیہ پر کر دی گئی ہے اس وجہ سے تلفیق کی یہ صورت ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے لیکن عمل کے وقت احتیاط یہ ہے کر عمل کرنے والا تلفیق کے جواز کے بارے میں کسی اپنے معتقد عالم سے رجوع کر کے ان کے قوسے پر نکل کرے۔
For extra caution, in the original treatise no issue was taken of such a kind that would be contrary to talfiq ijtima [??], and in two of the three issues mentioned in the previous pages this consideration exists, but only in one issue, i.e., tahrim musaharat, the decision of the Shari'a committee is not considered authoritative, and from the level of the well-known and conflicting madhhab of the Malikis, in some specific cases, touching with desire etc. does not cause tahrim musaharat, but in some cases it is taken according to the relied-upon and well-known opinion, and in some cases it is taken according to a single opinion from their madhhab, but we do not consider them as one act, rather considering the Muslim community's Shari'a committee as in the position of a judge is an independent issue, and making tahrim musaharat a cause of separation is a second independent issue, just as wudu is one act and salah is another act, and its clarification has been given in the preface margin of the original treatise. For this reason, this form of talfiq is permissible in our view, but at the time of action caution is that the doer should refer to a scholar whom he trusts regarding the permissibility of talfiq and then act upon their opinion.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage clarifies the permissibility of talfiq (legal patchwork) in the specific context of tahrim musaharat. The author explains that the ruling involves two independent issues: (1) whether the Shari'a committee's decision is authoritative like a judge's, and (2) whether tahrim musaharat can be a cause for separation. Since these are separate, talfiq is allowed. However, the author advises caution: one should consult a trusted scholar before acting on such a talfiq.

Key Terms
تلفیق (talfiq): Combining rulings from different madhahib in a single act to achieve a desired outcome.
حرمت مصاہرت (tahrim musaharat): Prohibition of marriage due to familial relationships established through marriage (e.g., prohibitions by affinity).
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Caution; in this context, the procedural requirement to consult a trustworthy scholar before acting on a talfiq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Follow the majority of scholars.
D) Avoid talfiq altogether.

Key Takeaway
Talfiq is permissible when rulings are independent, but one must consult a trusted scholar before acting.

Procedure for Separation Due to Hurmat Musaharat
Details the judicial procedure for separation when wife claims haram relationship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi judicial procedure for claims of hurmat musaharat, including the evidentiary hierarchy (confession, witnesses, oath) and the distinction between acts that inherently imply lust and those that require proof.

Core Idea
The qadi must follow a strict sequence: confession → witnesses → oath — and the type of act determines whether lust is presumed or must be proven.

When a wife claims that her husband or a relative has committed an act establishing hurmat musaharat, the Hanafi jurist does not simply accept the claim. Instead, a detailed procedure ensures that separation is only decreed when certainty is achieved. This lesson unpacks that procedure, focusing on the roles of confession, witnesses, and oath, and the critical distinction between acts that are inherently lustful and those that require external proof of lust.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimant and the procedural trigger
The wife claims hurmat musaharat. The qadi must handle the case as a legal claim, not a mere allegation.
The claim must specify the act and the person involved.
2
Follow the evidentiary hierarchy
First ask husband to confirm. If yes, separation. If not, require witnesses from wife. If no witnesses, offer oath to husband. If he swears, case dismissed; if refuses, separation.
The sequence is mandatory; not optional.
3
Distinguish between acts by husband vs. third party
The form of oath differs. For husband's act, oath denies the act or lust. For third party, husband swears about his belief in her truthfulness.
This distinction is crucial for the procedure.
4
Apply the classification of physical acts
Kissing mouth/cheek, touching private parts/breast: testimony alone suffices (lust presumed). Kissing forehead/head, touching other body parts: testimony must include proof of lust, otherwise oath on husband.
The list is exhaustive; not all touches are equal.
5
Determine the ruling outcome
Based on the evidence and oath, decree separation or dismiss the case.
If husband refuses oath, separation is obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصاہرت سبب ہے لہذا مجھ کو میرے شوہر سے علیحدہ کیا جائے تفریق واقع کر دی جائے تو اس صورت میں قاضی یا اس کا قائم مقام پہلے تو شوہر سے بیان میں اگر اس نے عورت کے بیان کی تصدیق کر دی جب تو تفریق کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے اور اگر شوہر نے اس دعوی کی تصدیق نہیں کی تو عورت سے گواہ لیے جائیں اگر وہ گواہ پیش نہ ہوں یا ان میں گواہی کی شرائعا موجود نہ ہوں تو شوہر سے حلف لیا جائے اگر وہ صاف کر لے تو مقدمہ خارج کر دیا جائے یعنی نہ تو تفریق واقع کی جائے اور نہ یہ فیصلہ کیا جائے کہ عورت بدستور شوہر کے ساتھ رہے اور اگر قاضی نے عورت کو اس کے نکاح میں رہنے کا حکم دے دیا تو اس کا حکم مسئلہ ہے میں آگے آرہا ہے اور اگر وہ حلف سے انکار کر دے تو تفریق واقع کردی جائے۔

حلف

اگر شوہر کے فعل پر دعوی حلف ، تصدیق اور گواہی سے متعلق وضاحت پر شلا یہ کہ اس نے ہو مثلاً بیوی کے اصول و فروع میں سے فلاں عورت کو شہوت کے ساتھ پکڑا ہے جب تو شوہر سے اس بات پر حلف لیا جائے کہ اُس نے ہرگز یہ حرکت نہیں کی ، یا شہوت سے یہ کام نہیں کیا اور اگر دوسرے کے فعل پر دعوی تھا مثلاً عورت اس طریقہ سے کہے کہ مجھے خسر نے شہوت سے پکڑا ہے تو شوہر سے اس طریقہ سے حلف لیا جائے گا کہ خدا کی قسم میرا، زیادہ تر خیال یہ ہے کہ عورت اس دعوی میں سچی نہیں اور اس واقعہ کا ہونا یا شہوت کے ساتھ ہونا میرے دل کو نہیں لگتا،

اور اگر گواہی میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ دہن اور رخسار پر بوسہ دینے اور شرمگاہ یا عضو مخصوص چھونے اور پستان چھونے کے دعوی میں تو صرف ان افعال کی شہادت دینے سے حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی شہوت کا انکار مسموع نہ ہوگا اور تفریق کا حکم کر دینا لازم ہو گا اور پیشانی یا سر و غیرہ پر بوسہ دینے اور باقی بدن چھونے میں اگر یہ شہادت ہو کہ یہ افعال شہوت کے ساتھ ہوئے تھے اور اس کا علم قرائن سے شاہدین کو ہو سکتا ہے تو اس گواہی سے حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی ، ورنہ صرف افعال پر شہادت دینا کالعدم ہے اس کی بنا پر تفریق کا حکم نہ کیا جاوے گا بلکہ خاوند سے حلف لیا جاوے کہ یہ افعال شہوت سے نہیں تھے، اگر حلف کرے تو خیر ورنہ تفریق کا حکم کردیں گے۔
Because of relationship by marriage, she asks to be separated from her husband; separation should be effected. In this case, the qadi or his deputy first asks the husband: if he confirms her statement, then separation is decreed. If the husband does not confirm the claim, then witnesses are taken from the wife. If she does not produce witnesses or the legal conditions for testimony are not met, then an oath is taken from the husband. If he swears [and clears himself], the case is dismissed, meaning neither is separation effected nor is it decreed that the wife continues with the husband. If the qadi ordered the wife to remain in the marriage, that ruling is a problematic issue that will come later. If he refuses to take the oath, then separation is effected.

Oath: If the claim is about the husband's act, e.g., he took hold of a woman from the wife's ancestors or descendants with lust, then the husband is made to take an oath on that matter that he never did this act, or did it with lust. If the claim was about another's act, e.g., the wife says that her father-in-law took hold of her with lust, then the husband is made to take an oath in this manner: 'By God, my predominant opinion is that the wife is not truthful in this claim, and my heart does not feel that this event occurred or that it was with lust.'

If the testimony includes these details: for claims of kissing on the mouth and cheek, and touching the private parts or specific organ, and touching the breast, then mere testimony of these acts establishes prohibition due to relationship by marriage; denial of lust is not heard, and it is necessary to decree separation. For kissing on the forehead or head, etc., and touching the rest of the body, if the testimony is that these acts occurred with lust and the witnesses can know that through circumstances, then by this testimony prohibition due to relationship by marriage is established; otherwise, mere testimony of acts is null, so separation is not decreed; rather, the husband is made to take an oath that these acts were not with lust; if he swears, then fine; otherwise, separation is decreed.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage outlines the Hanafi legal procedure when a wife claims that a relationship of prohibition due to marriage (hurmat musaharat) has occurred, such as her husband having sexual contact with her mahram relatives. The author, a Hanafi scholar, presents a step-by-step judicial process. First, the qadi asks the husband to confirm. If he confirms, separation is immediate. If not, the wife must bring witnesses. If witnesses are unavailable or insufficient, the husband is given an oath. If he swears, the case is dismissed; if he refuses, separation is decreed. The text then details the form of oath depending on whether the accused act is by the husband or a third party. For direct acts of the husband, the oath is a simple denial. For acts by another (e.g., father-in-law), the husband swears about his belief in her truthfulness. Finally, the text distinguishes between acts that inherently imply lust (kissing mouth/cheek, touching private parts/breast) where testimony alone suffices, and acts that require proof of lust (kissing forehead/head, touching other body parts). This distinction is critical for the validity of the claim. The passage is a practical guide for a qadi handling such sensitive family disputes, reflecting the Hanafi principle of prioritizing certainty and avoiding presumptuous separation.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmat musaharat): The prohibition of marriage established by relationship through marriage, e.g., if a man touches his wife's mother, his wife becomes forbidden to him.
حلف (halaf): An oath taken by the husband to deny the claim, either directly or by stating his belief.
شہادت (shahadat): Testimony of witnesses in court about the alleged act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the proper sequence after the husband denies the claim of hurmat musaharat?
A) Witnesses then oath.
B) Oath then witnesses.
C) Separation immediately.
D) Divorce by mutual consent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi procedure for hurmat musaharat claims requires a strict evidentiary sequence: confession, then witnesses, then oath — with the form of oath and proof of lust depending on the nature of the alleged act.

Conditions for Exercising Khiyar al-Bulugh in Marriage
Explaining rules for immediate verbal consent/rejection and role of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of khiyar al-bulugh to determine whether a minor married without consent can validly annul the marriage upon reaching puberty, and identify the required conditions for witnesses.

Core Idea
Immediate verbal expression is crucial for a non-virgin's khiyar al-bulugh; a virgin's silence does not forfeit her right.

This passage from Al-Hilat al-Najijah details the precise conditions under which a minor who was married without consent may exercise the option of puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) to annul the marriage. Understanding these conditions is essential for constructing a valid legal stratagem (hila) for dissolution. The text distinguishes between virgins (bikr) and non-virgins (thayyiba), emphasizing immediate verbal consent or rejection for the latter, and clarifies the role of witnesses in preserving the option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category of the person
Determine whether the minor is a virgin girl (bikr), a non-virgin girl (thayyiba), or a boy. The rules for immediacy depend on this category.
In Hanafi law, a boy's rule is identical to a thayyiba's: immediate verbal expression is required.
2
Check for compulsion (idhtirar)
If the person was unable to speak immediately due to a genuine excuse (cough, sneeze, forcibly silenced), the option is not invalidated provided they speak as soon as the excuse is removed.
Any delay without excuse invalidates the option for a thayyiba or boy.
3
Assess subsequent consent
If after puberty the person consents verbally or by action (e.g., kissing), the option is forfeited. For a virgin, silence alone does not constitute consent.
Consent must be explicit or implied by conduct; presence or absence of witnesses does not affect the validity of consent.
4
Apply the rule of knowledge
If the minor was unaware of the marriage before puberty, the option period starts from the time they learn of the marriage, not from puberty. All rules of immediacy are then applied from that moment.
The text emphasizes this as a key exception.
5
Implement witness requirements
When rejecting the marriage, a girl must have at least two male witnesses or one male and two female witnesses. She must explicitly state that she rejects at the moment of puberty, not earlier.
Witnesses can be present at the moment of puberty or summoned later; the declaration must be clear.

Whether [she consents or not], in every case immediate verbal expression is a condition. However, if due to coughing or sneezing etc. she was unable to speak immediately, or someone forcibly closed her mouth, then the delay caused by this compulsion does not invalidate the option, provided that as soon as the compulsion is removed she speaks immediately. If she delays speaking without any compulsion, the option is invalidated, and it is no longer permissible to have the marriage annulled. If she gets the marriage annulled through false statement, she will be severely sinful. Also, a virgin girl needs to make at least two men or one man and two women witness her verbal statement, so that when the matter is brought before a judge etc., they can testify. The detailed ruling of witnessing is mentioned later. And if the girl is a virgin, then speaking immediately is not necessary for her; rather, as long as she does not consent, the option to keep or not keep the marriage remains, no matter how much time passes. Merely remaining silent does not invalidate her option of puberty. However, if after puberty she says verbally that she consents to this marriage, or does some action that indicates consent, then the option is invalidated. And the ruling for a boy is the same as for a non-virgin girl: i.e., upon attaining puberty, it is not necessary for him to speak immediately; rather, as long as he does not consent by word or deed, the option remains. So if a boy or girl says once after puberty, verbally, that they consent to this marriage, then demanding annulment is forbidden, even if that consent was said in complete solitude or quietly such that no one heard it. Similarly, if after puberty kissing etc. occurs, then the option of annulment does not remain. And all this detail applies when they had been informed of the marriage before puberty. If someone did not know about the marriage before puberty, then khiyar al-bulugh is acquired from the time they come to know, and the detail about the option remaining or not will be considered from the time of knowledge. It is necessary for the girl to have witnesses at the time of puberty when she rejects the marriage. When the girl, upon becoming adult, rejects the marriage, she also needs witnesses for the rejection, as previously mentioned, but that was brief, so detail is written. The detail is that i.e. making witnesses, has two forms: First: if at the time she becomes adult there are witnesses present, then she should say at that moment: 'I have now become adult and I want to have this marriage annulled.' Second: if witnesses are not present at that time, then in that case she should immediately verbally reject and then call witnesses or go to them. Whether witnesses are found quickly or late, in every case she should say before them: 'I have now become adult and I want to annul the marriage.' She should never say it in a way that implies she had become adult earlier, even if the witnesses ask clearly, 'When did you become adult?'
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rules governing khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) within the Hanafi school, as a legal stratagem (hila) for a minor married without consent to dissolve the marriage upon reaching puberty. The text first establishes the general principle: for a thayyiba (non-virgin girl or boy), immediate verbal expression (fauran zabaan se kehna) is a condition for exercising the option. If she does not speak immediately without excuse, the option is lost. Exceptions are made for genuine impediments like coughing or being silenced. For a bikr (virgin), the rule is relaxed: she does not have to speak immediately; her option continues until she explicitly or implicitly consents. Silence alone does not invalidate her option. The ruling for a boy is identical to that of a thayyiba. The passage further clarifies that these rules apply only if the person knew of the marriage before puberty; if knowledge comes after puberty, the option period starts from the time of knowledge. Finally, it emphasizes the necessity of witnesses when rejecting the marriage: either existing witnesses at the moment of rejection or summoning them later, but the verbal declaration must clearly state that rejection occurs at the moment of puberty, not earlier.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option granted to a minor who was married without their consent to either ratify or annul the marriage upon attaining puberty.
ثیبہ (thayyiba): A female who has lost her virginity through previous marriage or intercourse.
بکرہ (bikr): A female who is a virgin and has not been previously married.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Her option of puberty remains valid regardless.
B) Her option is invalidated and she cannot annul the marriage.
C) She must immediately seek a judge's permission.
D) She can still annul the marriage within three days.

Key Takeaway
The validity of khiyar al-bulugh depends on the category of the person (virgin vs non-virgin), immediacy of expression (required for non-virgins/boy), presence of excuses, and proper witnessing; misapplying these conditions can forfeit the option.

Procedures and Legal Stratagem for Khiyar al-Faskh in Minor Marriage
Explains three petition scenarios and a hila when annulment already spoken

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scenarios for filing a khiyar al-faskh petition and apply the Hanafi hila to preserve the option when annulment has already been verbally expressed.

Core Idea
When a minor's marriage is annulled upon puberty, the method of filing and timing determines validity; a hila may preserve the option if executed promptly.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilatul Najijah provides a detailed procedural guide for a woman married as a minor who wishes to annul her marriage upon reaching puberty. It outlines three distinct ways to file a petition before a qadi, each with specific requirements regarding witnesses, oaths, and urgency. Additionally, it presents a legal stratagem (hila) for a woman who has already verbally annulled the marriage at puberty but now wishes to proceed formally. Understanding these procedures is crucial for a mufti advising on such cases to ensure the khiyar is not lost due to procedural errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the khiyar al-faskh and its conditions
The khiyar al-faskh is the option for a minor girl who reaches puberty to annul a marriage contracted by her guardian. The key condition is that it must be exercised immediately upon knowledge of puberty. Delay (e.g., one month with witnesses) voids it.
The passage clarifies that if witnesses testify, the option lasts one month; otherwise, haste is required.
2
Distinguish the three petition scenarios
The passage describes three scenarios: (1) when witnesses have already testified, (2) when witnesses are unavailable or have given detrimental details, and (3) when the woman states she has just reached puberty and disapproves. Each has different requirements for witnesses, oaths, and time limits.
In scenario 1, she must file within one month. In scenario 2, she must expedite and conceal the exact date of puberty. In scenario 3, no witnesses or oath are needed.
3
Analyze the hila for prior verbal annulment
If a woman has already verbally annulled the marriage at the time of puberty, she may still proceed by claiming she has just reached puberty and hiding the prior annulment. This hila is permissible only if done promptly; delay makes it sinful.
The hila relies on the principle that testimony can be based on mujmal (summary) statements, avoiding detailed disclosure that would invalidate the option.
4
Recognize the time limits and consequences
Time limits vary by scenario: one month after testimony (scenario 1), immediate but undefined (scenario 2), and same as scenario 2 (scenario 3). The passage cites Khulasat al-Fatawa that a delay of several days voids the khiyar.
The mufti must emphasize urgency to the woman to avoid loss of the option.

میں جہاں تک ہو سکے جلدی کرنا لازم ہے ۔ لیکن اس عمل کی کوئی حد کتب فقہ میں تلاش کے باوجود نہیں ملی، البتہ ، خلاصہ الفاوی کی ایک روایت سے اس قدر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر چند دنوں تک مقدمہ پیش نہ ہوا تو خیار رفح ساقط ا ختم ہو جائے گا اور صورت ما کا حکم بھی قواعد سے وہ ہی اختم
معلوم ہوتا ہے جو کہ دوسری صورت کا ہے،
واضح رہے کہ یہ مضمون قواعد سے لیا گیا ہے اس وجہ سے عمل کے وقت احتیاطی
کسی محقق عالم سے بھی دریافت فرمالیا جائے۔
اگر کسی عورت نے واقعہ بالغ ہوتے ہی قورا خیار فسخ باطل ہونے کی صورت زبان سے کہہ دیا ہے کہ میں اس نکاح کو
فسخ کرتی ہوں جب تو اس کو جھاڑ ہے کہ گواہوں سے یا قاضی سے اصل واقعہ پوشیدہ رکھ کر یہ کہہ دے کہ میں ابھی بالغ ہوئی ہوں اگر بلوغ کے بعد اس بات کے کہنے میں کچھ تاخیر کردی توضیح نکات کا اختیار باطل ہو گیا اب اس کے لیے ہر گز جائزہ نہیں کہ گرامی اور درخواست کے قبول ہونے کا حیلہ کرے اگر حیاہ کرے گی تو سخت گنہگار ہوگی۔
If she is asked, she should not give a detailed account but give a formal reply: 'I have now reached puberty' or just say 'I annulled the marriage immediately upon reaching puberty'. Because if she gives details to witnesses, they cannot testify in vague terms; and if they give detailed testimony, it will not benefit her. It is permissible for them to testify upon hearing summary (non-explicit) words; they do not need to inquire in detail nor have the right to do so. Then there are three ways to file a petition before the qadi: First way: if witnesses' testimony has already been given, she should file the petition before the qadi or his deputy saying: 'On such and such day upon reaching puberty I disapproved the marriage, and such and such are witnesses to that disapproval; therefore annul my marriage.' Upon this petition, the separation will be effected. Second way: if she cannot produce reliable witnesses or if the witnesses have revealed details that prevent them from giving beneficial testimony, then she should expedite the petition as much as possible, without mentioning when she reached puberty, only saying: 'I annulled the marriage immediately upon reaching puberty; therefore give a ruling of annulment.' Even if the judge asks when she reached puberty, she should not tell. If she tells, then separation cannot occur, and upon such petition the judge will administer an oath and annul the marriage. Third way: she may plainly state: 'I have just now reached puberty and I do not approve of this marriage; therefore I want the marriage annulled.' In this case, no witnesses are needed nor an oath; the qadi will accept the petition and annul the marriage without testimony or oath. Note that among the three scenarios, the first has a grace period of one month from the testimony for filing; if a month passes, the khiyar is lost. In the second case, haste is required as much as possible, but no fixed limit was found in fiqh books; however, a narration in Khulasat al-Fatawa indicates that if the case is not presented for several days, the khiyar becomes void. The ruling for the third scenario is deduced from the rules to be the same as the second. Note that this discussion is derived from principles, so when acting, one should consult a reliable scholar. If a woman has already verbally said 'I annul this marriage' at the time of puberty, making the khiyar apparently void, then she may conceal the real situation from witnesses and the judge and say: 'I have just now reached puberty.' If she delayed saying this after puberty, the option becomes invalid, and it is no longer permissible for her to use any stratagem to have the petition accepted; if she does so, she will be sinning severely.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) discussion from the Hanafi perspective on khiyar al-faskh for a woman married as a minor. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, presents procedural rules for filing a petition before a qadi to annul such a marriage upon reaching puberty. The passage details three scenarios: first, when witnesses are available to testify to the annulment; second, when witnesses are unavailable or have given damaging details, requiring urgency and concealment of the exact date of puberty; third, when the woman simply claims to have just reached puberty and rejects the marriage, which requires no witnesses or oath. The author then clarifies time limits: in the first scenario, one month after testimony; in the second, no fixed limit but haste is necessary; in the third, the same as the second. The final paragraph is a critical hila: if a woman has already announced annulment, thus seemingly losing the option, she may still proceed by claiming immediate puberty and hiding the past annulment. However, if she delays, the option is truly lost and any stratagem becomes sinful. The author emphasizes consulting a verifying scholar due to the sensitivity of the matter.

Key Terms
خیار فسخ (khiyar al-faskh): Option of annulment for a minor who reaches puberty and disapproves of a marriage contracted by her guardian
مجمل (mujmal): Non-detailed, summary statement (as opposed to tafsili)
حیلہ (hila): Legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding harm

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third scenario for filing a petition, what does the woman need to present?
A) Witnesses and an oath
B) A detailed account of when she reached puberty
C) Simply a statement that she has just reached puberty and does not approve the marriage
D) A written contract from her guardian

Key Takeaway
Three procedural scenarios exist for khiyar al-faskh; a hila is permissible only if exercised promptly; delay forfeits the option and makes any stratagem sinful.

Hila for Khiyar al-Bulugh Annulment: Procedure, Limits, and Stratagem
Procedural guide and legal stratagem for khiyar al-bulugh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a valid hila for khiyar al-bulugh annulment and identify when its use becomes impermissible deception.

Core Idea
If a woman prematurely announces annulment, she may use a hila by concealing that and claiming fresh puberty—but only if she acts immediately.

This passage from Ashraf Ali Thanwi's Al-Hilat al-Najijah addresses a delicate situation in Hanafi family law: a woman married as a minor reaches puberty but inadvertently speaks the annulment words before formally exercising her option (khiyar al-bulugh). The author provides the normal procedure, time limits, and a legally sound stratagem (hila) to salvage the annulment—along with a stern warning against misuse. Understanding this hila requires careful attention to the conditions and ethical boundaries laid out in the classical Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the normal annulment procedure
The woman states clearly 'I have just attained puberty and this marriage is not acceptable to me.' No witnesses or oaths are needed; the qadi accepts her claim and annuls the marriage.
This is the baseline scenario where the khiyar is properly exercised.
2
Distinguish the three scenarios and their time limits
Scenario 1: If witnesses testify to her puberty, she has a one-month grace period. Scenario 2: If no witnesses (she simply claims puberty), she must act as soon as possible; a narration from Khulasat al-Fatawa suggests a few days. Scenario 3: If she already spoke the annulment words before proper exercise, the khiyar is void unless she uses a hila immediately.
The text emphasises that in scenario 2 and 3, delay invalidates the khiyar.
3
Understand the hila for premature annulment statement
If she said 'I annul this marriage' before properly exercising khiyar, she must conceal that earlier statement and instead present a fresh claim: 'I have just attained puberty.' This is a permissible legal stratagem to give effect to her true intention.
The hila only works if she acts immediately after puberty; any delay renders the khiyar void.
4
Recognise the ethical boundary
If she delayed after puberty before speaking, or if she uses the hila after the khiyar has already lapsed, it becomes sinful deception (gharar and lying). The author strongly warns against any stratagem in such cases.
The hila is a legitimate tool, not a loophole for dishonesty.
5
Apply the ruling to a consultation scenario
A mufti advising a woman in this situation must first ascertain whether she has already spoken annulment words and whether any delay occurred. If the khiyar is still intact, guide her to the normal procedure. If she has spoken prematurely but immediately, the hila may be used. If delay, the khiyar is lost and she must seek other options.
This lesson integrates fatawa practice with classical fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تو درخواست دینے کی ایک صورت یہ ہے کہ صاف (صاف) اس طریقہ سے کہ دے کہ میں ابھی بالغ ہوئی ہوں اور یہ نکاح مجھے منظور نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے نکاح فسخ کرانا چاہتی ہوں تو اس صورت میں نہ تو کسی گواہ کی ضرورت ہے اور نہ حلف لینے کی بلکہ گواہی کے بغیر اور دانت کے بغیر قاضی اس درخواست کو قبول کر کے نکاح فسخ کر دے۔ واضح رہے کہ مذکورہ بالا تینوں صورتوں میں سے پہلی صورت خیار فسخ کی مہلت یعنی جب گواہ کی گواہی ہو چکی ہو تو اس سے ایک مہینہ تک درخواست کی مہلت ہے اگر ایک ماہ گزر گیا تو خیار فسخ ختم ہو گیا اور دوسری صورت 6 میں جہاں تک ہو سکے جلدی کرنا لازم ہے ۔ لیکن اس عمل کی کوئی حد کتب فقہ میں تلاش کے باوجود نہیں ملی، البتہ ، خلاصہ الفاوی کی ایک روایت سے اس قدر معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر چند دنوں تک مقدمہ پیش نہ ہوا تو خیار رفح ساقط ا ختم ہو جائے گا اور صورت ما کا حکم بھی قواعد سے وہ ہی اختم معلوم ہوتا ہے جو کہ دوسری صورت کا ہے، واضح رہے کہ یہ مضمون قواعد سے لیا گیا ہے اس وجہ سے عمل کے وقت احتیاطی کسی محقق عالم سے بھی دریافت فرمالیا جائے۔ اگر کسی عورت نے واقعہ بالغ ہوتے ہی قورا خیار فسخ باطل ہونے کی صورت زبان سے کہہ دیا ہے کہ میں اس نکاح کو فسخ کرتی ہوں جب تو اس کو جھاڑ ہے کہ گواہوں سے یا قاضی سے اصل واقعہ پوشیدہ رکھ کر یہ کہہ دے کہ میں ابھی بالغ ہوئی ہوں اگر بلوغ کے بعد اس بات کے کہنے میں کچھ تاخیر کردی توضیح نکات کا اختیار باطل ہو گیا اب اس کے لیے ہر گز جائزہ نہیں کہ گرامی اور درخواست کے قبول ہونے کا حیلہ کرے اگر حیاہ کرے گی تو سخت گنہگار ہوگی۔
So, one method of making the request is that she says clearly in this manner: 'I have just attained puberty and this marriage is not acceptable to me, therefore I want to annul the marriage.' In this case, there is no need for witnesses nor for taking an oath; rather, without witnesses and without an oath, the qadi accepts this request and annuls the marriage. It should be clear that among the three mentioned scenarios, the first scenario has a grace period for the option of annulment: that is, when the testimony of witnesses has been given, she has a one-month period to make the request; if one month passes, the option of annulment is lost. In the second scenario, it is necessary to hasten as much as possible. However, no limit for this action was found in the books of fiqh despite searching. Nevertheless, from a narration in Khulasat al-Fatawa, it is known that if the case is not presented within a few days, the option of annulment becomes void. And the ruling for the third scenario is also derived from the principles to be the same as that of the second scenario. It should be clear that this content is taken from the principles; therefore, at the time of practice, one should also consult a verifying scholar as a precaution. If a woman, immediately upon attaining puberty, has verbally said the words of annulment even before the option is lost, then she [must] conceal the real situation from the witnesses or the qadi and say: 'I have just attained puberty.' If she delayed saying this after puberty, then the option of annulment is void. Now it is absolutely not permissible for her to use a stratagem for [acceptance of] falsehood and acceptance of the request. If she uses such a stratagem, she will be a severe sinner.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a hila case from the Hanafi tradition. It begins by explaining a straightforward method for a woman who reached puberty to request annulment of her childhood marriage: she states clearly that she has just become baligha and does not consent to the marriage. No witnesses or oaths are needed; the qadi accepts her statement. The author then clarifies time limits: in the first scenario (where witnesses already testified to her puberty), she has one month to apply; otherwise the khiyar is lost. In the second scenario (where no witnesses are needed because she simply claims puberty), she must act quickly. Although no specific limit is found, a narration from Khulasat al-Fatawa suggests a few days. The third scenario (where she has already spoken annulment words prematurely) follows the same ruling. The author emphasizes caution and consulting a scholar. Finally, the hila: if a woman has already said 'I annul this marriage' before the khiyar is properly exercised, she can hide that fact and instead claim she just attained puberty. But if she delays even a little after puberty, the khiyar is void, and any further stratagem to get annulment would be sinful deception.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option a female who was married as a minor has to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract by the woman’s declaration or qadi’s ruling.
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem that achieves a permissible outcome through a lawful means, often involving concealment of a previous fact.
توریہ (tawriya): Concealment of a fact by a statement that is literally true but intended to convey a different meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can a woman use the hila of hiding her earlier annulment statement?
A) At any time after puberty, as long as she has not consummated the marriage
B) Only if she spoke the annulment words immediately upon reaching puberty and before any delay
C) Only if she has witnesses to her puberty
D) Only if she first obtains permission from her guardian

Key Takeaway
The hila for khiyar al-bulugh annulment is valid only when the woman acts immediately after puberty; any delay renders the khiyar void and further stratagems sinful deception.

Apostasy and Its Effect on Marriage: Correcting a Dangerous Hila Misuse
Rulings on apostasy and correction of a hila misuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on apostasy of each spouse, identify the conditions affecting mahr and iddah, and explain why using apostasy as a hila to break a marriage is invalid and sinful.

Core Idea
Apostasy dissolves marriage instantly, but a wife's apostasy does not free her to remarry—she must return to her original husband.

This passage from Al-Hilatun Najijah clarifies the rulings on apostasy (irtidad) in marriage. It distinguishes the husband's case—automatic dissolution by consensus of all four imams—from the wife's, where the marriage also dissolves but the woman is forced to re-embrace Islam and renew the nikah with her original husband. The passage strongly warns against a dangerous hila: some people mistakenly believe that a wife's apostasy allows her to marry another, leading them to commit apostasy as a 'solution'—a grave sin that achieves nothing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authority
The passage begins by noting that earlier scenarios (difference of religion) were uncontroversial; only the fourth scenario (apostasy) required collective signatures. This highlights the consensus among scholars.
The husband's ruling is by consensus of the four imams and majority of jurists.
2
Apply the condition of khalwat sahiha
For husband's apostasy, the financial consequences (mahr and iddah) depend on whether valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) occurred. If before: half mahr, no iddah. If after: full mahr, iddah, and nafaqah during iddah.
Khalwat sahiha is considered like actual consummation in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Recognize the common mistake
Some people incorrectly generalize the husband's ruling to the wife, assuming her apostasy also frees her to remarry anyone. This is a grave error.
The passage calls this an 'incompetent' deduction that leads to ruin.
4
State the correct Hanafi ruling for wife's apostasy
Zahir al-Riwaya (the relied-upon view) states that the wife's marriage dissolves immediately, but she is imprisoned and forced to re-embrace Islam and renew the marriage with her original husband.
There are three sayings in the Hanafi school; the other two opinions are not detailed but are not mufta bihi.
5
Understand the hila's invalidity
Using apostasy as a trick to escape a disliked marriage is futile: the wife cannot marry another man. Moreover, apostasy destroys one's good deeds and puts one in the 'great calamity'—a major sin.
The hila is not only invalid but religiously catastrophic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر کا مرتد ہو جانا (۲) دوسرے بیوی کا مرتد ہو جانا دونوں کے احکام علیحدہ علیحدہ ہیں اور اس چوتھی (صورت) احتمال کے احکام پرا کا بر علماء کے تصدیقی دستخط بھی موجود ہیں ۔ اختلاف مذہ کے حکم سے تعلق ایک ہدایت شوہر بیوی کے اختلاف مذہب کی پہلی صورت اور دوسری صورت کے ان چار احتمالات رصورتوں ) میں سے اول کے تین اختلالات کے احکام میں تو کوئی اختلاف نہ تھا اس وجہ سے ان کا مسودہ تمام حضرات کے سامنے پیش نہیں کیا گیا بلکہ صرف حضرت حکیم الامت اور چند حضرات کے ملاحظہ پر اکتفا کیا گیا۔ اور (چوتھی صورتوں ) کے حکم میں کچھ اختلاف تھا اس وجہ سے صرف اس صورت کے احکام کو پیش کر کے تمام حضرات کے دستخط حاصل کیے گئے کا فیصلہ اور حاکم کے حکم کی کوئی ضرورت ہیں۔ اور یہ شوہر کا مرتد ہونا خلوت صیحہ سے پہلے ہوا ہے تو آدھا مہر شوہر کے ذمہ ہے اور عورت پر عدت واجب نہیں، اور اگر خلوت صحیحہ کے بعد ارتداد ہوا ہے تو پورا مہر لازم ہے اور عورت پر عدت بھی واجب ہے نیز اس مرتد پر عدت کا نفقہ بھی لازم ہے ۔ بعض لوگوں نے مسائل نہ جاننے زوجہ کے مرند و جانے کا شرعی حکم کی وجہ سے مطلقا یہ مجھ لیا ہے کہ اگر کوئی عورت مزید ہو جائے (نعوذ باللہ ) جب بھی نکاح فسخ ہو جائے گا اور اسی وجہ سے نادافیقیت کی وجہ سے تمام روایات فقیہ کے خلاف یہ تفریع کر بیٹھے (یعنی یہ مسئلہ نکالنے لگے کہ ) اس نالائق کو تجدیدا سلام کے بعد دوسرے شوہر سے رہائی حاصل کرنے کا آسان علاج سمجھ لیا اور مرتد ہونے کی بلاء عظیم میں مبتلا ہو کر اپنے تمام عمر کے نیک اعمال برباد کر دیئے حالانکہ شہر کا بھی اُن کا مقصد حاصل نہیں ہو سکتا تھا کیونکہ اس صورت میں دوسرے شخص سے نکاح کی ہرگز اجازت نہیں بلکہ یہ لازمی ہے کہ دوبارہ اسلام لائے اور دوبارہ نکاح کر کے پہلے ہی شوہر کے ساتھ رہے چنانچہ مندرجہ ذیل فصیل سے معلوم ہوگا۔ وہ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کے مرتد ہونے کی صورت میں مذہب حنفیہ میں تین قول ہیں ۔ ایک ظاہر الروایتہ جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ عورت کے مرتد ہونےسے نکاح تو فورا فتح ہو جائے گا لیکن پھر اس کو جبس و قید کر کے تجدید اسلام پر بھی اور اس پر بھی مجبور کیا جائے گا کہ وہ اپنے پہلے ہی خاوند سے تجدید نکاح کرے جیسا کہ قاضی خاں اور عالمگیری اور در محار و شامی میں اس کی تصریح ہے کہ ظاہر الروایہ جس میں فتح نکاح کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اس کے ساتھ یہ بھی مذکور ہے کہ عورت تجدید نکاح کرے جیسا کہ قاضی خاں اور عالمگیری اور در متخار و شانی میں اس کی تصریح ہے کہ ظاہر الروایہ جس میں فسخ نکاح کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اس کے ساتھ یہ بھی مذکورہ ہے کہ عورت کو تجدید اسلام اور شوہر اقوال سے تجدید نکاح پر بزور
Husband's apostasy (2) Second, wife's apostasy. The rulings of both are separate, and the signatures of scholars are present on the rulings of this fourth (scenario) [؟]. Regarding the ruling of difference of madhhab, a guidance: first scenario of husband-wife difference of madhhab, and from the four probabilities (scenarios) of the second scenario, there was no difference in the rulings of the first three possibilities, therefore its draft was not presented before all elders, but was only shown to Hakim al-Ummat and a few persons. And in the ruling of (the fourth scenario) there was some difference, therefore only the rulings of this scenario were presented and signatures of all elders were obtained. The ruling for the case of the husband's apostasy: If a woman's husband, God forbid, deviates from Islam and becomes an apostate, then by consensus of the four Imams and agreement of the majority of jurists, his marriage is dissolved automatically; there is no need for a qadi's decision or ruler's order. And if this apostasy of the husband occurred before valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha), then half the dower is due from the husband and the woman is not obligated to observe iddah; and if apostasy occurred after valid seclusion, then the full dower is obligatory and the woman must observe iddah, and the apostate is also liable for the maintenance during iddah. Some people, due to ignorance of the rulings, have mistakenly concluded absolutely that if a woman becomes an apostate (God forbid), then her marriage will also be dissolved, and due to this [؟] against all authentic rulings they derived (i.e., they started extracting this ruling) that this incompetent person considered it an easy remedy to get freedom from another husband after renewing Islam, and by falling into the great calamity of apostasy, ruined all their lifetime's good deeds, whereas even their intended purpose could not be achieved because in this case permission to marry another person is absolutely not allowed; rather it is necessary that she re-embrace Islam and renew the marriage and remain with the first husband. So from the following detail it will be known. The detail is that in the case of a woman's apostasy, there are three sayings in the Hanafi madhhab. (1) Zahir al-Riwaya, whose summary is that from the woman's apostasy, the marriage is dissolved immediately, but then she will be imprisoned and forced to re-embrace Islam and also forced to renew marriage with her first husband, as is clarified in Qadikhan, Alamgiri, Durr Mukhtar, and Shami that Zahir al-Riwaya, in which the ruling of dissolution of marriage is given, along with it it is also mentioned that the woman should renew marriage, as is clarified in Qadikhan, Alamgiri, Durr Mukhtar, and Shami that Zahir al-Riwaya, in which the ruling of annulment of marriage is given, along with it it is also mentioned that the woman is forced to re-embrace Islam and to renew marriage with the husband.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hilatun Najijah addresses the rulings of apostasy (irtidad) and its effect on marriage, distinguishing between apostasy of the husband and apostasy of the wife. It begins by contextualizing that earlier scenarios (of difference in religion) were uncontroversial and only the fourth scenario required collective signatures. The author then provides the ruling for a husband's apostasy: By consensus of the four Imams and majority of jurists, the marriage is dissolved immediately without need for a qadi's decision. The mahr and iddah depend on whether valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) had occurred. If before seclusion, half mahr is due and no iddah; if after, full mahr and iddah with maintenance. The passage then warns against a common misuse: Some ignorant people think that a wife's apostasy also dissolves the marriage, leading them to use apostasy as a trick (hila) to escape a disliked husband and remarry. This is a grave sin and does not achieve the desired result because the correct Hanafi ruling (Zahir al-Riwaya) is that the marriage is dissolved, but the wife is imprisoned and forced to re-embrace Islam and then forced to renew the nikah with her original husband. Thus, the hila is invalid. The passage mentions that there are three opinions in the Hanafi school on this issue, but only the first (Zahir al-Riwaya) is detailed here. This passage serves to correct a dangerous misunderstanding and prevent people from committing apostasy under a false pretext.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who has left Islam, whether by word or action.
خلوت صحیحہ (khalwat sahiha): Valid seclusion between spouses after marriage, which is sufficient to establish full mahr and iddah obligations.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after dissolution of marriage before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband apostatizes after khalwat sahiha, what is the ruling regarding mahr and iddah?
A) Full mahr is due and no iddah
B) Half mahr is due and iddah is required
C) Full mahr is due and iddah is required
D) No mahr is due and iddah is required

Key Takeaway
Apostasy automatically dissolves marriage, but a wife's apostasy does not free her to remarry; she must return to her original husband, making apostasy a futile and sinful hila.

Three Narrations on the Apostate Woman's Marriage: Internal Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on apostate marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the effect of a woman's apostasy on her marriage and identify the single point on which all three agree.

Core Idea
All three narrations agree the apostate woman cannot marry another — the dispute is only how to handle the existing marriage.

Imam Abu Hanifa transmitted three different rulings on whether a woman's apostasy dissolves her marriage. This lesson unpacks those three narrations, their common ground, and the practical difference they make.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three narrations
Read the source passage and list the three positions: marriage dissolved (Zahir al-Riwayah), marriage not dissolved, and she becomes a concubine.
All three are attributed to Abu Hanifa himself.
2
Find the common agreement
The passage states all three agree on one point — what is it? Highlight the sentence that declares this unanimity.
She cannot use apostasy to escape the marriage and wed another.
3
Contrast the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of each narration? For example, under the first she must renew the contract; under the second she stays married; under the third she becomes a concubine.
The concubine ruling only applies in certain contexts (Dar al-Harb).

The government will compel her, whether her apostasy was for the purpose of separating from her first husband or her beliefs actually changed; in both cases she will be compelled to renew the marriage (as explicitly stated by al-Shami). In short, I say: The mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand and some mashayikh of Bukhara, like Zahid Abu al-Nasr Lusi and Abu al-Qasim Saffar, etc., give the fatwa that in the case of a woman's apostasy, the marriage is not dissolved; rather, this woman remains in the marriage of the first husband as before. The third saying is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that this woman will be made a concubine in Dar al-Islam, and her husband's control over her remains as before. Summary: If a woman becomes an apostate, there are three sayings from Abu Hanifa regarding her marriage. One: The marriage is dissolved, but after returning to Islam, she will be compelled to renew the marriage, and she will not be given the option to marry elsewhere (this is Zahir al-Riwayah). Second: The marriage is not dissolved; rather, both remain husband and wife as before. The detail of this issue is that if the woman becomes an apostate and goes to Dar al-Harb, or becomes an apostate while in Dar al-Harb, then there is agreement in Zahir al-Riwayah on making her a concubine. The difference in Zahir al-Riwayah is only whether she can be made a concubine while staying in Dar al-Islam or not. But with giving fatwa on this narration, it is also necessary that before renewal of Islam and renewal of marriage, the husband is not permitted to have intimate contact, etc., as will soon come in the text under the heading 'Some Issues'. Third: The woman will be kept as a concubine. Although there is some difference among these three sayings, all three agree on one point: that the woman will not be given any right to separate from her first husband's marriage and marry elsewhere. Therefore, it is agreed that the woman will have no option to marry elsewhere. Now in the present conditions of India, acting upon this agreed ruling by adopting the first narration is impossible, because after giving the ruling of dissolution of marriage, there is no authority among Muslims to compel her to remarry, and where such authority exists, there are also difficulties and hardships. For this reason, acting upon the first saying (Zahir al-Riwayah) has become impossible in the present condition of India, because although acting upon one part is in our control, the second part (bringing her back to Islam and compelling her to remarry) is certainly not in our control. Acting upon the Nawadir narration is also difficult, rather impossible in the current state. Therefore, there was no choice but to adopt the saying of the mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand and give fatwa upon it. Although the author of al-Nahr did not face the difficulties that we face today, he still, in his time, recommended giving fatwa on this narration and considered opposing it to be causing severe hardship. And Allamah Ibn Abidin al-Shami also does not oppose this fatwa. Whatever he said was at a time when the Nawadir narrations were accessible. When they are not accessible, then in his view as well, the mashayikh of Balkh...
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal stratagem (hila) for dealing with a married woman who apostatizes from Islam. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, discusses three narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa on the effect of apostasy on marriage. The first narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) states that the marriage is dissolved upon apostasy, but if she returns to Islam, she must renew the marriage with her original husband and has no option to marry anyone else. The second narration holds that the marriage is not dissolved at all; she remains married. The third narration says she becomes a concubine (kaniz), with her husband retaining rights over her. All three narrations agree on the key point: the woman cannot use apostasy as a means to escape her marriage and marry another man. In the Indian context, the author finds that implementing the first narration (the default, Zahir al-Riwayah) is impossible because there is no Islamic authority to compel her to return to Islam and remarry. The second narration (from the Nawadir) is also impractical. Therefore, following the mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand, he adopts the second narration that the marriage is not dissolved. This is a classic example of takhayyur (selecting a weaker opinion due to necessity) and maslaha (public interest). The author notes that even later scholars like Ibn Abidin endorsed this approach when the Nawadir narrations are inaccessible.

Key Terms
مرتدہ (murtadda): A female apostate; a Muslim woman who leaves Islam, whether by changing beliefs or for worldly reasons.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; the most authoritative transmission in the Hanafi school.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or weaker transmissions from the Hanafi imams, not included in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
