A) The marriage is always dissolved.
B) The woman becomes a concubine.
C) The woman has no right to marry anyone other than her original husband.
D) The woman may choose to marry another man after repentance.

Key Takeaway
Despite internal differences, the Hanafi school unanimously prohibits an apostate woman from remarrying outside her original marriage.

Choosing the Weakest Opinion: Takhayyur in the Indian Fatwa on Apostasy
Fatwa methodology in a non-Muslim state

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Ashraf Ali Thanwi adopted the second narration over Zahir al-Riwayah and identify the conditions for using takhayyur in Hanafi iftaa.

Core Idea
When the authoritative opinion cannot be implemented, a weaker opinion may be adopted to prevent harm and uphold the agreed prohibition.

Having established the three narrations, Ashraf Ali Thanwi turns to the practical reality of British India. He argues that the first narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) cannot be fully enforced, and the third is too harsh, so the second narration is chosen as a necessary legal stratagem (hila). This lesson examines the fatwa methodology behind that choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the practical impossibility
Find in the text why Thanwi says the first narration cannot be implemented in India. What specific component is missing?
The authority to compel her to return to Islam and remarry.
2
Understand the role of Nawadir
Thanwi mentions Nawadir as an alternative. Why does he reject them as well?
They are also difficult or impossible to apply in the current context.
3
Apply the principle of takhayyur
Takhayyur is selecting a weaker opinion due to necessity. How does Thanwi justify choosing the second narration?
He relies on the fatwa of the mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand.
4
Note the authority hierarchy
What is the authority level of the chosen opinion (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, or fatawa mutakhkhirin)?
It is from the fatawa mutakhkhirin, not the most authoritative level.

حکومت مجبور کیا جائے گا خواہ اس کے مرتد ہونے کی غرض خاوند اول سے علیحدہ ہونا ہیں ہو یا حقیقہ یا اس کے عقائد بدل گئے ہوں دونوں صورتوں میں اس کو تجدید نکاح پر مجبور کیا جائے (نکا صرح به الشامی) در شهر اقول : مشایخ بلخ و سمرقند اور بعض مشائخ بخارا المیل زاہد ابو النصر لوسی اور ابو القاسم سفار وغیر ہم کا فتوی ہے کہ عورت کے مرتد ہونے کی صورت میں نکاح فسخ ہی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بدستور یہ عورت شوہر سابق کے نکاح میں رہتی ہے تیسرا قول وہ نو اور کی روایت ہے امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ سے کہ یہ عورت دار الاسلام میں بھی کنیز بناکر رکھی جائے گی اور اس کے خاوند کا قبضہ اس پر بدستور سابتی باقی رہے گا۔ حاصل یہ میکہ اگر عورت مرتد ہو جائے تو اس کے نکاح کے بارے میں ابو حنیفہ کے تین قول ہوئے۔ ایک یہ کہ نکاح فسخ ہو جاتا ہے لیکن بعد تجد ید اسلام اس کو تجدید نکاح پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اور کسی دوسری جگہ نکاح کرنے کا اختیار نہ دیا جائے گا ۔ (وهو ظاهر الروائية) دوسرا یہ کہ نکاح فسخ ہی نہ ہوگا بلکہ وہ دونوں بدستور زن و شوہر ہی رہیں گے لے تفصیل اس مسئلہ کی یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب میں چلی جائے یا دار الحرب میں ہی مرتا ہو تو اس کو کنیز بنانے پر طاہر الروایتہ بھی متفق ہے تو اور اور ظاہر الروایہ کا اختلاف صرف اس میں ہے کہ داران اسلام میں رہتے ہوئے بھی کنیز بن سکتی ہے یا نہیں لیکن اس روایت پر فتوی دینے کے ساتھ یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ تجدید اسلام اور تجدید نکات سے قبل شوہر کو استماع بینی صحبت وغیرہ کی اجازت نہ دی جائے جیسا کہ متن میں بھی تحت عنوان - بعض مسائل بمرور یہ عنقریب آتا ہے۔ تیسرا یہ کہ عورت کو کنیز بنا کر رکھا جائے گا۔ ان تینوں اقوال میں اگر چہ کچھ اختلاف ہے لیکن اتنی بات پر تینوں متفق ہیں کہ عورت کو کسی طرح یہ حق نہ دیا جائے گا کہ وہ اپنے پہلے خاوند کے نکاح سے علیحدہ ہو کر دوسری جگہ نکاح کرلے ۔ اس لیے یہ بات متفق علیہ ہوگئی کہ عورت کو دوسری جگہ نکاح کا ہرگز اختیار نہ ہوگا ۔ اب ہندوستان میں موجودہ حالات میں اس متفقہ حکم پر عمل کرنا پہلی روایات کو اختیار کرتے ہوئے غیر ممکن ہے کیونکہ فسخ نکاح کا حکم دینے کے بعد پھر دوبارہ نکاح کرنے پر مجبور کرنے والی کوئی حماقت مسلمانوں کے پاس موجود نہیں ہے اور جس جگہ موجود ہوتی ہے وہاں پر بھی مشکلات اور دشواریوں کا سامنا ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے پہلے قول یعنی ظاہر الروایت پر عمل کرنا ہندوستان میں موجودہ حالت میں غیر ممکن ہو گیا کیونکہ اس کے ایک جز پر عمل کرنا اگرچہ اختیار میں ہے لیکن دوسرا جز یعنی دوبارہ اسلام لانا اور دوبارہ نکاح پر مجبور کرنا قطعی طور پر اختیار میں نہیں ہے ۔ نوادر کی روایت پر عمل اور نوادر کی روایت پر عمل کرنا تو ہر کیر روایت سے بھی مشکل بلکہ بحالت مو جودہ غیرممکن ہے اس وجہ سے اس کے مشائخ بلخ وسمرقند کے قول کو اختیار کیا اور میں پر فتوی دیا جائے کوئی چارہ نہ رہا اور صاحب نہر کو اگرچہ ان مشکلات کا سامنا نہیں تھا جو آج ہم پر گذر رہی ہیں مگر وہ اپنے وقت ہیں اس روایت پر فتوی دینے کو تجویز فرماتے ہیں اور اس کے خلاف کر نے کو سخت مشکل میں ڈالنا قرار دیتے ہیں اور حضرت علامہ ابن عابدین شالی بھی اس فتو الے کی مخالفت نہیں فرماتے اور جو کچھ فرمایا ہے وہ روایات نوادر پر قدرت ہونے کے وقت فرمایا ہے اور جب اس پر قدرت نہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک بھی مشائخ بلخ
The government will compel her, whether her apostasy was for the purpose of separating from her first husband or her beliefs actually changed; in both cases she will be compelled to renew the marriage (as explicitly stated by al-Shami). In short, I say: The mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand and some mashayikh of Bukhara, like Zahid Abu al-Nasr Lusi and Abu al-Qasim Saffar, etc., give the fatwa that in the case of a woman's apostasy, the marriage is not dissolved; rather, this woman remains in the marriage of the first husband as before. The third saying is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that this woman will be made a concubine in Dar al-Islam, and her husband's control over her remains as before. Summary: If a woman becomes an apostate, there are three sayings from Abu Hanifa regarding her marriage. One: The marriage is dissolved, but after returning to Islam, she will be compelled to renew the marriage, and she will not be given the option to marry elsewhere (this is Zahir al-Riwayah). Second: The marriage is not dissolved; rather, both remain husband and wife as before. The detail of this issue is that if the woman becomes an apostate and goes to Dar al-Harb, or becomes an apostate while in Dar al-Harb, then there is agreement in Zahir al-Riwayah on making her a concubine. The difference in Zahir al-Riwayah is only whether she can be made a concubine while staying in Dar al-Islam or not. But with giving fatwa on this narration, it is also necessary that before renewal of Islam and renewal of marriage, the husband is not permitted to have intimate contact, etc., as will soon come in the text under the heading 'Some Issues'. Third: The woman will be kept as a concubine. Although there is some difference among these three sayings, all three agree on one point: that the woman will not be given any right to separate from her first husband's marriage and marry elsewhere. Therefore, it is agreed that the woman will have no option to marry elsewhere. Now in the present conditions of India, acting upon this agreed ruling by adopting the first narration is impossible, because after giving the ruling of dissolution of marriage, there is no authority among Muslims to compel her to remarry, and where such authority exists, there are also difficulties and hardships. For this reason, acting upon the first saying (Zahir al-Riwayah) has become impossible in the present condition of India, because although acting upon one part is in our control, the second part (bringing her back to Islam and compelling her to remarry) is certainly not in our control. Acting upon the Nawadir narration is also difficult, rather impossible in the current state. Therefore, there was no choice but to adopt the saying of the mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand and give fatwa upon it. Although the author of al-Nahr did not face the difficulties that we face today, he still, in his time, recommended giving fatwa on this narration and considered opposing it to be causing severe hardship. And Allamah Ibn Abidin al-Shami also does not oppose this fatwa. Whatever he said was at a time when the Nawadir narrations were accessible. When they are not accessible, then in his view as well, the mashayikh of Balkh...
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal stratagem (hila) for dealing with a married woman who apostatizes from Islam. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, discusses three narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa on the effect of apostasy on marriage. The first narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) states that the marriage is dissolved upon apostasy, but if she returns to Islam, she must renew the marriage with her original husband and has no option to marry anyone else. The second narration holds that the marriage is not dissolved at all; she remains married. The third narration says she becomes a concubine (kaniz), with her husband retaining rights over her. All three narrations agree on the key point: the woman cannot use apostasy as a means to escape her marriage and marry another man. In the Indian context, the author finds that implementing the first narration (the default, Zahir al-Riwayah) is impossible because there is no Islamic authority to compel her to return to Islam and remarry. The second narration (from the Nawadir) is also impractical. Therefore, following the mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand, he adopts the second narration that the marriage is not dissolved. This is a classic example of takhayyur (selecting a weaker opinion due to necessity) and maslaha (public interest). The author notes that even later scholars like Ibn Abidin endorsed this approach when the Nawadir narrations are inaccessible.

Key Terms
مرتدہ (murtadda): A female apostate; a Muslim woman who leaves Islam, whether by changing beliefs or for worldly reasons.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; the most authoritative transmission in the Hanafi school.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or weaker transmissions from the Hanafi imams, not included in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Ashraf Ali Thanwi not give fatwa according to the first narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) in India?
A) He considered it unsound.
B) He lacked the authority to compel the woman to return to Islam and remarry.
C) He preferred the third narration.
D) He followed the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
When Zahir al-Riwayah cannot be enforced, a mufti may adopt a weaker but actionable narration from the Hanafi school to protect the agreed-upon prohibition.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Fatwa on Woman's Apostasy: Hila of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand
Presents a hila for when a woman's apostasy cannot lead to dissolution due to impossibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the hila of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand to a case of woman's apostasy when the original ruling is unenforceable, and identify the conditions that must be observed.

Core Idea
When enforcement is impossible, adopt a weaker opinion through necessity, but never compromise core prohibitions.

In the current state of India, the default Hanafi ruling on a woman's apostasy—dissolution of marriage followed by enforced re-conversion and remarriage—cannot be implemented due to lack of Muslim authority. The Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand offered a hila: adopt the opinion that the marriage remains intact, but with a strict prohibition on physical intimacy until the woman re-embraces Islam. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this hila and its essential conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The original ruling (Zahir al-Riwayah) requires both dissolution and enforced re-conversion/remarriage; the second part is impossible in a non-Muslim state.
2
Recognize the impossibility
Because there is no Muslim authority to compel re-conversion, the full ruling cannot be applied.
3
Locate the alternative
The Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand held that the marriage does not dissolve upon apostasy. This is a weaker opinion but becomes operative due to necessity.
4
Apply the hila with its condition
The marriage is considered ongoing, but the husband is absolutely forbidden from intercourse or intimacy until the woman renews her Islam.
5
Understand the analogy
Just as a jointly-owned slave-girl cannot be used for intercourse without permission, marital status does not automatically permit intimacy.

Source Text

اب ہندوستان میں موجودہ حالات میں اس متفقہ حکم پر عمل کرنا پہلی روایات کو اختیار کرتے ہوئے غیر ممکن ہے کیونکہ فسخ نکاح کا حکم دینے کے بعد پھر دوبارہ نکاح کرنے پر مجبور کرنے والی کوئی حاکمیت [؟] مسلمانوں کے پاس موجود نہیں ہے اور جس جگہ موجود ہوتی ہے وہاں پر بھی مشکلات اور دشواریوں کا سامنا ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے پہلے قول یعنی ظاہر الروایت پر عمل کرنا ہندوستان میں موجودہ حالت میں غیر ممکن ہو گیا کیونکہ اس کے ایک جز پر عمل کرنا اگرچہ اختیار میں ہے لیکن دوسرا جز یعنی دوبارہ اسلام لانا اور دوبارہ نکاح پر مجبور کرنا قطعی طور پر اختیار میں نہیں ہے ۔
نوادر کی روایت پر عمل [بھی؟] کرنا تو ہر کیر [؟] روایت سے بھی مشکل بلکہ بحالت موجودہ غیر ممکن ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس کے مشائخ بلخ و سمرقند کے قول کو اختیار کیا اور اس پر فتوی دیا جائے کوئی چارہ نہ رہا۔
اور صاحب نہر کو اگرچہ ان مشکلات کا سامنا نہیں تھا جو آج ہم پر گزر رہی ہیں مگر وہ اپنے وقت میں اس روایت پر فتوی دینے کو تجویز فرماتے ہیں اور اس کے خلاف کرنے کو سخت مشکل میں ڈالنا قرار دیتے ہیں۔
اور حضرت علامہ ابن عابدین شامی بھی اس فتوی کی مخالفت نہیں فرماتے اور جو کچھ فرمایا ہے وہ روایات نوادر پر قدرت ہونے کے وقت فرمایا ہے اور جب اس پر قدرت نہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک بھی مشائخ بلخ و سمرقند کے قول پر فتویٰ دینا متعین ہے۔ اسی طریقہ سے دوسرے فقہاء میں بھی اس قول کو نقل کر کے تردید نہیں کرتے۔
پس ہندوستان میں بحالت موجودہ کہ حکومت مسلمانوں کی نہیں ہے، اس کے علاوہ مذہب حنفی پر عمل غیر ممکن ہے، کہ مشائخ بلخ و سمرقند کے قول کے موافق اس طریقہ سے فتوی دیا جائے کہ عورت کے مرتد ہونے سے نکاح فسخ نہیں ہوتا۔
عورت کے مرتد ہونے سے نکاح باقی رہنے کے بارے میں مشائخ بلخ کی رائے کے بعض مسائل ضروریہ: سلام [؟] مشائخ بلخ کے قول کے موافق جبکہ بقاء نکاح کا فتوی دیا جائے تو ساتھ ہی اس امر کا لحاظ رکھنا ضروری ہے کہ تجدید اسلام کے قبل شوہر کے لیے اس مرتدہ سے جماع اور اس کے دوائی مثلاً تقبیل و لمس بالشہوت وغیرہ کو جائز نہ کہا جائے کیونکہ آیت کریمہ "لا تمسكوا بعصم الكوافر" [؟] سے کافر عورتوں کے ساتھ نکاح اور استمتاع کا حرام ہونا ظاہر ہے اور اس پر اجماع بھی ہے۔
اور کتابیہ کا استثناء جو آیت "والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب" [؟] میں وارد ہے اس سے کتابیہ اصلیہ مراد ہے، وہ مرتدہ اس میں داخل نہیں جس نے اہل کتاب کا مذہب اختیار کر لیا ہو۔
اور قول مذکور پر بقاء نکاح سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ حالت کفر میں محبت و... اے مرتدہ سے مباشرت [؟] ہی ناجائز ہے۔ اس طریقہ سے نوادر کی روایت کی صورت میں بھی اس عورت پر شوہر کا اگرچہ مالکانہ قبضہ ہو جائے گا لیکن شوہر کو اس سے ہمبستری وغیرہ جائز نہیں جیساکہ مشترک باندی سے مالکانہ تصرف کے باوجود اس سے نفع اٹھانا ہمبستری وغیرہ جائز نہیں۔
Third: that the woman will be made to stay in place [unable to remarry]? Among these three sayings, although there is some difference, they all agree on this much: that the woman will not be given any right to separate from her first husband's marriage and marry elsewhere. Therefore, it became agreed upon that the woman will have absolutely no option to marry elsewhere. Now, in the current conditions in India, acting upon this agreed ruling while adopting the earlier narrations is impossible because there is no Muslim authority that compels [re-]marriage after giving a ruling of annulment, and wherever such authority exists, there too difficulties and hardships are faced. For this reason, acting upon the first saying, i.e., Zahir al-Riwayah, has become impossible in the current state in India, because although acting upon one part of it is within capability, the other part—i.e., bringing [the woman] back to Islam and compelling remarriage—is definitely not within capability. Acting upon the Nawadir narration is even more difficult than [acting upon] every narration? but rather in the current situation it is impossible. For this reason, the saying of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand was adopted, and a fatwa is given upon it; there was no other option. And the author of al-Nahr, although he did not face the difficulties that are passing over us today, yet in his time he prescribes giving fatwa upon this narration, and considers acting contrary to it as placing oneself in great difficulty. And Allamah Ibn Abidin al-Shami also does not oppose this fatwa; whatever he said, he said at a time when there was capability upon the Nawadir narrations, and when there is no capability upon them, then in his view too it is determined to give fatwa on the saying of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand. In the same way, other jurists also transmit this saying without refuting it. Therefore, in India in the current situation, where the government is not Muslim, besides that acting upon the Hanafi school is impossible, the fatwa should be given according to the saying of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand in this manner: that the marriage is not dissolved by the woman's apostasy. Regarding the marriage remaining after the woman's apostasy, some necessary issues from the opinion of the Mashayikh of Balkh: ... [unclear]... According to the saying of the Mashayikh of Balkh, when a fatwa is given for the continuity of the marriage, then it is necessary to also observe this matter: that before the renewal of Islam, for the husband, intercourse with this apostate woman and its like, e.g., kissing and touching with desire, etc., should not be considered permissible, because the noble verse 'Do not hold onto the marriages of disbelieving women' [approx. Quran 60:10] makes clear the prohibition of marriage and enjoyment with disbelieving women, and there is consensus upon this. And the exception of the Kitabiyyah that appears in the verse 'And the chaste ones from those who were given the Book' [Quran 5:5] refers to the original Kitabiyyah; an apostate woman who has adopted the religion of the People of the Book is not included in that. And from the aforementioned saying of the continuity of marriage, it does not necessarily follow that love and... of the apostate woman is permissible? [unclear] In this manner, in the case of the Nawadir narration as well, even though the husband has possessory control over this woman, yet intercourse etc. is not permissible for him, just as in the case of a jointly owned slave-girl, despite possessory control, benefiting from her through intercourse etc. is not permissible.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage presents a legal stratagem (hila) for a specific problem: how to handle a woman's apostasy when the default Hanafi ruling (from Zahir al-Riwayah) requires dissolution of the marriage and immediate re-conversion and remarriage, but this is impossible in a non-Muslim state like India. The mashayikh of Balkh and Samarkand offered a solution: adopt the opinion that the marriage does not dissolve upon apostasy. This is a weaker opinion (from Nawadir), but necessity allows it. The author then clarifies essential conditions: even though the marriage is considered intact, the husband cannot have intercourse or physical intimacy until the woman re-embraces Islam. This prevents any violation of the Qur'anic prohibition against marriage with disbelievers. The analogy to a jointly-owned slave-girl (where ownership does not permit intercourse without the co-owner's permission) illustrates that marital continuity does not automatically permit physical relations. Thus, the hila balances legal necessity with adherence to core prohibitions.

Key Terms
مرتدہ (murtaddah): A woman who has left Islam and adopted another religion or becomes an atheist.
ظاہر الروایت (zahir al-riwayah): The most authoritative narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa and his students, transmitted in the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah).
مشائخ بلخ و سمرقند (mashayikh Balkh wa Samarqand): Later Hanafi jurists from the regions of Balkh and Samarqand, known for pragmatic fatwas.

Checkpoint

Hila for Marriage of an Apostate Woman: Fatwa Strategy
Legal stratagem preserving marriage after female apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a fatwa for preserving a marriage after female apostasy, applying the Mashayikh of Balkh's view while observing the caution of tajdid nikah.

Core Idea
Marriage is not dissolved, but intimacy is forbidden until she returns to Islam and the marriage is renewed with a fresh mahr.

This passage from Al-Hilat al-Najizah addresses a critical fatwa scenario: how to preserve a Muslim marriage when the wife apostatizes under non-Muslim rule. The author presents a legal stratagem (hila) based on the Mashayikh of Balkh's opinion that marriage does not dissolve. However, the hila comes with strict conditions and a recommended caution of renewing the contract upon her return to Islam. This lesson walks through the ruling, its proofs, and its practical application for the mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem and the two positions
A woman apostatizes; Zahir al-Riwayah says marriage dissolves; Mashayikh Balkh say it doesn't. The fatwa necessity in non-Muslim lands leads to adopting the latter.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both views have authority.
2
Understand the hila's mechanism
Marriage remains valid, but all intimate relations are prohibited while she is apostate. This is supported by Quran and consensus on prohibition, and analogies from fiqh.
The prohibition is on intimacy, not on the marriage contract itself.
3
Apply the condition after return to Islam
Even under the hila, the author recommends caution (ihtiyat) by requiring renewal of marriage (tajdid nikah) with a new mahr of at least ten dirhams, as per Zahir al-Riwayah.
No compelling need to abandon the stronger view here.
4
Detail the fatwa components
No need to wait for 'iddah; previous mahr remains unless apostasy happened before seclusion.
New mahr is required; previous mahr is a debt.
5
Formulate the final fatwa
Summarize the operative ruling: marriage continues; intimacy prohibited during apostasy; after return, renew marriage with new mahr; previous mahr status depends on seclusion.
The fatwa is tailored to necessity and caution.

The fatwa must be given according to the statement of the Mashayikh of Samarqand. In this way, other jurists do not refute it by transmitting this statement. Therefore, in India, in the present situation where the government is not of Muslims, there is no other way to act upon the Hanafi school except to give fatwa according to the statement of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand, i.e., that marriage is not dissolved by the woman's apostasy. Regarding the marriage remaining with every apostate woman, the opinion of the Mashayikh of Balkh [applies]. Some essential issues: When a fatwa of the continuation of marriage is given according to the statement of the Mashayikh of Balkh, then it is necessary to also observe that before the renewal of Islam, for the husband, sexual intercourse and its preliminaries such as kissing and touching with desire, etc., should not be permitted with this apostate woman, because the noble verse 'Do not marry the polytheist women until they believe' clearly indicates the prohibition of marriage and enjoyment with disbelieving women, and there is consensus on this. And the exception of the People of the Book in the verse 'And the chaste women from those who were given the Scripture' refers to original People of the Book, and the apostate woman who has adopted the religion of the People of the Book is not included in this. And from the said statement of the continuation of marriage, it does not necessitate that enjoyment and intimacy are permissible in the state of disbelief; rather, intercourse with the apostate woman is impermissible. In this way, even in the case of the narration from the Nawadir, the husband will have possessory control over that woman, but intercourse etc. is not permissible for him, just as it is not permissible to derive benefit including intercourse from a jointly owned slave girl despite possessory enjoyment. Intercourse and its preliminaries remain permissible [after return to Islam?], there are such precedents in Hanafi fiqh that despite the validity and continuation of marriage, intercourse and its preliminaries are prohibited, such as a woman married under a shubha (doubtful contract) whose marriage remains as before, but intercourse is completely prohibited until the expiry of the term. Similarly, if a pregnant woman from zina marries someone other than the fornicator, although the marriage is valid, the husband is not permitted to have intercourse. Further, the ruling of renewal of faith and renewal of marriage. That entry of Islam is a condition for the state of enjoyment has been established from the mentioned verse and consensus etc. in the first issue. Then, after renewal of Islam, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, renewal of marriage is also necessary; without it, enjoyment is not permissible. But according to the statement of the Mashayikh of Balkh, renewal of marriage is not a condition. However, in this particular part, there is no compelling need to abandon Zahir al-Riwayah; therefore, renewal of marriage will also be deemed necessary, because there is caution in this. Issue no. 3: In the mentioned scenario, for renewal of marriage, completion of 'iddah is not necessary (as is apparent), but a small new mahr is necessary, which should not be less than ten dirhams, as is explicitly stated in Fath al-Qadir etc., and the previous mahr remains a debt upon the husband, as is apparent. However, if she had apostatized before seclusion, then the previous mahr becomes void. Summary of the fatwa: From this compilation, the summary obtained of this fatwa is that the woman, as before...
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a hila (legal stratagem) from the Hanafi tradition, specifically from the work Al-Hilat al-Najizah, addressing the complex situation of an apostate woman (murtaddah) in a Muslim marriage. The author presents the opinion of the Mashayikh of Balkh and Samarqand, which provides a pragmatic solution for Muslims living under non-Muslim rule where applying the full Hanafi ruling might be difficult. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, a woman's apostasy immediately dissolves the marriage (faskh). However, the Mashayikh of Balkh hold that the marriage remains valid (baqa' al-nikah). The passage clarifies that this hila does not permit any intimate relations while the woman remains in apostasy. It cites Quranic evidence (Surah al-Mumtahina: 10) and consensus to forbid intercourse with disbelieving women, and explains that the exception for People of the Book does not apply to an apostate who adopts their religion. The author draws analogies with other cases in Hanafi fiqh where marriage is valid but intercourse is temporarily prohibited, such as a woman married under shubha (doubtful marriage) or a pregnant woman from zina. After the woman returns to Islam, the author recommends following Zahir al-Riwayah by requiring a renewal of the marriage (tajdid nikah) for caution, even though the Mashayikh of Balkh do not require it. Additional conditions: no need to wait for 'iddah, but a new mahr of at least ten dirhams is required; the previous mahr remains a debt unless the apostasy occurred before seclusion (khalwah), in which case it is void. The passage concludes with a summary that the woman's marriage remains as before, but with the conditions mentioned.

Key Terms
مرتدہ (murtaddah): A woman who has left Islam (apostate)
تجدید نکاح (tajdid al-nikah): Renewal of the marriage contract after the woman returns to Islam
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hila of Mashayikh Balkh presented in this passage, what is required for the husband to have intercourse with his apostate wife after she returns to Islam?
A) He must wait for her 'iddah to expire.
B) He must renew the marriage contract and pay a new mahr of at least ten dirhams.
C) He may resume intercourse immediately without any conditions.
D) He must divorce her first.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa practice, necessity can justify adopting a weaker riwayah, but caution may require supplementing it with the stronger view where possible.

Parsing the Components of a Missing Husband Case
Introducing the components of a missing husband case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and categorize the various fiqh issues that arise in a missing husband case as outlined by the author.

Core Idea
A comprehensive hila requires addressing multiple dimensions: the wife's financial state, fear of sin, age, madhhab adherence, and scholarly authority.

The author of al-Hilat al-Najiza introduces a question about a missing husband by listing its components. This parsing exercise is essential for the mufti to systematically address each concern and construct a valid legal stratagem. Let us break down the components to understand the complexity of the problem.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central legal problem
The passage revolves around a missing husband (mafqud). The wife cannot remarry because her husband's whereabouts are unknown. First, recognize the core fiqh issue: the need to dissolve the marriage to prevent hardship.
This is a classic Hanafi problem where a hila may be needed.
2
List the components from the passage
Go through the Arabic text and extract the numbered items (some numbers missing due to OCR). They include: (1) wife's destitute life, (2) fear of adultery, (3) age of wife after sixty years, (4) no place for her in Hanafi school, (5) accusation of harshness, (6) hadith from Muwatta, (7) scholars' practice during need. Make a complete list.
OCR may have skipped some numbers; treat the listed items as components.
3
Categorize each component by fiqh theme
Group the components: financial hardship (1), moral risk (2), temporal limitation (3), madhhab loyalty (4 & 7), textual evidence (6), methodological criticism (5). This shows the multi-faceted nature of the problem.
Categorizing helps the mufti decide which Hanafi principles to apply.
4
Note the author's intention
The author states he will answer each component sequentially. This preview indicates that the hila will be built part by part, addressing each concern. Understand that the hila is not a single answer but a composite response.
The hila may involve adopting a ruling from another madhhab in cases of necessity (darura).
5
Reflect on the mufti’s role
The mufti must balance strict adherence to Hanafi fiqh with the woman's genuine hardship. The components show that a purely Hanafi solution may be impossible, so a hila (lawful stratagem) is sought, often by temporarily following another school.
This is a core feature of Hanafi ifta' fiqh: the use of hila to avoid haram.

This passage introduces a section of the book where the author responds to a question about a missing husband (mafqūd). The question details a woman's difficult situation. The author lists the components of the question: her destitute life, fear of adultery, her age after sixty years, the accusation of harshness, a hadith from the Muwatta, and the issue of following another madhhab. This sets the stage for a detailed hila (legal stratagem) to resolve her marital situation according to Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A person missing, especially a husband whose whereabouts are unknown, whose wife cannot remarry without dissolution.
حیلة ناجزة (hilatun najiza): An effective legal stratagem to resolve a fiqh problem without violating the ruling.
اجزائے سوال (ajza-e-sawal): The components or parts of the question, as listed by the author to be answered separately.

The Mufti's Role in Constructing a Hila for a Missing Husband
Introducing the methodology for answering a missing husband case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the process a Hanafi mufti follows to formulate a hila (legal stratagem) for a missing husband case, including the factors considered and the use of other madhahib.

Core Idea
A hila for a missing husband is a composite solution built by addressing each component of the problem, often by following another school under necessity.

This lesson focuses on the mufti's methodology as implied by the passage. The author, Ashraf Ali Thanwi, sets out to answer each component separately. This reflects the ifta' process: understanding the problem, identifying the relevant Hanafi principles, and where no direct solution exists, crafting a hila by adopting a ruling from another madhhab under the rules of darura and talfiq.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi default ruling on mafqud
In Hanafi fiqh, a missing husband's wife must wait until he is proven dead or a judge declares him deceased. Traditionally, this required waiting 90 years or until all contemporaries die. This ruling is based on the principle that a marriage contract remains valid until dissolution is certain. Recognize this as the source of hardship.
This default is why a hila is needed.
2
Identify the components causing hardship
As seen in the passage, the wife's destitution, fear of adultery, and age are practical hardships. The mufti must weigh these against the strict Hanafi ruling. Each component may point to a different fiqh principle: necessity (darura), prevention of harm (darar), or following a concession (rukhsa).
The author's list of components serves this purpose.
3
Determine the need for a hila
If the Hanafi school provides no direct solution to the combined hardships, the mufti may construct a hila. A hila is a lawful stratagem that achieves the desired result while technically complying with the letter of the law. In the missing husband case, a common hila is for the wife to temporarily follow the Maliki school, which allows dissolution after a shorter period.
This is permissible under Hanafi ifta' due to necessity (darura) and the principle that 'necessities permit the forbidden.'
4
Apply the components to select the hila
The mufti uses each component to tailor the hila. For example, the component of 'no place in Hanafi' justifies adopting another madhhab. The component of 'scholars' practice during need' provides precedent. The component of 'accusation of harshness' is addressed by showing that the hila is within the spirit of the Shariah.
The hila is not arbitrary; each component must be satisfied.
5
Formulate the fatwa
The final fatwa will include: acknowledgement of the Hanafi default, explanation of the hardship, the basis for applying necessity, and the specific ruling (e.g., the wife may remarry after following the Maliki opinion). The mufti must also guide on how to implement the hila practically.
The fatwa should be clear, authoritative, and cite relevant evidence.

Answers to questions on al-Hilat al-Najiza, i.e., Wifaq al-Mujtahidin. A treatise passed before me in which after giving a brief answer to a question about a missing husband, the responder set eight items for a detailed answer. He writes: Now I wish to give a detailed answer to some parts of the question, but before answering, list the components of the question. Their list is: (1) She lives a helpless, destitute life; (2) There is a national fear of adultery; after sixty or seventy years pass, the woman will not be fit for marriage, then why is a long period set? (3) When there is no place for me in the Hanafi school, what should I do while remaining in this school? (5) Accusation of harshness on the Hanafi school. 149. Investigation of the narration of Imam Malik's Muwatta. (7) The reality of true scholars giving fatwa according to another school at the time of need, and the original ruling of the Hanafi school and its full investigation. After that, he wrote the answer to all components sequentially, and the main purpose of this treatise is that the scholars of the later period in the issue of the missing husband would give fatwa according to the majority school?
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage introduces a section of the book where the author responds to a question about a missing husband (mafqūd). The question details a woman's difficult situation. The author lists the components of the question: her destitute life, fear of adultery, her age after sixty years, the accusation of harshness, a hadith from the Muwatta, and the issue of following another madhhab. This sets the stage for a detailed hila (legal stratagem) to resolve her marital situation according to Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
حیلة ناجزة (hilatun najiza): An effective legal stratagem to resolve a fiqh problem without violating the ruling.
دارورہ (darura): Necessity that permits normally prohibited actions under strict conditions.
تلفیق (talfiq): Amalgamating rulings from different madhahib in a single case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The popularity of the Maliki school

Key Takeaway
A hila is a carefully constructed response to a compound problem, grounded in ifta' methodology and the principles of necessity and precedent.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
advanced
8 min
When a Hanafi Mufti May Give Fatwa by Another Madhab: The Darurah Exception
Explains the hila for Hanafi mufti to use another madhab under necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa according to a non-Hanafi madhab, and apply the concept of darurah to construct a valid hila.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti may apply another madhab's ruling under genuine necessity — but only as a stratagem, not as a change of madhab.

While the default rule is that a Hanafi mufti must give fatwa by the preferred view in his own madhab, the Hanafi tradition recognizes that necessity (darurah) can create an exception. This lesson unpacks the primary objection to such an exception — the usuli dispute about taqlid of a mufdol (inferior mujtahid) — and shows how later authorities, especially Ibn Hajar and al-Shami, resolved it to permit the stratagem. You will learn the precise conditions under which this hila operates, focusing on the scenario where no Maliki judge is available to implement a Maliki ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Begin with the baseline: 'Taqlid is permissible for oneself, but a mufti should only issue fatwa by the preferred (raajih) view of his own madhab.' This is the starting principle of the passage.
This rule prevents frivolous switching.
2
Identify the objection and its basis
The apparent prohibition against a Hanafi mufti using another madhab is based on the claim that one must follow the superior mujtahid (Abu Hanifa) and not an inferior. This objection comes from some usulis and a narration from Imam Ahmad.
The opposing school holds that taqlid of a mufdol is invalid.
3
Examine the usuli dispute
The passage cites al-Tahrir and its commentary stating that the majority (Hanafis, Malikis, Hanbalis, Shafi'is) hold that taqlid of the mufdol is permissible even when a superior is available. This is the relied-upon view.
The Hanafi response considers the opposing view weak (da'if).
4
Derive the hila (stratagem)
Since following an inferior mujtahid is allowed in principle, a Hanafi mufti can, under necessity, adopt a ruling from another madhab (e.g., Maliki) as a practical solution. The necessity (darurah) is key: the mufti does not change madhab but employs a temporary dispensation.
The hila is not a change of madhab but a contextual ruling.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
The passage gives the example of iddah (waiting period) calculation. If a Hanafi judge is faced with a case where the Hanafi ruling causes hardship and no Maliki judge is available to implement the Maliki ruling, necessity (darurah) is realized, and the judge may give fatwa by the Maliki view.
This is the thamarah (practical consequence) of the usuli dispute.

(4) And taqlid is permissible with condition, but it is for the one acting for himself, not for the mufti; so the mufti should not issue fatwa except by the preferred (raajih) in the madhab. From these statements it is established that giving fatwa and judging by another Imam's madhab is not permissible. The answer is that the first statement is... [unclear]. The second statement: 'If it is said to a Hanafi: What is the madhab of Imam Shafi'i on such issue? He says: Abu Hanifa said such-and-such' from Durr Mukhtar. Third: 'Indeed a qadi who is a muqallid, if he violates the well-known of his madhab, his ruling is not executed in the reliable opinion' from Durr Mukhtar. From these statements it is established that issuing fatwa and judging by another Imam's saying is not permissible. The answer is that the first statement is part of... [unclear]. The second statement is a weak saying. Regarding it, Allama Shami clarified: 'This is based on some usulis that it is not permissible to follow the inferior (mafdool) when the superior is present.' And in the preface, Ibn Hajar is quoted stating that this saying is weak. He said: 'Abu al-Wana? mentioned in al-Tahrir and its commentary that it is permissible to follow the inferior even when the superior exists, and this is the view of Hanafis, Malikis, most Hanbalis and Shafi'is; and in a narration from Ahmad and a large group of jurists it is not permissible.' He said after lines: 'And I have seen at the end of the Qawi of Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani explicit mention of some of that; for he gave an example from the worship of al-Nasafi mentioned in the text about confusion when we are asked...' Then a discussion of the views of Shafi'i imams, then he said: 'That is built upon the weak opinion that one must follow the superior only; the correct view is that he may choose to follow the inferior even if his i'tiqad is otherwise.' After that, it is said: 'This saying is not hujjah, and if accepted, it will be interpreted as lacking necessity like the third and fourth expressions. And for the answer to the third expression, it is sufficient to quote Shami's full words.' Then the text from Durr Mukhtar: 'Yes, what necessitates? Maliki... as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr, and our teacher al-Khas? has organized it.' Over that, Shami first wrote: 'It is critically examined because he is a mujtahid... and all this is a refutation of what is in al-Bazzaziyya. The Allama said: The fatwa in our time is on the saying of Malik, and on what is in Jami' al-Fusulain, that if a qadi judges by qada? its consequences... no attention is paid to what is against one's own madhab, especially for our time's qadis.' Then after a few lines he said: 'I say: But this is when it is possible for a Maliki judge to judge by it or to refer to his arbitration; but in lands where there is no Maliki to judge by it, the necessity is realized. And this is the way of the order from al-Bazzaziyya and Jami' al-Fusulain. And his statement in al-Nahr that there is no need for fatwa is rejected as error... And because of this, al-Zahidi said: Some of our companions used to give fatwa by Malik's saying in this issue due to necessity.' And then: 'And what is mention? about hila, the commentator Miskin mentioned from al-Sayyid al-Hamwi...'
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage addresses a hila (legal stratagem) for a Hanafi qadi or mufti to give a ruling according to a non-Hanafi madhab when necessity dictates. The author starts by quoting a general rule: taqlid is permissible for oneself, but a mufti should only give fatwa by the preferred view within his madhab. This suggests that normally a Hanafi mufti cannot give fatwa by another madhab. However, the author then examines objections and counters them by citing differences among usulis regarding taqlid of a mufdol (inferior mujtahid) when a superior is present. He shows that the stronger view (as per Ibn Hajar and Shami) allows it, so the prohibition is not absolute. The passage then gives a concrete hila: a Hanafi qadi facing a case where the correct ruling according to the Hanafi madhab might cause hardship can apply a Maliki ruling if no Maliki judge is available. This is supported by Shami's statement that in the absence of a Maliki judge to implement the Maliki ruling, necessity (darurah) arises, and thus fatwa by a Maliki view is allowed. The text references the Maliki calculation of iddah (post-divorce waiting period) to illustrate a specific application. The hila thus works by temporarily adopting the Maliki ruling as a matter of necessity, not as a change of madhab, but as a practical solution to avoid injustice. The conditions are: (1) genuine necessity (e.g., no Maliki judge available), (2) no harm to the principal madhab, and (3) the case must be one where the other madhab's ruling is more equitable or solves a problem.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Following a mujtahid's ruling without knowing the evidence, in a matter of 'amal (practice).
مفضول (mafdool): A mujtahid of lower rank compared to another (al-afdal) in knowledge or piety.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits applying a dispensation (rukhsah) or switching to another madhab's ruling.
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem that achieves a permissible outcome by applying an alternative ruling, often to avoid hardship or injustice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when may a Hanafi qadi apply a Maliki ruling in a case?
A) Whenever he prefers the Maliki view over the Hanafi view.
B) Only if the case involves divorce (talaq).
C) When no Maliki judge is available to implement the Maliki ruling, causing necessity.
D) He may never apply a non-Hanafi ruling.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may, under genuine necessity, issue a fatwa by another madhab as a temporary hila, but only when the superior (Abu Hanifa) cannot be followed without hardship and no judge of that madhab is available.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
8 min
Fatwa by Another Madhhab in Necessity: Permissibility and Conditions
Defending ifta bil-madhhab al-ghayr against objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may give fatwa according to another madhhab and apply the criterion of darurah to evaluate objections.

Core Idea
Giving fatwa by another madhhab is permissible when necessity (darurah) makes the Hanafi ruling impossible to follow.

This passage from Al-Hilatul Najijah mounts a vigorous defense of the principle known as 'ifta bil-madhhab al-ghayr' – issuing a fatwa according to a school other than one's own (Hanafi) in a particular issue. The author answers two main objections: first, that the practice originated from unreliable mashayikh; second, that it contradicts the general rule of adhering to one's own madhhab. By tracing the origin to Imam Yusuf and citing the consensus of both early and later scholars, he establishes that the key is the presence of genuine necessity (darurah). Understanding this principle is essential for any mufti navigating situations where the Hanafi ruling would cause extreme hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The passage addresses whether a Hanafi mufti can validly give a fatwa based on another madhhab (e.g., Maliki or Shafi'i) when the Hanafi ruling leads to difficulty. The objection is that this has no basis in the school.
The issue arises in cases like the missing husband (mafqud) or water impurity.
2
Examine the proofs for permissibility
The author cites two main proofs: (1) the consensus of reliable mashayikh, including early scholars like Imam Fazli and Faqih Abu al-Layth, and later scholars like the author of Hidayah and Qadi Khan; (2) the precedent of Imam Yusuf, who adopted the Maliki ruling on water impurity in a case of necessity.
These proofs show that permissibility is not based on weak narrations alone.
3
Understand the opposing argument
Ibn Shahnah and others object that Hanafis have no need to resort to another madhhab because their own school provides sufficient rulings. They assume that the Hanafi ruling can always be applied without hardship.
The objection hinges on the absence of necessity (darurah).
4
Analyze the author's response
The author responds that the objection is valid only when necessity is absent. When darurah is verified, the permissibility becomes operative. He also addresses the concern about unreliable narrators by showing that reliable scholars (muhaqqiqeen) accepted and transmitted the principle, making it authoritative.
The response reframes the debate: the ruling is conditional on necessity.
5
Extract the conditions of darurah
From the passage, the conditions for permissibility are: (1) a genuine necessity (darurah) that makes the Hanafi ruling extremely difficult; (2) the possibility of resorting to another madhhab (i.e., its ruling is accessible and valid); (3) the mufti or qadi acts only to the extent of the necessity.
These conditions prevent misuse of the concession.

Source Text

تحقق ضرورت کے وقت مسئلہ بحوث فیہا میں فتوی دے سکتے تھے اور اب ان کی نقل سے تائید ہو گئی۔ خاص کر جب محققین نے ان کی نقل کو قبول کر لیا ۔ غرض زاہدی و قہستانی کاشف اس مسئلہ کی نقل میں مضر نہیں کیونکہ وہ نقل صرف تائید کے واسطے ہے اصل مدار ان پر نہیں بلکہ مشایخ محققین یعنی امام فضلی وغیرہ پر ہے بلکہ مسئلہ افتاء بمذهب الغیر ضرورت کی اصل خود امام یوسف سے بھی منقول ہے چنانچہ شامی نے رسم المفتی میں بحوالہ بزاز یہ نقل کیا ہے انه صلى الجمعة مغتسلا من الحمام فوجد بئر الحمام فيه فأرة ميتة فقال ناخذ بقول اخواننا من اهل المدينة اذا بلغ الماء قلتين لم يحمل جنتا اھ اور اس کے بعد صاحب رسالہ نے ابن شحنہ سے بحوالہ شامی مسلما مفقود میں اخذ بمذهب الغیر یران الفاظ میں اعتراض نقل کیا ہے لکنه اعتراض على الناطق بانه لا حاجة للحنفى الى ذلك لان ذلك علات مذهبنا فحذف اولی چونکه اس اعتراض میں خود یہ لفظ موجود ہے لا حاجة للحنفى الاذالك اس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ ابن شحنہ وغیرہ ضرورت کے تحقیق میں کام کر رہے ہیں ۔ کہ تحقیق ضرورت کے جو فتوئی اور قضاء بمذہب الغیر کے جوار میں اس کے بعد اسی امر دوم کے قسم کے قریب رسالہ کے مت پر جو لکھا ہے کہ لوگ بہت تعجب کریں گے کہ جب حضرت علامہ ابن عابدین شامی مذہب کے خلاف فتوی دینا منع کرتے ہیں اور علامہ زاہدی اور علامہ قہستانی کو غیر معتبر بھی کہتے ہیں پھر بعض مسائل جیسے مفقود اور ممتدة والنظر وغیرہ کے بارے میں حرج اور ضرورت کے وقت حضرت امام مالک کے قول پر عمل کرنا کیوں جائز لکھتے ہیں جس کا جواب یہ ہے
In this, Allamah Shami himself clarified that the ruling of 'la yasihh' regarding qada by the madhhab of another is specific to when there is no need. And from the statement of Sahib al-Nahr, 'al-idda'i and ma imkan al-tarafu' ilayh', it is also clearly evident that if necessity calls and resort to the Maliki is not possible, then giving fatwa by the madhhab of another is not problematic. And the answer to the fourth expression became known from this, because fatwa and qada have the same ruling in this chapter. In Durr Mukhtar Rasm al-Mufti it is: the summary of what Allamah Qasim mentioned in his correction is that there is no difference between the mufti and the qadi. I said: he followed his referent as Shami stated. Moreover, in the aforementioned expression, permission for both fatwa and qada is explicit. For example, in the expression of Bazzaziyya, fatwa is explicit, and in Jami' al-Fusulain, qada is explicit. As for the research written by Marmad, that the beginning of ifta bil-madhhab al-ghayr was from non-reliable mashayikh, the first answer is that when reliable mashayikh accepted it, it becomes a reliable statement, as is not hidden. The second answer is that from Zahidi and others, the origin of the issue is only that he narrated ifta bil-madhhab al-ghayr in those specific partial cases; otherwise the original issue of ifta bil-madhhab al-ghayr is not dependent on their narration, because the original issue is established from the explicit statements of the early and later scholars. Thus, on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran, among the later scholars, the author of Hidayah, Qadi Khan, and the author of Kanz and others, all the muhaqqiqeen give fatwa, and among the early scholars, Imam Fazli and Faqih Abu al-Layth also gave fatwa, the details of which are in the introduction to the second chapter of Hilah Najizah. From this it is clearly proven that the mashayikh are in agreement on the permissibility of giving fatwa by the madhhab of another in times of necessity. After that, there is no need for a specific fatwa to be transmitted for a particular issue. So if the narration of Zahidi and others did not exist, after the original issue is established, when necessity is realized, one could give fatwa in the issues under discussion. And now their narration has become a support. Especially when the muhaqqiqeen have accepted their narration. In short, Zahidi and Qahistani's disclosure is not harmful in the narration of this issue, because that narration is only for support; the original basis is not on them, but rather on the muhaqqiqeen mashayikh, i.e., Imam Fazli and others. Rather, the origin of the issue of ifta bimadhhab al-ghayr due to necessity is itself narrated from Imam Yusuf. As Shami narrated in Rasm al-Mufti with reference to Bazzaz that he (Imam Yusuf) said: He prayed Jumu'ah after bathing from the bathhouse, and found a dead mouse in the well of the bathhouse. He said: We take the saying of our brothers from the people of Medina: when water reaches two qullahs, it does not become impure. And after that, the author of the treatise narrated from Ibn Shahnah with reference to Shami, concerning the missing person (mufqud), taking by the madhhab of another, he objected with the words: but it is an objection on the speaker because the Hanafi has no need for that, because that is in accordance with our madhhab, so deletion is better. Because in this objection, the words 'la hajata lil hanafi ila dhalik' are present. This proves that Ibn Shahnah and others are working in the verification of necessity. So the verification of necessity for the permissibility of fatwa and qada by the madhhab of another. After that, regarding the second matter, near the end of the treatise, he wrote: People will be very surprised that when Hazrat Allamah Ibn Abidin Shami forbids giving fatwa against the madhhab and also considers Allamah Zahidi and Allamah Qahistani unreliable, then why does he permit acting on the saying of Imam Malik in some issues like mafqud and mumtaddah and nazar etc. due to hardship and necessity? The answer to that is:
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is from Al-Hilatul Najijah, defending the principle of giving fatwa according to another madhhab when necessity requires. The author refutes the objection that this practice originated from unreliable mashayikh. He argues that the ruling is established by the consensus of reliable scholars, both early and later. He cites examples: hiring for Quran teaching was permitted by later authorities like the author of Hidayah and Qadi Khan, and early authorities like Imam Fazli and Faqih Abu al-Layth. Thus, specific transmission from Zahidi is not the basis; it only supports. He also traces the origin to Imam Yusuf, who adopted the Maliki view on water impurity due to necessity. The author then addresses the apparent contradiction in Ibn Abidin's position: he forbids fatwa against the madhhab yet permits it in specific cases like mafqud. The answer is that in those cases, necessity is verified, making it an exception. The passage emphasizes that the core principle is necessity (darurah), and when necessity is established, fatwa by another madhhab is permissible.

Key Terms
افتاء بمذہب الغير (ifta bil-madhhab al-ghayr): Giving a fatwa according to a school other than one's own (Hanafi) in a particular issue.
ضرورت (darurah): A necessity that makes following one's own madhhab extremely difficult or impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the basis for the permissibility of giving fatwa by another madhhab in necessity?
A) Specific narrations from Zahidi and Qahistani
B) The consensus of the mashayikh, both early and later
C) The opinion of Imam Shafi'i
D) The practice of the general public

Key Takeaway
Giving fatwa by another madhhab is an established Hanafi concession valid only when genuine necessity is verified and the alternative school's ruling is accessible.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
advanced
8 min
Critique of Following the Maliki School for Missing Husband Cases
Critique of a hila and clarification of Hanafi tafwid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key objections to following another madhhab for a missing husband case and explain the correct Hanafi position on tafwid.

Core Idea
A Hanafi cannot adopt another madhhab's ruling without a judge; the Hanafi tafwid already gives sufficient flexibility.

In the Hanafi school, the case of a missing husband is addressed through the principle of tafwid (delegation to the judge's ijtihad). Some later scholars suggested that in the absence of a Maliki judge, Hanafis could follow the Maliki ruling. This lesson critically examines that proposal and clarifies why the Hanafi mechanism is both sufficient and obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed hila
What exactly is being proposed? A Hanafi may act on the Maliki school for the missing husband case if no Maliki judge is available.
2
Analyze the objections
The author raises four objections: the permission itself is a fatwa, Maliki school requires a judge, laymen cannot act on weak narrations of their own school let alone another, and the public cannot be taught another school.
Consider each objection in light of usul al-iftaa.
3
Examine the confusion about waiting periods
The author corrects a misinterpretation: the four-year period applies to all wives, not just minors. This shows that confusion about narrations does not justify leaving the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the true meaning of tafwid
Tafwid does not give the judge unlimited discretion; it means the judge decides based on evidence and Hanafi precedent. This already provides ease without resorting to another school.
This is the core Hanafi position.
5
Apply the ruling
Conclude that the relied-upon position is that following another madhhab in this case is impermissible; the judge should apply tafwid within the Hanafi framework.

هل يجوز للإنسان العمل بالضعيف من الرواية في حق نفسه؟ لهم: إذا كان له رأي. أما إذا كان عامياً لا رأي له... لكن مقتضى تقبيل هذا الرأي أنه لا يجوز من ذلك. قال في خزانة الروايات: العالم الذي يعرف معنى النصوص والأخبار وهو من أهل الدراية يجوز له أن يعمل عليها وإن كان مخالفاً للمذهب - اهـ
پھر مذہب غیر پر عمل کی اجازت کیسے ہو سکتی ہے۔ چوتھے عاملی [؟] کو مذہب غیر معلوم کیسے ہو گا جبکہ اہل علم کو اس رسالہ میں بتانے تک سے بھی منع کیا گیا ہے گو پھر خود بتلا بھی رہے ہیں اور اس پر عمل کی اجازت بھی دے رہے ہیں۔ امر سوم کی تحقیق میں روایات مختلفہ نقل کر کے جو اضطراب ظاہر کیا گیا ہے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک روایت [؟] \"کمک کند و افقی را به طلاق زن\" [؟] بائیں رفتہ مالک مکتب مالکیہ بلکہ خود مدون امام مالک کی تقریبات [؟] کے خلاف ہونے کے سبب قابل اعتماد نہیں اور رسک الختام [؟] کی عبارت [؟]۔
او صغیرہ ہے اور چار سال کا یہ حکم نہیں [؟] کامل غلط ہے کہ بہ ترجمہ کیا گیا ہے کہ چار سال کی مدت صرف صغیرہ اور آئسہ یعنی زوجتہ الصغیر کے لیے ہے اس لیے شبہ میں پڑ گئے ورنہ اس کا تو صاف اور سیدھا مطلب تو یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ اور آئسہ کے لیے بھی وہی چار سال کی مدت ہے جو کبیرہ حائضہ کے لیے اس سے پیشتر بیان ہوئی نہ معلوم اس کے یہ معنی کسی طرح قرار دے لیے کہ صغیرہ کا اور حکم ہے اور کبیرہ کا اور۔ اب رہ گئیں در مختار اور فتح الباری کی روایتیں سو ان میں اجمال اور تفصیل کا فرق ہے اور یہ اضطراب نہیں کہلاتا اور گو فتح الباری سے کسی قدر تفصیل معلوم ہوگئی مگر وہ مسلک فتح الباری کی روایت بھی محمل بلکہ موہم [؟] ہے اگر پوری تحقیق اور صحیح تفصیل مطلوب ہو تو حیلہ ناجزہ ملاحظہ فرمایا جائے اس میں مدینہ منورہ کے علمائے مالکیہ کے وسوط [؟] اور مدلل قنادی [؟] حاصل کر کے شائع کئے گئے ہیں۔ فقط واللہ اعلم آٹھویں جزء میں خدشہ تو کئی مقدمات پر ہے مگر ہم بغرض اختصار صرف اصل مقصد پر کلام کرتے ہیں جیسا کہ دوسرے اجزاء میں بھی ضروری امور پر کام کیا گیا ہے۔ اس جزو کا اصل مقصد یہ ہے کہ حاکم کی رائے کے تفویض کرنے کا قول جو کہ فقہ حنفی میں موجود ہے اس میں زوجہ مفقود کے لیے کافی رعایت موجود ہے اس سے دوسرے امام کا مسلک اختیار کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہتی غالبا مصنف نے تفویض کا یہ مطلب قرار دیا ہے کہ حاکم کو پورا پورا اختیار دیا ہے کہ جب چاہے مفقود پر موت کا حکم لگائے اسی وجہ سے مصنف نے \"احسن المقال\" کے عنوان \"تفویض الی رائے الامام\" کا ترجمہ یہ کیا ہے کہ \"مفقود کا معاملہ قاضی اسلام کے حوالہ کر دیا جائے\" لیکن دراصل اس قول کا یہ مطلب نہیں اس وجہ سے اس قول سے کوئی سہولت اور رعایت نہیں نکل سکتی۔
If there is no Maliki judge or mufti, then out of necessity you can act yourself while adhering to all the rulings of the Maliki school. First, there is a severe objection: this permission itself is a fatwa, while the author of the treatise forbids others from giving fatwas. Is the specific word 'fatwa' a condition for a fatwa? Second, how is it possible to act oneself when in the Maliki school the judge's ruling is a condition, and the author forbids the judge from judging by another school? Third, a layman is not even allowed to act on a weak narration of his own school, which is lighter than acting on another school. Thus, al-Shami narrated from Allamah Biri: 'Is it permissible for a person to act on a weak narration concerning himself? For them: if he has an opinion. But if he is a layman with no opinion... but the implication of accepting this opinion is that it is not permissible. He said in Khizanat al-Riwayat: The scholar who understands the meaning of texts and reports and is among the people of deduction may act upon them even if they contradict his school.' Then how can acting on another school be allowed? Fourth, how will the general public know another school when the people of knowledge have been forbidden from even informing in this treatise, even though they themselves are informing and allowing action upon it. As for the third matter, the confusion shown by transmitting various narrations in research means that one narration... left the Maliki school, rather it contradicts the statements of Imam Malik himself, thus unreliable. And the text of Risalah al-Khatam... She is a minor, and this ruling is not for four years? It is completely wrong that it was translated that the period of four years is only for the minor and the ayyisah, i.e., the young wife, so they fell into doubt. The straightforward meaning is that the same period of four years applies to the minor and the ayyisah as was previously mentioned for the menstruating adult woman. How they derived that the minor has a different ruling and the adult another. Now remain the narrations from Durr Mukhtar and Fath al-Bari, in which there is a difference of generality and detail, which is not called confusion. And although some detail is known from Fath al-Bari, that narration from the school of Fath al-Bari is also suggestive rather than precise. If full research and correct detail is desired, look at Hilah Najizah; in it, the Maliki scholars of Madinah al-Munawwarah have published their clearly argued proofs. Only Allah knows best. In the eighth part, there are several issues, but we, for the sake of brevity, speak only on the main purpose. The main purpose of this part is that the statement of delegating to the judge's opinion, which exists in Hanafi fiqh, provides sufficient consideration for the wife of a missing person. There is no need to adopt the school of another imam in this matter. Apparently, the author has taken this meaning of tafwid: that the judge has full authority to declare the missing person dead whenever he wishes. That is why the author translated the title 'Tafwid ila Ra'yi al-Imam' as 'The case of the missing person should be referred to the Islamic judge.' But in reality, this is not the meaning of that statement; therefore, no ease or consideration can be derived from it.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of the claim that a Hanafi can follow the Maliki school in the case of a missing husband. The author presents four objections: (1) The author who permits this is himself forbidding others from giving fatwas, yet he is giving a fatwa. (2) Acting on the Maliki school requires a Maliki judge's ruling, but Maliki judges are not available, and the author forbids non-Maliki judges from judging by the Maliki school. (3) A layman cannot even act on weak narrations of his own school, let alone another school. A quote from Khizanat al-Riwayat clarifies that only a scholar capable of ijtihad may act on weak narrations, not a layman. (4) The general public cannot know the details of another school, especially when scholars are forbidden from teaching them. The author then addresses a confusion about the waiting period for minor and ayyisah wives, asserting that the four-year period is the same for all, as per Hanafi rulings. Finally, the author clarifies the true meaning of 'tafwid ila ra'yi al-imam': it does not give the judge unlimited discretion; rather, it means the judge should decide based on evidence and precedent. Thus, the Hanafi position already provides sufficient ease without resorting to another school. The lesson is a critical refinement of a proposed hila (following another madhhab) and a clarification of the correct Hanafi mechanism.

Key Terms
ضعيف الرواية (da'if al-riwayah): A narration from the founding imams that is weak in transmission or contradicts stronger authorities within the madhhab.
تفويض إلى رأي الإمام (tafwid ila ra'yi al-imam): Delegation of the decision regarding the death of a missing person to the judge's ijtihad, based on evidence and precedent within the Hanafi school.
عامي (ammi): A layperson who does not have the ability to derive rulings from evidence or to perform ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Maliki school's requirement for a judge a key objection to a Hanafi following that school?
A) Because the Hanafi school does not allow judges.
B) Because the Maliki school's rulings on missing persons are invalid without a judge, and no Maliki judge is available.
C) Because the author forbids any judge from judging by another school.
D) Because the Hanafi school requires a judge even within its own framework.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of tafwid already provides sufficient ease for missing husband cases, making it unnecessary and impermissible to adopt the Maliki school.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
intermediate
7 min
Correspondence on Tafwid, Qadhi, and Tahkim
Letter seeking fatwa on legal stratagems for missing person case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principles of tafwid and tahkim to construct a legal stratagem for a missing person case, and evaluate the necessity of sticking to the Hanafi madhhab when a hila exists.

Core Idea
When a Hanafi hila exists, acting on another madhhab is unnecessary.

This lesson presents a scholarly correspondence between Mawlana Abdul Karim Gothalvi and Hakim al-Ummat Ashraf Ali Thanwi. The letter raises three critical questions about the missing person (mafqud al-khabar): the correct meaning of tafwid (delegation to the judge's opinion), the validity of appointing a qadhi with delay, and the use of arbitration (tahkim) as an alternative. The response clarifies these points and emphasizes a core principle of Hanafi iftaa: the mufti must exhaust all legal stratagems within his school before considering other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti's method
Observe how the questioner presents three distinct issues (tafwid, qadhi appointment, tahkim) and how the respondent addresses each with reference to Hanafi sources (Fath, Durr al-Mukhtar). This models proper fatwa correspondence.
Notice the respectful tone and systematic approach.
2
Define tafwid ila ra'y al-imam
From the response, extract the precise definition: the judge may rule on death based on predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) from circumstantial indications, even without death of peers.
Contrast with the misconception that peers' death is required.
3
Analyze the role of tahkim
Tahkim (arbitration) is equated to qada; the arbitrator's decision is binding. This provides an alternative to formal qadhi appointment, especially when quick resolution is needed.
The passage cites Durr al-Mukhtar's discussion on tahkim.
4
Apply the principle of preferring Hanafi hila
The respondent argues that if a valid Hanafi stratagem exists, acting on another madhhab is unnecessary. This is a key rule in mufti adab: exhaust your school first.
The basis is absence of darurah (necessity).
5
Synthesize the fatwa
The mufti provides a ruling that the missing person can be declared dead via tafwid, using tahkim if needed, and there is no need to leave the Hanafi school.
This is the mufta bihi position.

(1) عریضیہ سابقہ سے واضح ہو چکا ہے کہ تفویض الی رای الامام کا مطلب ہے کہ حاکم کو جب قرائن ظاہرہ والہ سے موت مفقود کا غلبہ ظن ہو جائے ۔ تو وہ بدون موت اقران بھی حکم بالمورت کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ موت اقران
In the letter, I have repeatedly mentioned the reference to Hilah Najizah. If possible, please send me a copy so that I can benefit. For now, please satisfy me with answers to the following matters; it is hoped that disagreements will be resolved. Regarding the meaning of tafwid (delegation), the meaning I have written is also cited by Allamah Shami under Durr al-Mukhtar quoting Fath, as he said: 'He said in Fath: ...' But it is necessary that this narration not be trivial, but only after ijtihad and predominant conjecture. But does this prove discretion or not? Please reflect further. Once this is settled, all will be settled. (2) The appointment of a qadhi with delay (bi al-tarakhi) - is appointment with consent correct? (3) If this is not the case, and for temporary proceedings a hakam (arbitrator) is appointed, will the restriction remain? Because tahkim (arbitration) is like qada and the arbitrator is like a judge, especially what the author of Durr al-Mukhtar wrote; please reflect well. (1) From the previous letter, it is clear that tafwid ila ra'y al-imam means that when the ruler, through apparent circumstances and indications, has predominant conjecture of the death of the missing person, then he can rule on death even without death of peers, because death of peers...
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents a scholarly correspondence typical of the Hanafi tradition, where a student or colleague (Mawlana Abdul Karim Gothalvi) seeks clarification on several points from the master (Hakim al-Ummat Thanwi). The letter references key Hanafi sources: Fath al-Qadir, Durr al-Mukhtar, and the commentary of Allamah Shami. The core issue is the legal stratagem (hila) for the missing person (mafqud al-khabar) who has been absent for a long time with no news. The letter raises three points: (1) the correct meaning of tafwid (delegation to the judge's opinion), (2) the permissibility of appointing a qadhi with delay (bi al-tarakhi), and (3) whether arbitration (tahkim) can substitute for a proper qadhi appointment. The response clarifies that tafwid means the judge can declare death based on predominant conjecture from circumstantial evidence, without requiring the death of peers. The letter also questions the need to act on another madhhab if a valid Hanafi hila exists, emphasizing that Hanafi law provides sufficient mechanisms. This reflects the principle that within Hanafi fiqh, there is often a hila that avoids the need to resort to other schools. The response is a model of proper fatwa: direct, source-based, and respectful.

Key Terms
تفویض (tafwid): Delegation of authority to the imam's opinion; specifically, the judge's authority to rule on death based on predominant conjecture from indications, without requiring death of peers.
تحکیم (tahkim): Arbitration; appointing a hakam (arbitrator) who functions like a qadhi in resolving disputes.
نصب القاضی بالتراخی (nasb al-qadhi bi al-tarakhi): Appointment of a judge with delay; whether a judge appointed with the consent of the parties but with some delay is valid.

A) The missing person must have reached the age of death of his peers.
B) The judge must have predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann) based on apparent indications.
C) The family must submit a written request.
D) The judge must consult with the community elders.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi iftaa, the mufti must exhaust all legal stratagems within his school before considering other madhhabs.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems

Appointment of Qadi by Mutual Consent and the Missing Person's Arbitration: A Hanafi Critique
Critique of appointing a qadi without proper authority and rejection of hakam for missing persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for valid qadi appointment and arbitration, and evaluate why the hila of appointing a hakam for a missing person is invalid.

Core Idea
A qadi must be appointed by legitimate authority; mutual consent alone is insufficient. Arbitration requires consent from both parties.

This lesson presents a critical refinement of a proposed hila regarding the appointment of a qadi by community consensus and the use of a religious arbitrator for a missing person. The author, drawing on Hanafi authorities like Shami and Bazzaziyya, argues that these solutions lack textual and rational support, are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah, and lead to practical difficulties. Understanding the conditions for valid appointment and arbitration is essential for issuing sound fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two hila under critique
The passage examines two proposed solutions: (1) appointing a qadi by mutual consent of Muslims in the absence of a ruler, and (2) appointing a religious arbitrator (hakam) for a missing person. Recognize both as attempts to resolve practical problems but deemed invalid by the author.
2
Extract the Hanafi conditions for valid qadi appointment
From the text, note that a qadi must be formally appointed by the ruling authority or a valid delegation. Mutual consent alone is not sufficient. Cite Shami's quotation from Bazzaziyya as evidence.
3
Analyze the missing person case (mafqud)
Understand that arbitration requires explicit consent from both disputants. For a missing person, obtaining such consent is impossible, making the hila of appointing a hakam invalid. The author stresses this as a fundamental condition.
4
Examine the author's critique of the opposing view
The author argues that the proposed solutions are not supported by reliable narration (riwayah) or rational reasoning (dirayah). They are new opinions that do not belong to Zahir al-Riwayah and would open doors to disagreement.
5
Evaluate the alternative Maliki position
The text mentions that adopting the Maliki view might be necessary in some contexts, but the author considers this difficult because it involves opposing major Hanafi scholars like the author of Hidayah.
