Because at this time, this saying cannot be included in the Zahir al-Riwayah, due to which Shami etc. have supported it. Rather, it will be a new saying that can be supported neither by narration (riwayah) nor by rational reasoning (dirayah). It is obvious that such a saying cannot be acceptable in any way. Therefore, prescribing absolute discretion for the judge in this chapter is completely baseless. [Unclear] from the people of knowledge. And Allah knows best what is correct, and to Him is the return and the refuge. (2) Appointment of a judge by mutual consent of Muslims is not valid. As Shami has quoted from Bazzaziyya. 'And the consensus of the people of affliction...' The juristic expression related to the selection of a judge [unclear]. Allama Shami said after it: 'But this is where there is no necessity, and [unclear] the appointment of a judge.' Firstly, there is a serious objection: this statement, which is referred to later, says 'they make him a governor, so he becomes a judge' literally, and directly from Allama's side there is no mention of appointing a judge in it, therefore the claim is not proven. Regarding the objection related to the case of the missing person, the second submission is that in a country where the judge gains power and authority by the consent of Muslims, there might be some leeway, but in this country, the general appointment does not work; rather, a wide door of new disagreement will open. Therefore, considering it correct is in no way analogous. Out of three types, the first type, i.e., 'they make him a governor and he becomes a judge' occurring in our region is very distant, and the insufficiency of the second type was mentioned, and the constructive type, i.e., 'a non-Muslim ruler and consent of Muslims' is possible, but for many years efforts have been ongoing but still at the beginning. And if the Holy Lord grants success, then even then there is no alternative without adopting the saying of the Maliki scholars, because handing over to the judge does not solve the problem, as was submitted in the previous letter. Firstly, it is difficult to oppose the author of Hidayah and other great scholars, especially when the cause ('illah) of their saying, i.e., the fear of the common people falling into difficulty, is increasing nowadays, which is observed. Secondly, that in the case of a missing person, it is not possible to appoint a religious third arbitrator because for that the consent of both parties is a condition, and there is no way to obtain the consent of the missing person. Therefore, a fatwa cannot be given to make him a hakam, i.e., a third arbitrator. Only Allah knows best, and His knowledge is most complete and most wise. Written by the humble Abdul Karim, may he be forgiven. Khanqah Imdadia Thana Bhawan, 1st Muharram al-Haram. Your letter was also passed through the review of Maulana [may his blessings endure], and he approved the annotation, and instructed that Moulvi Sahib be sent my greetings and also write that your efforts have pleased my heart, I pray for blessings, may Allah Almighty grant more success. Note: Al-Hilatun Najijah has been completed, praise be to God. In the following pages, endorsements from senior scholars are presented. Khurshid Hasan Qasimi.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement regarding the appointment of a qadi (judge) and the use of a hila (legal stratagem) in the case of a missing person (mafqud). The author begins by arguing that a proposed view does not qualify as part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is unsupported by both transmitted and rational proofs. Therefore, granting a judge absolute discretion in this matter is baseless. He then states a clear ruling: appointment of a judge by mutual consent of Muslims is not valid, citing Shami's quotation from Bazzaziyya. The author critiques Shami's subsequent remark, pointing out that the quoted text does not explicitly mention appointment of a judge, thus the claim remains unproven. Regarding the missing person case, the author explains that even if in some countries mutual consent gives the judge power, in their context it leads to further disagreement. He describes three types of judge appointment: (1) making someone a governor who becomes a judge (unlikely in their region), (2) insufficient type, and (3) a non-Muslim ruler with Muslim consent (possible but efforts have not succeeded). The author suggests that without adopting the Maliki position, the problem remains unsolved. He then reaffirms the difficulty of opposing great Hanafi scholars like the author of Hidayah, especially since their concern for common people's hardship is still valid. Finally, he concludes that for a missing person, appointing a religious arbitrator (hakam) is impossible because both parties' consent is required, and the missing person's consent cannot be obtained. Hence, no fatwa can be given for such a hila.

Key Terms
قاضی (qadi): A judge appointed to adjudicate disputes according to Islamic law; must be properly appointed by the ruler or his deputy.
مفقود (mafqud): A person who is missing and whose whereabouts or status (alive/dead) is unknown.
حکیم دینی (hakim dini): A religious arbitrator or third party appointed to resolve a dispute.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani forming the authoritative transmitted corpus of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it not permissible to appoint a religious arbitrator (hakim dini) in the case of a missing person (mafqud)?
A) Because the missing person is not present to defend themselves
B) Because the consent of both parties is required, and the missing person's consent cannot be obtained
C) Because only a properly appointed qadi can handle such cases
D) Because the Maliki school forbids it

Key Takeaway
A hila is invalid if it violates a fundamental condition of the school, such as the requirement of consent for arbitration or formal appointment for a qadi.

Hila Shariyyah — Legal Stratagems
advanced

Fatwa with Other Madhhabs in Necessity
Endorsement of a risala allowing marriage annulment based on Maliki madhhab under necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may give a fatwa based on a non-Hanafi madhhab and apply the principle of darura to such cases.

Core Idea
Necessity permits a Hanafi mufti to adopt another madhhab's ruling, but only strictly within that necessity.

This passage is an endorsement (taqriz) of a risala that permits annulment of marriage for defects like impotence by adopting the Maliki ruling on annulment. It affirms that giving fatwa with other madhhabs in cases of dire necessity is accepted among the mashayikh, but warns the mufti against making it a habit. The passage also notes that for insanity, a basis exists within the Hanafi school itself, and that rulings by Abu Yusuf or Muhammad are not contrary to the Imam. Let us examine the conditions and the underlying principle of darura.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The risala deals with the annulment of marriage due to defects like impotence (al-'anin) and insanity (al-majnoon). The Hanafi default ruling: a woman married to an impotent man may seek annulment after a one-year waiting period; for insanity, the option is more limited. Identify the Hanafi position and why the risala turns to the Maliki madhhab.
2
Recognize the necessity (darura)
The passage uses terms like 'inda al-hajah wa al-darurah al-mulihhah (when there is dire necessity and pressing need). Consider what kind of situation would make the Hanafi ruling insufficient—e.g., prolonged hardship, lack of alternative recourse.
3
Understand the principle of following other madhhabs
The passage states that giving fatwa with other madhhabs in necessity is accepted, citing al-Qahistani (on the missing husband) and al-Ramli (on the obstinate). The mufti may adopt the Maliki ruling on annulment, but only due to necessity.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi basis
For the insane husband, the passage notes that a basis exists even in Muhammad's opinion, and that ruling by Abu Yusuf or Muhammad is not contrary to the Imam's madhhab. This provides an alternative within the school before going outside.
5
Apply the mufti's adab
The passage concludes with a warning: the mufti must not make such fatwas a habit (la yaj'ala hadhihi al-fatawa 'u'datan), must not exceed the specific necessity, and must be cautious because the matter is of great danger. This is the operative condition for the ruling.

Source Text

و بعد فقد نظرنا معشر خدام الملة الاسلاميه بالمدرسة العالية الأمداديه في الرسالة التي صدرت في هذا العصر من صدر من موصدر هذا الدهر - وجهبذ اهل التحقيق بالتحقيق شيخ الشريعة والطريقة - عارف المذهب والحقيقة اشرف الانام باهر بالشرف الجلى مولينا اشرف على اكرمه الله الولى - وموضوع الرسالة انما هو القول يفسخ نكاح زوجة العنين والمجنون والمقصور والمتنت عند مس العاجة والضرورة الملحة - اخذا في جل هذا الباب بمذهب سیدنا مالك رحمة الله عليه وعلى صيع المجتهدين. ولا يخفى ان الفتوى بمذاهب الة المدى لدى الضرورات مستوع عند المشائخ واهل الديانات كما ذكر القهستاني في حق المفقود والرملي في المتعنت واما العنين فالتاجيل شقر التفريق فى حقاب مشهود عند الفضية ثم لا يخفى على اهل الاشتغال بالفته واما المجنون فاصل حكو ايضا مما يوجد له اصل عند الأحناف ولو على مذهب محمد رحمه الله تعالی لان الحكم بما هو مذهب اصحاب الاسامحكم بمذهبه اذا كان برعاية الاصول المقررة ففي الشامي نقلاً عن الدور من كتاب الدعوى واما اذا حكم الحنفى بذهب الى يوسف او محمد أو نحوهما من اصحاب الامام فليس حكماً بخلاف رأيه هذ اول و تراجع في اقوال المالية وغيرها الى كتبه و عنه المطالعة بن اعتمدنا على المنقول في الرسالة عند الطالبة فانه نقل ثقة عمن هو عادت بالمنقول عنه وغير ناقل الاعن المقبول عليه - واما الدنابات للرساله فمعلومات الضرورة ليست فيها بشديدة مثل هذه الحوادث ولا سيما الفتود ونحوه - ومتم ذلك لو تحققت في حادثة فلا باس بالفتوى بغير مذهب الإمام اذا الضرورات نسوع مثل هذ ا و لكن يجب على المفتى ان لا يجعل هذه الفتاوى عرضة له وعليه ان لا يتجاوز موضع الضرورة فان المقام مقام خطر عظيم والله الموفق و المعين . والحمد لله رب العلمين والصلوة على رسوله والله وصحبه أجمعين العبدا المفتقر الى رحمہ ذی المان محم مر تضی حسن عفی عنہ صدر المدرسين بالمدرسة العالية العربية الاعدادية الواقع بلدة مراد آباد الملتجی الی اللہ مختار الله (المدعو ) میر کے شاہ عفا اللہ عنہ دعانا صدر الاخبار عبده المفق إلى الله الحمد بالمدرسته العالية الاعدادية احمر الزمن خلیل احمد کان اللہ لہ مفتی المدرسة الحالية ... محمد سید حسن عفا اللہ عنہ
And after, we, the servants of the Islamic nation, at the high preparatory school, looked at the treatise that was issued in this era from a leading figure of this time—a genius of verification, the Shaykh of Sharia and Tariqa, knower of the madhhab and reality, the most eminent of people, brilliant in manifest honor, our master Ashraf Ali, whom Allah honored. The subject of the treatise is the ruling that the marriage of the wife of an impotent, insane, imprisoned, or obstinate [husband] is annulled when there is dire necessity and pressing need—taking in most of this chapter the madhhab of our master Malik, may Allah have mercy on him and on all mujtahids. It is not hidden that giving fatwa with the madhhabs of the imams in cases of necessity is accepted among the mashayikh and religious people, as al-Qahistani mentioned regarding the missing [husband] and al-Ramli regarding the obstinate. As for the impotent, the postponement and separation is witnessed in the court. Then it is not hidden from those engaged in fatwa. And as for the insane, there is a basis in the Hanafi madhhab as well, even according to the madhhab of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, because a ruling that is the madhhab of the companions of the Imam is a ruling with his madhhab if it observes established principles. In al-Shami quoting from al-Durr from the book of claims: 'When a Hanafi judges according to the madhhab of Abu Yusuf or Muhammad or others of the Imam's companions, it is not a ruling contrary to his opinion.' This is the first [point]. And we refer in the statements of the Maliki and others to their books and require review. We relied on what is transmitted in the treatise for the seeker, for it is a reliable transmission from one who is trusted in what is transmitted from him, and he does not transmit except what is accepted. As for the endorsements of the treatise, the necessities are not as severe as these incidents, especially al-fatwad and the like. The gist is that if such is verified in an incident, there is no harm in giving fatwa with other than the Imam's madhhab when necessities permit like this. But it is incumbent on the mufti not to make these fatwas a habit, and he must not exceed the place of necessity, for the situation is one of great danger. Allah is the Granter of success and Helper. All praise is due to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and blessings upon His Messenger and his family and companions. The servant in need of the mercy of the Possessor of Bounty, Muhammad Murtada Hasan, may he be pardoned, head teacher at the high Arabic preparatory school located in the town of Muradabad, seeking refuge in Allah, Mukhtar Allah (known as Mir Kay Shah), may Allah pardon him, invited us [as] the chief of reports. His servant in need of Allah's praise at the high preparatory school, the scholar of the time, Khalil Ahmad, may Allah be with him, mufti of the current school... Muhammad Sayyid Hasan, may Allah pardon him.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a taqriz (endorsement) of the risala Al-Hilatul Najijah, written by a group of scholars addressing the issue of annulling a marriage due to defects like impotence, insanity, etc. The core legal discussion is the permissibility of a Hanafi mufti giving a fatwa according to another madhhab (here, Maliki) in cases of dire necessity. The scholars affirm that this is acceptable based on the principle that necessity permits such recourse, citing earlier authorities like al-Qahistani and al-Ramli. They note that for the insane, a Hanafi basis exists even in Muhammad's opinion. They emphasize that the mufti must not make a habit of this and must strictly limit himself to the specific need, as the matter is grave. The passage thus provides a clear ruling on when a mufti may step outside his own madhhab, with conditions and warnings.

Key Terms
العنين (al-'anin): A husband who is impotent and unable to consummate the marriage.
المجنون (al-majnoon): A husband who is insane, affecting the validity of the marriage.
الضرورة (al-darura): Dire necessity that permits a ruling outside the dominant madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required of a Hanafi mufti when giving a fatwa with a non-Hanafi madhhab in cases of necessity?
A) He may do so freely for any case.
B) He must not exceed the specific necessity and must not make it a habit.
C) He must follow the Hanafi madhhab exclusively.
D) He must obtain permission from the ruler.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may adopt a non-Hanafi ruling only under verified darura, with strict limits and no habitual use.
